**The letter regarding the Tehillim societies:** Igros Kodesh of the Rebbe Rayatz, Vol. 6, letters 1785–6. There, one can also find the "Machne Israel" letter on this topic and the society's regulations.

**Chairman of the Executive Committee:** Machne Israel.

## 23

*[Late 5702]*

B"H

Immediately upon his arrival in America two and a half years ago, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita, began tireless work to awaken American Jews to teshuvah, Torah, and maasim tovim. He made it clear that the harsh decrees against Jews are the *chevlei Mashiach*, and that there is only one salvation:

"L'alter l'teshuvah" (Immediate teshuvah), through which there will be "L'alter l'geulah shleimah" (Immediate complete redemption) through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, with kindness and mercy.

The words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita, have had their effect. In broad circles of the Jewish population, a teshuvah movement has begun, and various Jewish organizations have placed teshuvah advocacy on their agendas.

In order to give everyone the opportunity to familiarize themselves with the words and letters of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita, regarding "L'alter l'teshuvah" and "L'alter l'geulah," we are printing herewith a collection of some of his words and letters from the recent period.

We urge and hope that the Rabbis, the bnei Torah shlita, and in general, anyone who is a person of influence, will—in accordance with the call of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita—utilize the Yimei HaSelichos and Aseres Yemei Teshuvah to:

a) Clarify that the current harsh decrees against Jews are the *chevlei Mashiach*;

b) Awaken everyone to *teshuvah amitis* (true repentance) and to strengthen the observance of Torah and mitzvos;

c) Explain the concept of purifying the atmosphere through the recitation of the letters of the Torah, and specifically Mishnayos, wherever permitted by halacha;

d) Ensure that everyone enrolls in the *Chevras Tehillim*, which, by joining the global *Chevras Tehillim* in Yerushalayim (may it be rebuilt and established speedily in our days), will thus participate in its prayer on behalf of Klal Yisrael.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V'Chasimah Tovah*, for immediate teshuvah—for immediate redemption.

**Menachem Schneerson,**

**Chairman of the Vaad HaPoel**

## 25

25

B"H, 8th of Tishrei, 5703

To the esteemed *avreichim* of the *Temimim*, G-d-fearing men, men of action, students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, may Hashem grant them life, Montreal.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your *Leshana Tova* letter: May the one who blesses be blessed with abundant blessings from above, in both soul and body, with much goodness in the most essential matters.

The name "Tamim" signifies that one is whole (*shalem*) in the fulfillment of the *mitzvos*. According to our Sages, the 248 positive *mitzvos* correspond to the 248 limbs, and the 365 negative *mitzvos* correspond to the 365 sinews.

Chassidus, which reveals the *pnimiyus* (inner dimension) within everything, has explained (Likutei Torah, *d'h Ki HaMitzvah*, 282, and elsewhere) that becoming a *tamim* through the fulfillment of *mitzvos* occurs when the fulfillment of the *mitzvah* is done in such a way that *Havayah*—for all *mitzvos* are dependent upon one of the letters of the Name *Havayah*—becomes *Elokecha* (your G-d), your strength and your vitality. This means that the one who learns becomes one with the Torah, *v'talmudo b'yado* (his learning is within his grasp). This is achieved through the prerequisite of the *avodah* of *tefillah* (Torah Ohr, *d'h HaBa'im Yaresh*; Likutei Torah, *Ki Tavo*, etc.).

Now, one who has sinned, caused a blemish, and strayed from the path—becoming, G-d forbid, a *ba'al mum* (one with a blemish) through this—the remedy for this is *teshuvah*, for *teshuvah* brings healing to the world.

However, *refuah* (healing) is only for the future, and "a trace of his name"—of the blemish—remains upon him (Yoma 86a). He is not yet the *tamim* he once was, until he reaches a higher level of *teshuvah me'ahavah rabbah* (teshuvah from great love) from the depths of the heart, where "willful sins are transformed into merits" (Tanya, Chapter 7), which uproots the sin from its very inception.

To help one reach such a *teshuvah*—which must be *b'chol me'odecha* (with all your might) (Likutei Torah, *d'h Velo Avah* and its explanation)—this is done through a Rebbe, for "a wise man uproots it from its source" (Kesuvos 74b), by seeking and finding within the sinner himself the opening for repentance.

— And in *d'varim sheb'pnimiyus* (inner matters), it should be noted that the possibility of an opening for repentance for a sin, and that only a wise man can find it, is derived from the fact that the four things the Holy One regrets are the *yetzer hara* (Sukkah 52b). —

May we all very soon merit the coming of *Moshiach*, who comes to restore the *tzaddikim*—*b'chol nafshecha* (with all your soul)—in *teshuvah*—*b'chol me'odecha* (with all your might).

— And one should note *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 60, and Likutei Torah, *d'h Lehavin Inyan Yom Tov Sheni Shel Galuyos*. —

With blessings for a *Chasimah Tovah* and a *Gemar Chasimah Tovah*, immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to life, immediately to *Geulah*,

**Menachem Schneerson**

Chairman of the Vaad HaPoel

**A further point on the above:**

Regarding a *ben Noach*, only a *mechusar eiver* (one missing a limb) is disqualified. For a *ben Noach* and a *Bnei Yisrael*, the distinction was made through the Giving of the Torah, the purpose of which was to nullify the decree that "the inhabitants of the upper realms shall not descend [to the lower realms], and the inhabitants of the lower realms shall not ascend [to the upper realms]," but rather that the heavens and the earth were unified. **In terms of *dakus* (subtlety)**, this is the innovation of the teachings of Chassidus: *ein od milvado* (there is nothing else besides Him) in truth; Hashem is One, both above and below. This is why for a *ben Noach*, only a *mechusar eiver*—a total lack of the *mitzvah*—disqualifies him, whereas for *Chassidim*, many matters—blemishes—disqualify one from the *hiddur mitzvah* (beautification of the *mitzvah*). And generally, *Elokim* in *gematria* is *HaTeva* (nature), and in *gematria* is *mum* (blemish); and it must be that "He created *Elokim*" [to mean] to heal/perfect nature.

26

26

B.H., 26th of Cheshvan, 5703

To our dear friend, the brilliant Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and wise, etc.,
Moreinu HaRav A.A. shlita,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your blessing for the coming year: whoever blesses others is himself blessed with an abundance that exceeds the primary blessing, both in material and spiritual matters, for yourself and your family shlita.

Indeed, anyone who offers a blessing surely strives to the extent of his ability to ensure that his blessing is fulfilled, and this applies to the blessing for "Meluch" and "Machaneh Yisrael" as well. I am certain that you, too, are doing everything in your power to bring the goals of "Meluch" and "Machaneh Yisrael"—as outlined by the Rebbe shlita—from potential into action, by working in the spirit of their programs.

By way of a clever allusion, one might suggest that the name Avraham Eliyahu is significant, for "a name is a matter of substance," and the Sages are precise regarding names (Yoma 83b), as this name hints at the totality of Seder Hishtalshelus and our avodah.

Seder Hishtalshelus: Avram is Avraham, the intellect that is hidden from all thought, Chochmah Stumah, until there must be the "saying" of "Asher Areka" (that I will show you) (Torah Ohr, Drushei Lech Lecha). And Eliyahu is the "Angel of the Covenant," the Yesod, the conclusion of the body, the messenger sent to the lowest of the low (see Maamar "Ve'atah Yigdal Na," 5668).

The Order of Avodah: Avraham is one of the seven shepherds (Sukkah 52b), the waters descending from above to below. And Eliyahu is one of the eight princes (see Drushei Chanukah), ascending from below to above.

The General Concept of Avodah: After the sin of the Tree of Knowledge, the avodah is to refine the world and illuminate the darkness, after the seven generations had removed the Shechinah from below to above (Bereishis Rabbah, ch. 19). The beginning of bringing the Shechinah down below was through Avraham, who began to illuminate the world; therefore, the mitzvah of milah was given to him, so that through it, the spiritual influences (hemshechos) generated by Torah and mitzvos could be brought down into physicality (see Likkutei Torah, Likkutei Gimmel Parshiyos, Parshas Lech Lecha, s.v. Lehavin, with additional explanation). However, the mitzvah of periah was not given to him (Yevamos 71b), because at the initial stage, there was not yet a place for such an influence, as the thin skin of the periah would have hindered it (see Maamar "LaMenatzeach Al HaSheminis," and briefly in the concept in the end of the Maamar "VeAtem Tihyu," 5660).

But afterwards, the mitzvah of periah was also given, so that there could also be a revelation of a more sublime light through the avodah throughout all the generations, which requires the removal of this thin kelipah as well, and the refinement of physicality. The ultimate refinement of physicality is through Eliyahu HaNavi, whose body ascended in a whirlwind (see the end of the Maamar "Samei'ach Tisamach," which also mentions Chanoch. However, see Torah Ohr, s.v. "Mi Sam Peh," that Chanoch is not as relevant to this world).

Regarding the avodah, the matter of milah and periah represents the revelation of the external and internal aspects of the heart, "U'maltem" and "U'mal Es Ha'Orlah" (Iggeres HaKodesh, ch. 4; Yom Simchas Torah, 5668). Currently, it is only "U'maltem," but "U'mal Es Ha'Orlah" in the world at large will occur in the days of Moshiach (although Avraham—and in a general sense, within a specific spark, it is possible even now—attained this; see Torah Ohr and Likkutei Torah, Likkutei Gimmel Parshiyos, s.v. "BeEtzem HaYom HaZeh," and the explanation there). This is accomplished by Eliyahu, who comes "to prepare the heart" of the Jewish people (the language of the Rambam, end of Hilchos Melachim), as it is written, "And he shall turn the heart of the fathers," etc.

May the Almighty merit us immediately to complete teshuvah, and immediately to the complete Geulah. With blessings for a happy holiday,

**Rabbi Menachem Mendel**
**Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

P.S. Regarding the matter of milah and periah, and the fact that Avraham and the generation of the desert were not commanded regarding periah, there are two opinions (see Likkutei Torah, Likkutei Gimmel Parshiyos, s.v. "BeEtzem HaYom HaZeh," ch. 5, in the gloss and the sources cited there). And based on what is written in Sefer HaMitzvos, end of the Mitzvos of Milah, s.v. "Amar HaKosev," it can be said that from the perspective of Avraham himself, he did not need to remove the skin of the periah—and on the contrary.

However, from the perspective of his avodah and his influence upon the world, the reason is—even according to the second opinion—that there was not yet a revelation of such a high light, as mentioned above in the body of the letter.

## 27

[25 Tishrei, 5705]

In order not to send a letter empty of the words of our Sages, even though it contains a matter of mitzvos, I will write briefly—as verbosity for your honor is superfluous—and in outline form.

The law of *shechitah*: For a *behemah* (domesticated animal), it is mandatory according to all opinions from the Torah. Regarding a *of* (bird), there is a dispute, but the *halachah* is that it requires *shechitah*. Fish do not require *shechitah*; gathering them is sufficient (*Chullin* 27b and there).

The concept is based on what is explained in many places in *Chassidus* and hinted at in the *nigleh*: **The concept of *shechitah***—"And he shall slaughter (*v'shachat*)" means nothing other than "and he shall draw (*v'mashach*)" (*Chullin* 30b)—is that one completely transfers the animal to a different domain. This is done by taking its life (*Shabbos* 75a) and its vitality from the place where it previously existed. Only then can it be transformed into the blood and flesh of a human being and add strength to his *avodah* of Hashem, rather than causing a fall, *chas v'shalom*.

**A *behemah*** is created from the earth and cannot elevate itself from the ground at all, unless someone else lifts it. In terms of *avodah*: This refers to the body and the *nefesh habehamis*, for "a wild ass's colt is man born" (Iyov 11:12) and "the inclination of man's heart is evil from his youth"—from the moment he is shaken and emerges into the world (*Yerushalmi Berachos* 3:5). Therefore, according to all opinions, it requires *shechitah*—the meaning of which is as stated above—for this is the entire purpose of the soul’s descent below: it does not require rectification for its own sake, but rather to rectify the body (*Tanya*, Chapter 37).

**A *of*** is created from the *reka*—water and earth—and flies in the air from time to time, though it must rest on the earth because it becomes weary and tired from its flying (see *Bereishis Rabbah* 39, cited in *Tosafos* to *Shabbos* 49a).

In terms of *avodah*: This is the *nefesh hasichlis*, which is an intermediary between the *nefesh habehamis* and the *nefesh elokis* (see *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Bechukosai*, the second *maamar*, and its explanation at length in the *maamarim* of *Shavuos* 5702). It can grasp matters of *Elokus*, even though its essence is human intellect, because the *nefesh elokis* is enclothed within it. Therefore, there is a dispute as to whether it requires *shechitah*, but the final ruling is that it does.

**Fish** are always found in their place of vitality, and the moment they depart from it, they die (*Berachos* 61b).

In terms of *avodah*: This is the *nefesh elokis*, which even at the time of sin was "in trust with Him, may He be blessed," with the Source of Life, the Life of lives, except that it is like the parable of the King, etc. (*Tanya*, end of Chapter 24). Therefore, *shechitah* is not required, because it is found in its place of vitality. However, it does require "gathering" (*asifah*), because through the enclothement in the body and the *avodah* of *birurim*, the soul and its powers become scattered in the matters of this world, and one must gather and collect them.

—And more subtly, one could say: *Of* corresponds to *nefesh-ruach-neshamah* (the internal levels), while fish correspond to *chayah-yechidah* (the encompassing levels), but this is not the place to elaborate.

**A *chagav* (locust)** does not require *shechitah* (*Rashi, Chullin* 66a; *Tosafos, Chullin* 90b). In *Taamei HaMitzvos*, it is explained that this is because both [the locust and the earth] are from the same element, whereas *behemah* and *chayah* require *shechitah* from *Malchus*. Alternatively, it could be said that they have no blood (*Peirush HaMishnayos, Terumos* 10:9; *Eduyos* 7:4)—no desires at all. They possess *bitul*—"and we were like grasshoppers in our own eyes" (*Bamidbar* 13:33)—and unity—"the locusts have no king, yet they go forth in bands" (*Mishlei* 30:27; they do not separate from one another, *Metzudos David*). Yet, there is also the aspect of being "like a threshold that is trampled," a connection of nerves, etc., which is why there are also impure locusts. But here, where "great is peace," etc., even they, at least, are permitted.

May it be the will of Hashem that through the *shechitah* of the *yetzer* now, according to the words of our Sages (*Sanhedrin* 43b), we will merit speedily the promise for the time to come (*Sukkah* 52a): "The Holy One, blessed be He, will bring the *yetzer hara* and slaughter it."

May He revive us, sustain us, and gather our exiles through *Moshiach Tzidkeinu* very soon.

## 28

28

B"H, 28 Tishrei, 5705.

To my friend, the outstanding avreich, the G-d-fearing, etc., the Rav,
the Temimim,
Moreinu HaRav Moshe Eliyahu, may he live, Gerlitzky,
Montreal, Canada

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your invitation and the invitation of your brother, the talmidei hatemimim, may they live, to come and participate with you in the joy of your wedding:

After expressing my gratitude for the invitation, I must inform you that due to circumstances beyond my control, I am unable to travel from here for a few days. I must content myself with participating in your joy from afar, though I am close in spirit.

I send you my blessing that "He who declares the end from the beginning" —

(One may say: **"Beginning"** — through the avodah now, for the entirety of avodah is from below to above, that "a woman who fears Hashem, she shall be praised" [Mishlei 31:30] — through this, one arrives at the **"End"** — the revelation of the World of Freedom, the Yovel, and even higher, the revelation of the Memalei Kol Almin, which is the revelation of the future to come, "a great shofar shall be sounded" [Yeshayahu 27:13], and with great awe. See Likutei Torah, beginning of the maamar "Lehavin Mah Shene'emar Bahaggadah" and the maamar "Vehayah Bayom Hahu Yitaka" section 6.)

— will say to the one who cleaves, "Good, for 'He who finds a wife finds good'" [Mishlei 18:22] — that through the wife, the blessing is drawn down into physical life and actual material sustenance (see Likutei Torah, end of Parshas Bracha).

One may say that this is the second interpretation of "He who declares the end from the beginning": an outpouring from above to below, which comes about through the avodah from below to above, as mentioned above. "Beginning" refers to Chochma (see the maamar "Vayita Eshel" 5701, which indicates the wondrous nature of the sefirah of Chochma); "End" refers to Malchus, the conclusion and end of all the sefiros and the outpourings.

I will conclude with a precious pearl that I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may he live: on Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Noach 5691, in continuation of a maamar of Chassidus he delivered then — on the parsha of Noach — "A tzoher (light/window) you shall make for the teivah (ark)." He began to say:

"This is how one learns in Gan Eden; this is a pshat from Gan Eden. 'Tzoher (a light) you shall make for the teivah' — 'Zohar (radiance) you shall make for the teivah.' And 'el amah' (to a cubit) — and then it will be **A**leph (Hashem) **M**elech (King) **H**aOlam (of the world). 'Tichleina mil'ma'alah' (they shall be completed from above) — that the vessels, too, will be made from above. And the Rebbe (the Alter Rebbe) gave someone through this actual, physical life." End quote.

I sign with the blessing that you may elicit the will of Hashem, the Good, in a good that is revealed and manifest, and with regards to all the Temimim, may they live, with love,

* * *

P.S. If you have the maamar "Tzoher" from 5691 mentioned above, I am enclosing it herewith, as it contains an explanation of the aforementioned concept of "tzoher" at length. Since I have only this one copy, please be kind enough to return it to me, and thank you in advance.

B"H, 4 Cheshvan, 5703

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letters from the end of the week and from Wednesday of last week, regarding the first point, etc.:

The price for each set—bound—is four local dollars. Per your letter, we are waiting for an opportunity via a traveler. If you prefer them sent by post, please let us know.

6) We are surprised that you are having difficulty sending money here, as according to the law, everyone can send up to 25 shekel from your country. Sending it promptly, especially regarding the *Sefer Torah*, would be greatly appreciated.

He should participate in the expenses of the *Sefer Torah* appropriately, *l’fum gamla shichna* [according to the camel is the load], as the expenses are great. Naturally, one does not speak about this with everyone, *v’dai l’meivin* [a word to the wise is sufficient]. The same applies to efforts with others who are involved in this, such as the Albert brothers, etc.

8) The *sicha* from Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah has not yet been transcribed. Enclosed, **to be returned**, is the *sicha* from Parshas Bereishis, **which is unedited**.

9) ....

10) While R’ Z. Pliskin, may he live, was here, he promised me his participation in all matters of *Melach* [Merkaz L’Inyonei Chinuch] and *Machne Yisroel* in your country, provided that he is told what he needs to do. Surely, he himself and his household will also draw closer to all these matters by engaging in this work.

With the blessing of *L’alter L’teshuvah, L’alter L’Geulah* [Immediate repentance, immediate redemption].

**Menachem Schneerson**

Chairman of the Executive Committee

Please convey my regards to all the *Temimim*, may they live.

B"H, 4 Cheshvan, 5703

Your letter from Chol Hamoed Sukkos, with the enclosed, has arrived. As you requested, it has been delivered to the *Kodesh HaKodashim* [the Rebbe Rayatz] to which it pertains. Also enclosed are two receipts and three letters from the committee for the *Sefer Torah*.

Surely you have already begun, as you promised, to take an interest in establishing "Shabbos Parties," and we await your good news regarding this.

And surely you will endeavor, with the help of Hashem, that "Shabbos Parties" for girls will also be established.

I am your friend who wishes you well, with blessings for *L'Alter L'Teshuvah - L'Alter L'Geulah*.

Chairman of the Executive Committee

Surely there are orphanages in Chicago, and I would appreciate it if you could provide us with details: a) The name and address, b) the number of orphans, c) the names of the directors, d) what kind of spirit prevails there, etc. Thank you in advance.

## 32

21 Cheshvan, 5703

In response to your letter,

1. The reason we remind the members of "Machane Yisrael" every month regarding their commitment to perform four activities is because the concept of *zerizus* (promptness/diligence) is of great importance. See *Sifrei, Naso*, and *Midrash Rabbah, Parshas Bamidbar*, Chapter 4: "One only encourages those who are already diligent." In *Toras Kohanim*, beginning of *Parshas Tzav*—cited in Rashi on the verse "Command Aharon"—it states that "command" (*tzav*) implies nothing other than *zerizus*, and the Kohanim were diligent (*Shabbos* 20a).

2. Regarding your comment about the matter of *hatznei leches* (walking humbly/discreetly): It is obvious that there is no need to publicize every single activity; four activities are sufficient. Furthermore, this is known only to the administration of "Machane Yisrael." Surely, what remains hidden is far greater than what is revealed, for four activities over the course of a full month is a very minimal amount. The only reason they settled on four activities was to establish a membership contribution that is equal for everyone.

It is highly probable that for those who perform only four activities over the course of a **full month**, had it not been for the reminder and the reporting to the administration, they would not have done even that. They are included in the category of "a person should always engage in Torah and mitzvos, even if not for their own sake, for from [doing them] not for their own sake, one comes to [do them] for their own sake" (*Pesachim* 50b). In *Tosafos, s.v. Ha'oseh* (*Berachos* 17a), it explains that this refers to doing so in order to be honored. In the *Hilchos Talmud Torah* of the Alter Rebbe (Chapter 3, Paragraph 4), he explains this regarding lower levels. See also *Sefer Shel Beinonim*, Chapter 27.

3. Regarding your comment that this diminishes the aspect of *lishmah* (doing it for its own sake): There is nothing to boast about in four activities over the course of a month, when one takes into account what is explained in *Chassidus*—that "days are fashioned, and not one of them [is missing]"—meaning that there are many days, and time is an "irrecoverable loss," in which one did not draw down a single *bichinah* (aspect) of holiness (see *Likutei Torah*, end of *Parshas Shelach*). This is at a time when the days were fashioned and given to man so that each day he would fulfill his mission below, so that there would be "for him" (*lo*—spelled with a *vav*) "one" (*echad*) among them, as is discussed in many places, including the *maamar* "Tov Li Toras Picha" 5705 (where it is explained according to the *kri* [the way it is read], while in the aforementioned *Likutei Torah* it is explained according to the *kesiv* [the way it is written]. See also Rashi, who brings both interpretations. See also *Sotah* 31a). You surely heard what the Rebbe, my father-in-law, the Nasi, said at the *Shemini Atzeres* *farbrengen* this year regarding the concept that "a Yid is *echad* (one)," and he concluded that "the *echad* must be heard not only within oneself, but also act upon others."

Especially when one considers that each and every day "its curse is greater than the day before" (*Sotah* 49a). If so, it is obvious that in terms of a "good measure," there must be, on the contrary, an **additional** level of elevation each day compared to the previous one, so that he goes "from strength to strength" in this world. It could be said that this is what the Gemara in *Sotah* concludes with: "And upon what does the world stand? Upon *Kiddush Hashem* and *Talmud Torah*" (see Rashi there). This corresponds to the concept of the *beis knesses* and *beis medrash*, which is the "going from strength to strength" (end of *Berachos*). However, in *Sotah*, it refers to the world in general—"upon what does the *olam* (world) stand"—and therefore it must be a matter in which **all** of Israel are involved, *Kiddush Hashem*, etc., whereas in *Berachos* it refers to the individual.

May the *Ribono shel Olam* merit us to see "complete days," at which time "I will fulfill the number of your days" (see *Torah Or*, end of *Parshas Mishpatim*), which can be explained as a form of *teshuvah sheleimah* (complete repentance), through which the *Geulah Sheleimah* (complete redemption) comes.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *Geulah*.

## 34

B"H, 25 Cheshvan, 5703

To our dear friend, the distinguished Tamim, the energetic and accomplished activist, etc., R' Moshe Dolcin, may he live, Mexico.

Peace and blessing!

As a Tamim who takes an interest in and participates in the activities of the Rebbe, may he live, you will surely be interested to hear about the work of two important institutions under the presidency of the Rebbe, may he live: Machne Israel and Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch.

Regarding the work of Machne Israel, we have already written about *Hakriah Ve'hakdushah*, the monthly publication issued by Agudas Chabad, as well as in the *Morgen Journal* (a clipping of which is enclosed). Thank G-d, the activities of Machne Israel have expanded, and the number of members from all circles of those who observe Torah and mitzvos—regardless of affiliation—has grown through the establishment of Tehillim societies, Mishnayos-by-heart societies, and so on.

While the work of Machne Israel is primarily dedicated to adults, Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch is dedicated primarily to the children of Israel, to strengthen their education so that it remains on the foundation of purity and holiness. The branches of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch are numerous: the establishment of "Mesibos Shabbos" societies (we have sent you a booklet with a report on this work), the founding of schools for girls, evening classes for Charedi teachers and educators, and the publication of reading material for Jewish children and youth—specifically the monthly booklet *Shmuessen mit Kinder un Yugend* (in Yiddish and English). We have just completed, with G-d's help, the first year of publication, having released 24 such booklets, which have captured the hearts of the youth, their teachers, and their parents.

It is unnecessary to say that this work, thank G-d, has succeeded in bearing fruit in the strengthening of Torah and Yiddishkeit, and in raising a new generation—a generation of the upright—to the honor and glory of our ancestors.

It is a well-known teaching that "the steps of man are established by Hashem." Every Tamim, wherever he may be, has a special duty to bring light to the Jewish settlements in his location, and to act as much as possible, with mesiras nefesh, in the matter of "spreading your wellsprings outward." This is especially true in these days of *ikvesa d'meshicha*, when a double and redoubled obligation is placed upon every one of the Temimim and Anash to fulfill the mitzvah of "Love your fellow as yourself" and to be among those who bring merit to the many. I am confident that you will exert yourself to be active and productive in all the aforementioned matters and to participate in our holy work, which unites all the Temimim in all four corners of the world. We would be happy to hear back from you regarding what has been done and achieved by you in this regard. We are ready to assist and support you by providing the various materials, and you, for your part, should exert every effort to do everything possible.

I am your friend, seeking your welfare and blessing you with the blessing of "immediately to Teshuvah, immediately to Geulah."

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
**Chairman of the Executive Committee of Machne Israel and Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch**

## 35

B"H, 2 Kislev, 5705

To our dear friend, the distinguished Rav and Chassid, the Temim, the excellent and G-d-fearing, etc., etc., Rabbi Moshe Pinchas Katz, may he live, Newark.

Peace and blessing!

As per your suggestion, letters of thanks and encouragement have been sent to Rabbi Kahan, Mr. Shalom Yaakov Friedman, Mr. Chaim Dovid Friedman, Mr. Mink, and Mr. Fingerman, may they live. Surely you will now endeavor, at the appropriate opportunity and in the proper manner, to ensure that this results in practical benefit, for "today is the day to do them."

Regarding your letter, that we should urge the members of the "Machaneh" not to settle for the easy path, but rather that each one should engage in matters commensurate with his level and capabilities:

a. The concept of the "Machaneh" and the manner of its avodah is that it be without any mixture of ulterior motives of honor or self-aggrandizement. This is why it is conducted without publicizing the names of the members and the workers, and in accordance with the will of the Rebbe shlita. This is a factor which—

b. Makes it very difficult, even for the administration, to precisely evaluate the activities of the members—whether they have engaged and acted to the best of their ability and according to the conditions of their environment, or whether they have settled for a minimal effort, merely to fulfill their obligation.

Therefore, the administration—

c. Relies on the presumption that surely one who joins a camp of workers for the sake of the magnitude of the avodah in strengthening Torah and mitzvos—especially in this time of *ikvesa d'meshicha* and the birth pangs of Moshiach, Heaven forbid—**exclusively**, without any mixture of self-interest, certainly strives to ensure that their avodah is as it should be.

d. Especially since it is known from our Sages (Kesuvos 66b and there) that if one does not do as one ought to do, he is called "one who does not do the will of the Makom," and the punishment for this is great. See also (Avodah Zarah 17b) that it is as if he has no Eloka, etc., if he does not do as he ought. This is explained in Tanya, Iggeres HaKodesh, Chapter 30: "And whoever has not reached... and what difference does it make to me whether it is the aspect of 'turn from evil' or the aspect of 'do good,' etc., but in truth, etc." Terrible words! The administration has nothing to do but—

e. To urge from time to time—in accordance with our Sages (Sifrei, Parshas Naso, and Bamidbar Rabbah, Chapter 7), "one only urges those who are already diligent"—regarding their commitment, without a neder, to at least four good deeds each month. (See Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 14, and the details there, only they are on a higher level, from which it is implied that the avodah must also be ever-increasing, from level to level. And that which is written in Torah Or, in the maamar *Mi KeHashem Elokeinu*, and there, that the text of the prayer in one manuscript is, etc., requires resolution. But this is not the place for it.)

With the blessing of "immediately to teshuvah, immediately to Geulah,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

B"H, 9 Kislev, 5705

To our esteemed friend, the outstanding Avreich, G-d-fearing and learned, etc.,
Rabbi Menachem Zev Gringlas
Montreal

Shalom u’Bracha,

1. Your letters from the 16th, 19th, and 21st of MarCheshvan, along with the enclosed sicha of Shabbos Parshas Bereishis, the letter from Mr. Mendelson, and the postcard from Erev Shabbos Parshas Toldos, have duly arrived. For several reasons, the response has been delayed until now. I am now answering, and we shall address the first matters first.

2. You are surely occupied with the task of recording the memoirs as you promised, and with diligence. Do not say "when I have time," etc., especially in a place where forgetfulness is common.

3. You have surely received the forms for the Sefer Torah long ago; it is surprising that you have not confirmed their receipt. You are surely making an effort to provide them to the people involved in this matter. There is no need to elaborate on the importance of this endeavor.
The receipts for the 25 shekel that you sent for the Sefer Torah via the bank have surely arrived.

4. The rest of the printed materials you requested have been sent, except for those from the sichos of previous months, which have all been sold. Therefore, it is best that in the future you inform us in advance of your estimate of how many you will need. As for the calendar, the first edition has already run out; a second edition is currently being printed, and upon its publication, the hundred copies you requested will be sent to you.

5. The editing of your Chassidus materials is being delayed due to the heavy workload here. When things ease up, they will be sent to you.

6. Letters and samples of the publications issued by Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch have been sent to the United Talmud Torahs and also to the Adas Yisroel community, as you instructed. (The letters were sent on the 8th of Kislev).

7. Your request regarding the Kuntres has been conveyed.

8. Regarding what is brought in the sicha of Shabbos Parshas Bereishis: "Getzoigter" means one who pulls his hair. Its meaning is: one who curls his hair, is particular about the arrangement and beauty of his clothing, and the like. "Gepeishteter" means pampered.

9. The sicha of Simchas Torah has not yet been edited (except for the section that is in the Kuntres). As for Shemini Atzeres, there is only an **unedited** version. If you do not have it yet, let me know, and I will send my copy **on the condition that it be returned**.

10. Mr. Arlin delivered ten shekel on his behalf. It has been recorded toward the balance due for printing matters. Nothing was received via the "Guter Yid," as he calls him.

11. Materials printed in Warsaw were also sent via the "Guter Yid." They have surely reached you. You have surely also received the items sent by Mr. Arlin: one Tanya and the Warsaw Maamarim. There are unbound Tanyas that are missing pages 129–136. Only a few copies of complete Tanyas remain, and the price is 50 cents; the bound ones are priced at 75 cents for students. A set of Likutei Torah is priced at 4 shekel (here).

12. Thank you for the news about the city of Winnipeg. We heard about a Rav there by the name of Kanovitch. Do you know his nature?

13. Enclosed is a circular letter sent to all members of the camp every month. If you provide us with the addresses of members in the camp, we would send it to them as well. The responses to this letter come before the Rebbe, Nasi of the camp.

14. Enclosed is a copy of two letters of response to some of the camp members regarding their questions concerning the aforementioned circular.

15. You will surely inform us about your work regarding the Shabbos gatherings and the organization of Beis Rivkah, as you wrote in your letter.

With the blessing of "L'alter L'teshuva, L'alter L'geula,"

**Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Vaad Hapoel

B"H, 4th day of Chanukah, 5703

To our dear friend, the eminent Rabbi and Chassid, a man of many talents and accomplishments, etc., Rabbi A. Dubraw, Washington.

Shalom u’Bracha!

We are sending you—in a separate package—a copy of the letter from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita, for the day of the *Tishrei* [holiday] **and the days that follow**. It is superfluous to draw your attention to the great necessity of publicizing it among the widest possible circles in your camp and wherever your influence extends, by posting it on the walls of the *beis medrash* and the like.

Before the past *Rosh Hashanah*, we also sent you various printed materials regarding the awakening of *teshuvah*, etc., from the *sichos* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita. It is surprising that we have not been honored with a response from you until now, nor have you confirmed their receipt.

Now, the matter of the *Chanukah* light is to illuminate the outside and the public domain (*reshus harabim*). It is explained in *Torah Or*, in the *maamar* beginning "Ki Atah Neri Hashem," that this is, in particular, the *avodah* of our generations, the *ikvesa d’Meshicha*.

It is ruled as *halacha* that even if one lives in an upper story (*aliyah*)—(I have seen "those of the *aliyah*," and they are few, for their *avodah* is for the sake of the High One and on a very high level, as written in *Sefer Shel Beinonim*, Chapter 10)—and they have no opening (to the matters of this world), one must still place the *Chanukah* light at least in a window that illuminates the public domain.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Chairman of the Executive Committee

B"H, Ner Daled of Chanukah, 5703

To the honorable Rav, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, a man of many virtues and great accomplishments, etc., Moreinu HaRav Avraham Eliyahu, may he live, Axelrod,
Baltimore

Shalom u’Bracha!

It is surprising that we have not received any response to our letter from the 31st of MarCheshvan.

To conclude with matters related to the above and to the days of Chanukah: the concept of the Chanukah light is to illuminate the outside. Even if one lives in an upper story—"I have seen those who ascend, and they are few"—one must place it in the window adjacent to the public domain to illuminate the place of darkness (see *Drushei Chanukah* 259). It is explained in *Torah Or*, in the *maamar* beginning "For You are my lamp," that this is also the concept of "And Hashem will illuminate my darkness" for our generations, the *ikvesa d’Meshicha*. It can be said that specifically in this time of the birth pangs of Mashiach and harsh decrees, Heaven forbid (*Sanhedrin* 97b), the concept of "Hashem decrees and the Tzaddik annuls" must be realized. This is achieved by turning a wicked person into a *baal teshuvah*, as explained by the Targum and Rashi (*Yirmiyahu* 15:19) and according to our Sages (*Bava Metzia* 85a), this is through Torah study for the sake of the unlearned.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Chairman of the Executive Committee

Please expedite its publication; if it is possible to publish it in your newspaper as well, that would be excellent. I am also writing to our friend, the Chassid, etc., R. M. L., may he live, regarding this.

The essence of the Chanukah lights is to illuminate the place of darkness, as explained in *Gevuros Hashem* (Chanukah discourses, 259) and in *Torah Ohr* in the *maamar* beginning "For You are my lamp," that this is also the concept of "Hashem will illuminate my darkness" for our generations, the *ikvesa d'meshicha*. It can be said that specifically in this time of the birth pangs of Moshiach and harsh decrees, Heaven forbid (Sanhedrin 97b), we must fulfill the concept that "Hashem issues a decree and the Tzaddik annuls it." This is achieved by causing a wicked person to repent, as explained by the Targum and Rashi (Yirmiyahu 15:19), and according to our Sages (Bava Metzia 85a), this is accomplished through Torah study for the sake of an unlearned person.

With blessings for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

Chairman of the Executive Committee

B"H, 4th day of Chanukah, 5703

To the honorable Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing man, and man of many accomplishments, whose lips guard knowledge and whose Torah is upon him, etc., Moreinu Harav R. A. HaKohen, may he live, Philadelphia.

By way of a *chiddush* (play on words), one could say (Shabbos 21b) that the **ner** (candle) of Chanukah is a mitzvah to place at the entrance of one’s house **on the outside** — and according to the *Mishneh Torah* (Hilchos Megillah v’Chanukah 4:7), at the entrance adjacent to the **public domain** (and according to the opinion of the *Tosafos*), in a place and time where the *amgusha* (magician/heretic) can say "from the middle and above, etc." (*Sanhedrin* 39a), and not in a private domain. And if one lives in an upper story, being among the "people of the upper realm," who are few in number (*Sukkah* 45b) and do not have an entrance open to the matters of this world, one must at the very least place it in a window adjacent to the public domain.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Chairman of the Executive Committee

B”H, 4th day of Chanukah, 5703

To the esteemed donor, G-d-fearing and upright, etc., [Name]...

Peace and blessing!

You have surely already received your membership card for the Chevra Mishnayos B’al Peh.

The Gemara states (Shevuos 39a) that all Jews are responsible (*areivim*) for one another. Regarding this, the Rebbe Shlita said: "The word *arev* has three meanings: sweet, mixed together, and surety. A Jew to a Jew is sweet; a Jew with a Jew is intermingled; and a Jew is surety (*arev*) for another Jew," end quote.

Through one Torah, Jews become one nation, which is unified with Hashem Elokeinu Hashem Echad.

We hope that you will not be satisfied with merely a good eye for your own self, but will be among those who merit the masses, and that you will participate with all possible means in the far-reaching work of Machaneh Yisrael.

As the Rebbe Shlita has warned on several occasions, we are currently in the final times of the galus, and Torah and teshuvah are the only means to alleviate the birth pangs of Moshiach.

The ahavah that every Jew must feel for another Jew calls forth in his heart the greatest compassion for one who is not doing teshuvah in these times.

From the newspaper clipping that we have enclosed, you will see in which area, given the circumstances, it is easiest for you to begin working. Before one begins the work, it may seem difficult, but once one approaches the work, one sees that with the help of the Ribono shel Olam, one accomplishes.

Awaiting your prompt reply,

With the blessing of "Immediately to teshuvah, immediately to Geulah,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

P.S. The Rebbe Shlita has issued the letter that we are enclosing here, and it is a great mitzvah to publicize it as much as possible—posting it in shuls, etc.

43

[Erev Rosh Chodesh Teves, 5703]

In response to your comments:

1) Regarding your observation concerning what was brought in my letter from Kesuvos (67a), "according to the camel is the burden," and the teaching of our Sages, "one who offers much and one who offers little [are equal, provided one directs his heart to Heaven]," the latter statement applies to a case where the one who offers little does not do so because of a lack of intent of heart toward Heaven—as the conclusion states, "provided one directs his heart"—but rather, the Sages are teaching us that their reward is equal.

Therefore, this refers to a situation where either it was not in his power to offer more (see Berachos 5b, where this teaching of our Sages is cited by Rabbi Elazar, who wept because he could not study as he desired—according to the initial thought—and it is also said of Rabbi Elazar in Eruvin 54b, "with her love you shall always be intoxicated." And in Berachos 17a, Rashi explains [s.v. *v'shama*] that he did not have an "open heart," etc.), or where offering more is not the point of the matter (this is the question of the Tosafos [s.v. *l'lamdecha*] in Shevuos 15a, that the concept of "one who offers much" does not apply there because the two aforementioned conditions are absent: the increase there is a mitzvah, and it was in their power to increase. They answer that we know "one who offers much" [is not a reason] to boast, etc.).

This is unlike a case where the mitzvah involves an increase and it is within one’s power to do so, for then, "according to the camel is the burden," etc. This is straightforward.

2) Regarding your comment that the teaching of our Sages, "one only encourages those who are already encouraged," is also brought in Makkos (23a).

Indeed, even in *Otzar HaPitgamim* by Rabbi Hyman, he only cites Makkos and Bamidbar Rabbah, omitting the fact that it is found in Sifrei Naso. The reality is the opposite: the primary source of the statement is in Sifrei, but because the book of Sifrei is not as commonly available, it is also noted in Bamidbar Rabbah. (One could delve into the books of *klalim* regarding the distinction between Sifrei and Midrash Rabbah, concerning the rule that one does not derive [halachic rulings] from Aggadah—Yerushalmi Peah 2:4—and see also *Likutei Torah*, *Beha'aloscha*, "Lo Tashbit," 60a. Furthermore, Sifrei is for Tannaim, unlike Midrash Rabbah). In Makkos, this statement is brought:

a) As a variation. It is known that sometimes it is the way of the Shas to vary even in minor details (see the book *Klalei HaShas*).

b) Regarding a matter of "sit and do nothing" (*shev v'al ta'aseh*).

c) Contrary to the view of Rava—who is a later authority—and in the context of the dispute between Rabbi Yehuda and the Sages. This is not the case in Sifrei, where it is possible that they do not disagree—see the commentaries on Rashi at the beginning of Parshas Tzav, the explanation of the Malbim on Parshas Naso, and elsewhere.

Since we are on the subject, it is necessary to clarify:

a) The possibility that the reward could be equal even though one offers more, etc., can be noted from what is explained regarding Rabbi Elazar ben Durdaya (*Likutei Torah* of the Arizal, Tehillim, section 32; and one may delve further into *Likutei Torah*, the *maamar* beginning "Ki B'yom HaZeh" I, section 4, and "Tiku" I, section 2) and from what is written in *Torah Or*, the *maamar* beginning "Chayav Inish."

b) Seemingly, one could say that regarding sacrifices, one must bring the choicest of the species one wishes to bring (Menachos 83b), but there is no obligation to increase the number of sacrifices—even though one receives reward for the increase. Only regarding Re'iyah and Chagigah, concerning which it is said "according to the gift of his hand," must it be according to his wealth (Chagigah 8b). Similarly, one may bring a bird even if one is wealthy (see *Lechem Mishneh*, *Hilchos Ma'aseh HaKorbanos* 15:9). This is the precision in the extra wording of the Shas in Menachos (104b), "whose *way* is," etc.—meaning that this is indeed the way, but it is possible that a wealthy person may also bring a *minchah*.

With this, one can explain: 1) The intent of Rashi in Menachos (110a), s.v. "one who offers much," where he added the words "to bring sacrifices"—meaning that he increases the number, and not as in the passage in Shevuos, which refers to an increase in quality. 2) The extra wording in Rashi in Berachos (5b, 17a), where he writes that "one who offers much" is said regarding sacrifices. This is because, for Rashi, the phrase "one who offers little" implies that it was in his power to offer more, yet he offered little. Since the passage in Berachos refers to Torah study, Rashi emphasizes that this [principle] is regarding sacrifices—specifically. The reason is as mentioned above, that there is no obligation [to increase in sacrifices], unlike Torah study.

The fact that the Shas in Berachos brings proof from this refers to the fact that if the "little" does not diminish the intent of his heart toward Heaven (and in Torah study, this is only possible if it is not in his power, as is understood—for if it were in his power, then it would be said of him, "for he has despised the word of Hashem"—Sanhedrin 99a), then "one who offers much," etc. Consequently, in Torah study, where one offers little because it was not in his power, his reward is like that of one who offers much. And this is clear.

With blessings for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 44

44

B"H, Zos Chanukah, 5703

To the honored and distinguished, G-d-fearing and wise, etc., R’ Y. Sheinfeld, may he live,
Roxbury, Mass.

Greetings and blessings!

In accordance with the instruction of the Rebbe when he was here, we have sent to your esteemed daughter, may she live, the printing materials published for the youth by the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch. We are certain that with her great energy and influence, your esteemed daughter will endeavor to ensure that the monthly publications and the like reach the boys and girls, and in doing so, she will be among those who bring merit to the public, for the merit of the public will depend upon her.

Our hope is strong that in the future, too, you will endeavor, to the best of your ability, to provide the youth circles within your sphere of influence with the material published by the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, whose sole desire is to bring the sons and daughters of Israel closer to Torah, mitzvos, and the tradition of our fathers. For "if there are no kids, there will be no goats," and the little ones and students of today are the sages of tomorrow; upon this depends the resting of the Shechinah upon Israel, as the language of the Yerushalmi (Sanhedrin, Chapter 10, Halachah 2) states.

In these days, days of harsh decrees like those of Haman, as our Sages of blessed memory have said (Sanhedrin 97b), the advice offered by our Sages (Bava Metzia 85a) is to teach Torah to the children of the common people and to bring the wicked to teshuvah—as per the Targum and Rashi on the verse in Yirmiyahu there—for then the decree is nullified. Every person must view the world as half-innocent and half-guilty, and through his good deeds, he tips the scale of the world to the side of merit, thereby bringing about salvation and rescue.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate redemption,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 45

*[Chanukah, 5703]*

... 11) Regarding your question in your holy letter of Cheshvan 5705, concerning the omission—in the copy of *Sefer Shel Beinonim*, Chapter 6—of the phrase *eish mislakachas* (a fire infolding itself). You mean to ask the intent of the copyist, since the *gimel klippos temeios* (three impure klippos) are: *ruach* (wind), *se'arah* (storm), and *anan gadol* (a great cloud).

While one could find a basis for interpreting *ruach se'arah* as a **compound** of two, based on what is written in *Avodas HaKodesh* (cited in *Likutei Torah*, Parshas Kedoshim, Part *Sefer Torah*, Chapter 19—and this is in *Zohar* III, 196a) that *ruach se'arah* refers to *Zon*, whereas *ruach* alone or *se'arah* alone [refer to something else], this is merely for the sake of pilpul. It is simple that in *Sefer Shel Beinonim* this is a printing omission, and it should read: *ruach, se'arah, anan gadol, v'eish mislakachas*.

See *Etz Chaim*, Gate 7, Chapter 3, and *Likutei Torah*, discourse *Vayikchu Eilecha Parah*, which discuss the matter of Chapter 6 of *Sefer Shel Beinonim*, and it is stated there explicitly, including *eish* as well.

There are countless places in general where *eish mislakachas* is counted among the *klippos* (for example, *Zohar* III, 231a).

However, on the face of it, it is puzzling that in *Sefer Shel Beinonim* he lists and explains *ruach, se'arah,* and *anan gadol*, but *eish mislakachas* is only hinted at with the word "etc." Especially since it is known how precise the Alter Rebbe was in the language of his *Sefer Shel Beinonim*. Yet, in all the editions of *Tanya* that I have seen, including those printed during the Alter Rebbe’s lifetime, it is written as mentioned above.

Simply put, it could be said: "Are we to act like a peddler and count every detail?" A hint suffices.

The reason he explains "and a great cloud" but does not write "wind, storm, etc." is because the wording of the verse is: "A stormy wind came out of the north, a great cloud, and a fire infolding itself, and a brightness was about it." If he had written in *Sefer Shel Beinonim* "wind, storm, etc.," there would be room to err that the "north" is one of the *gimel klippos temeios*. But the "etc." that follows "a great cloud" cannot be mistaken in its intent. Furthermore, the words "a fire infolding itself" are adjacent to the words "a great cloud."

— Were I not afraid, I would say that in *Sefer Shel Beinonim* it should be *anan* (cloud) without a *vav*, according to the wording of the verse. Just as it begins "and they are called, etc.," to which "cloud" without a *vav* would correspond later. But in all editions, it is written with a *vav*. —

One must also understand the intent of what is written in *Sefer Shel Beinonim*, "and they are called in the Chariot, etc.," for seemingly, what is the practical difference here? It could be said that he comes to indicate from where the *gimel klippos temeios* (and also the *klippah* of *nogah*) emerged, since there is no good in them at all (see this at length in *Likutei Torah*, *Likkutei Gimmel Parshiyos*, discourse *Lehavin Inyan HaBrachos*, section 7-8). Regarding this, he says "and they are called, etc.," meaning this is their root above.

— See the explanation in *Eileh Masei* 3, at the beginning. He did not say this earlier in Chapter 1, because there the *gimel klippos temeios* were not mentioned except in passing. —

While speaking of this matter, I would like to note that, for the time being, I have not found in *Chassidus* an explanation of the distinction between the *gimel klippos temeios* themselves, one from the other, aside from the general distinction in the aforementioned *Eileh Masei*. At first glance, it could be said that they correspond to the three lines (the three elements: fire, wind, and cloud—which is water; and the element of earth is included in them, as is known). The right line in the powers of the soul is water; the left is fire; and the middle is wind.

Regarding the moral and *avodah* aspect, their matter is explained in *Reishis Chochmah*, *Shaar HaYirah*, Chapter 4. In *Pardes*, Gate 26, Chapter 7, it is explained—based on *Tikkunei Zohar*—that cloud, fire, and wind correspond to *Chokhmah, Da'as, Ruach*. In *Koheles Yaakov*, under their entries, fire, cloud, and wind are *Binah* and *Zon* of *klippah*—based on the introduction to *Tikkunei Zohar* that the letters of the Name *Havayah* are embedded within them—and under the entry for the four *klippos*, they are *Chagas, Nehi, Malchus* of *klippah*, and *klippas nogah* is *Ein Sof* and *Chachmah, Binah, Da'as* of *klippah*, etc. If so, according to what is explained in the discourse *BeYom HaShemini Atzeres* 5711 and the discourse *Lo Silbash Shatnez* 5728 (see *Etz Chaim*, Gate 48, Chapter 3; *Mevo Shearim*, Gate 6, Part 2, Chapter 4), in *klippah* the order is reversed: *Malchus* and below it *Ze'er Anpin*, etc. According to this, *eish mislakachas* is below *ruach* and *anan*. This requires further study in light of the aforementioned *Likutei Torah*, *Masei*. In *Etz Chaim*, Gate 48, Chapter 4, it is implied that their order from below to above is *ruach, se'arah, anan,* and *eish*.

See also what is written regarding the third *klippah* in the nut (which is fire) in *Zohar* III, 287a and 287b—cited in *Pardes* there, Chapter 26—and in *Pri Etz Chaim*, *Shaar HaPurim*, near the end. But this is not the place to elaborate.

To conclude with something good and relevant to the days:

The *mitzvah* and purpose of the Chanukah lights is to illuminate the public domain, the place of darkness—see *Torah Or*, discourse *Ki Atah Neri*, that this is also "and I will turn darkness into light" in our generations, the heels of Mashiach. Now, *choshech* (darkness) is an acronym for *chamor* (donkey), *shor* (ox), *kelev* (dog), as written in the discourse *Ner Chanukah* 5699 (printed in *HaTamim* 3). These are the *gimel klippos temeios*: *chamor* is the right line, *shor* is the left line, and *kelev* is *Amalek*, as written in the aforementioned discourse, the *Da'as* of *klippah*. This is possible only through *Torah Or* (Chassidus), unlike *tefillah*, as explained in the Chanukah discourses of 5659.

It is proven there that this is specifically through the revealed part of Torah, the Oral Torah, which is in the place that is being clarified (see *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 26; the introduction to *Biurei HaZohar*; *Kuntres Etz Chaim*; the letter printed in *HaTamim* 3 to our master and teacher, and more).

Were I not afraid to say something new, it would seem that the **avodah of studying** Chassidus has the advantage, as it is both, for it is the inner dimension of the Torah and is found in the place that is being clarified.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 48

24 Teves,
The Hilula of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe,
5705

To our esteemed friends, the distinguished and excellent Rabbis and Chassidim,
Men of valor in the army of Torah, the Temimim, may they live,
Montreal, Canada

Shalom u’vracha!

You are surely aware of the details regarding the work of the "Merkaz L’Inyonei Chinuch" (Central Organization for Education), which the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, established more than a year ago. A brief report was also published in *HaKriah VeHaKedushah* for Tishrei-Teves 5705.

One of the primary aspects of this work is the education of the **daughters** of Israel, an area that has suffered from much neglect for various reasons. Specifically, this involves the establishment of schools for them—under the names "Beis Rivkah" or "Beis Sarah"—and the founding of "Shabbos Clubs" for young girls.

Following the presentation by the director of the Merkaz, Rabbi Ch. M. A. Hodakov, shlita, regarding his visit to Montreal, the Merkaz has decided to establish the aforementioned in your camp, and subsequently, to the extent possible, in other cities in your country as well.

We are therefore turning to you to take upon yourselves—all of you, or a few of you who are suited for this, according to your choice and judgment—this invaluable work. As the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, says: "A covenant is forged for propaganda and work that they shall not return empty."

The details of the work plan vary according to the conditions of each location, but in general, it is divided into three categories:

a) Establishing a school for young girls and adolescents;
b) Establishing "Shabbos Clubs" for young girls;
c) Organizing classes—in the form of courses or friendly discussions—whose goal is to train, in a short time, counselors for the "Shabbos Clubs," speakers, and organizers for outreach among the girls and adolescents, and in general, those who can take part in the work in all its aforementioned categories.

Experience here has shown that one should hope for influence in wider circles and less opposition if the aforementioned is done without any mixture of other agendas or matters, even matters of holiness, or even a secondary name. Indeed, here too, the Merkaz is an independent institution.

An awakening to work in this field is surely superfluous for people like you. I will only add a few remarks:

In the *Mechilta*—cited in Rashi on the Torah, *Shemos* (19:3)—it is stated that the Holy One, blessed be He, prioritized "the house of Jacob," which refers to the women, over the "children of Israel," the men. In *Shemos Rabbah* (beginning of ch. 28), the reason given is that they are diligent in the performance of mitzvos; another explanation is so that they might lead their children to Torah. See the *sicha* of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, Riga 5694, on this.

Similarly, regarding reward, our Sages say in *Berachos* (17a), "The promise that the Holy One, blessed be He, made to women is greater than that made to men."

Especially in our time, the footsteps of Moshiach, the primary work is the work of *tzedakah*, as written in *Iggeres HaKodesh* (Section 7), "And Israel is only redeemed through *tzedakah*." Our Sages say (*Taanis* 23b) that in this, women have an advantage over men, for they give bread (food) while men give coins.

The explanation of this statement of our Sages in *Taanis* regarding *avodah* can be understood in the following way: The manner of influencing another—and also one’s own *nefesh habahamit*—can be done in two ways:

1) First and foremost, one seeks strategies to ensure that his fellow does everything incumbent upon him during his descent on the mission of the King in this world, even if it is through *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke) on the part of the fellow. That is, even if he does not yet understand the necessity of the matter and lacks *ahavah* and *yirah* (love and fear of Hashem). (See Rambam, *Hilchos Teshuvah*, end of ch. 10: that we educate them to serve out of fear until their knowledge increases and they serve out of love). It is understood that one who is himself a person of *kabbalas ol* has a "sense" and an attraction to such a method, and he will easily find the "letters" in speech and action that can influence his fellow.

2) Another method is to begin by attempting to explain to his fellow the greatness of the Creator, His love, His fear, etc., until through this, his fellow comes on his own to the correct recognition and the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos. It is understood that this method is favored by those who are "men of intellect," *maskilim*, whose conduct is based on the intellect and knowledge, firmly and unchangeably.

This is the meaning of the statement of our Sages in *Taanis*: "When a poor person comes"—and there is no "poor" person except one who is poor in knowledge—one must act according to the words of the prophet, "Is it not to share your bread with the hungry..." (Yeshayahu 58:7). The Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, explained—*sicha* of Purim 5691, *Kuntres* 13—that when one sees a Jew who is "naked," without *tzitzis* and without *tefillin*, "cover him." This is based on *Tanna D'bei Eliyahu* (ch. 27), which states: "If you see a person who lacks knowledge of Torah, bring him into your house and teach him *Krias Shema* and *tefillah*, and teach him one verse or one *halacha*, and urge him in mitzvos, for there is no one 'naked' in Israel except one who lacks Torah and mitzvos, and he is like one who is naked."

If the "poor person" meets a man—whose way and nature is to go outside and to distant places and to trade with his silver and gold, as explained regarding *avodah* in the *maamarim* of *Parshas Vayeshev*—he gives the poor person a coin, *ahavah* and *yirah*.

Since these are "wings"—as explained in *Sefer Shel Beinonim* (end of ch. 15)—and the ultimate goal is service out of love, the poor person still has the burden of acquiring his meal.

But if he meets a woman—for "everything a woman acquires, her husband acquires," "For your Maker is your husband, Hashem, Master of Legions is His name"—as explained in *Torah Or* (in the *maamar* beginning "Lo Tihyeh"), that *ahavah* and *yirah* are a gift from Hashem, etc.—and like a servant, for everything he acquires, etc., and her service is only that she does the will of her husband, *kabbalas ol*, such that even *ahavah* and *yirah* are in this manner—she gives the poor person bread, which is ready for the meal. For through *kabbalas ol*, it can be achieved even for the poor person without any gradual process at all. (To note from *Likutei Torah*, end of *Parshas Vezos HaBerachah*, and also from the *maamar* beginning "V'Hashem Amar HaMechaseh"—the continuation of *Reshimu*—regarding the explanation that "extra understanding" was given to women more than to men).

And *mesiras nefesh*, *kabbalas ol*, and the fulfillment of mitzvos in deed and action is also the virtue of the "footsteps" and the generation of the footsteps of Moshiach—see the *sicha* of 20 Kislev 5694, section 9.

May it be the will of Hashem that we all merit, speedily and in our days, the fulfillment of the promise, "I will take the children of Israel from among the nations... and My servant David shall be king over them," a great deed (*Torah Or*, *maamarim* of *Vayigash*; "V'Avdei David" 5699), "A woman of valor is the crown of her husband."

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*.

## 50

[Beginning of Shevat, 5703?]

...Regarding what you noted in the margins of your letter concerning the statement in Maseches Sofrim (Chapter 2, Halacha 5) that the lights of Chanukah increase in number, where two reasons are provided—"we elevate in matters of holiness and do not lower," and "corresponding to the days that are departing"—even though in Shabbos (21b) this is a dispute between Amoraim: this has already been noted in the commentary *Nachalas Yaakov* on Maseches Sofrim (printed in the Shas), although he does not explain it at all, stating only: "The Gemara here holds like both reasons mentioned in the Shas."

It may be said that since we are not in a position to decide between the two reasons, and neither contradicts the other, and there is no practical difference between them, they are considered equal and both may be cited. We find even stronger instances in the Shas where, even in cases with practical implications, they say (Berachos 59a-b, and elsewhere): "Therefore, let us say both." One may also point to the commentary of the Rashbam in Bava Basra (75a), "Let it be according to this opinion and according to that opinion," and other similar instances.

Since the matter has come up, let us say a word regarding the reasoning behind "the days that are entering" versus "the days that are departing," and why the number of lights increases or decreases. This depends on clarifying whether the miracle of Chanukah was progressively greater from day to day, or the opposite. Now, in the year of the miracle, when they did not yet know how many days the oil would last (and the commentators have already raised difficulties regarding the answer that they divided the oil on the first day into eight parts—and one could add a further difficulty from Zevachim (88a) that sacred vessels only sanctify when full, and if the measure is lacking they do not sanctify, and from Menachos (88b) that it is obvious that with the first measure, etc.), it is clear that **to the eyes of the observers**, the miracle was going and increasing from day to day. However, our Sages said in Shabbos (ibid.) that they only established Chanukah for the following year. By then, it had already been revealed retroactively that it was **in the potential** of the oil found in the flask on the first day to burn for eight days, whereas on the second day, it did not have the potential to burn for more than seven days, and so on.

This is the reasoning of Beis Shammai, corresponding to the "days that are entering," for the measure of the burning for all eight entering days was included, by way of a miracle, in the quantity of this oil, and from day to day the miracle was going and decreasing. But Beis Hillel say that the miracle of the entering days was only **in potential** and had not yet emerged into actuality. One should not be stringent and insist that everyone recognize such a miracle, for the majority of the world only acknowledges what their eyes see in actuality.

—Similar to the statement of our Sages in Yoma (21a): "They count the miracles that are external, they do not count the miracles that are internal."

Therefore, we must light corresponding to the "days that are departing," for the miracle is in actual reality, especially regarding the lighting of the Chanukah candles, which is a matter of *pirsumei nisa*—publicizing the miracle—**to the many**, and from this perspective, the miracle goes and increases from day to day.

—Based on the above, it is explained that here, too, Beis Shammai follow the stringent view and Beis Hillel the lenient view.—

By way of a *chidud* (sharp insight), one could say that we find a similar approach to the positions of Beis Shammai and Beis Hillel here in other places as well.

This is in Uktzin (Chapter 3, Mishna 4): "From when do fish become susceptible to impurity? Beis Shammai say: From when they are caught," for then, in potential, they are already dead, since they have been separated from their place of life and are only lacking time. Beis Hillel say: "From when they die in actual reality."

To conclude with a matter of *mussar* and *avodah*, in brief: the second reason in the dispute between Beis Shammai and Beis Hillel is "corresponding to the festival offerings," and "we elevate in matters of holiness."

For the approaches of Shammai and Hillel in a person’s *avodah* to their Creator are explained in Shabbos (31a): Shammai for stringency and Hillel for leniency.

Therefore, for one whose *yetzer hara* has defiled their sanctuary and who comes to be purified and to enter under the wings of the *Shechinah*: according to Beis Shammai, the beginning and essence of the *avodah* is "turn from evil" and "burn the evil from within you." When one begins the *avodah*, the evil is at its peak, and one requires great exertion and great light, and such exertion is demanded of them. But from day to day, the evil goes and decreases, and consequently, there is no need for as great a light as on the first day. An example of this is the festival offerings, which are brought corresponding to the seventy nations so that the world will not be "desolate" (*tzadia*—empty) of them (Yalkut Shimoni, end of Parshas Pinchas), but rather that they will be turned to good; and from day to day, the evil within them goes and decreases, and therefore there is no longer a need for such a large number of sacrifices.

—Based on this, it is understood that there is no contradiction between the reason that the festival offerings decrease corresponding to the seventy nations (see Rashi, end of Parshas Pinchas, and Chiddushei Aggados in Shabbos) and the statement of our Sages in Sukkah (55b) that they are to provide atonement for them.—

But Beis Hillel say that at the very beginning, one must enter under the wings of the *Shechinah* even while the evil is still at its peak within them, and begin their *avodah* with matters of "do good"—actual *avodah* in holiness—and "one mitzvah leads to another," and "we elevate in matters of holiness," that little by little they will gain strength to go and increase, until they acknowledge and praise His **great** Name, so that the seed of Amalek will be erased and the Name will be great and complete (see Tosafos, s.v. *Ve'onim*, Berachos 3a).

We would be happy to hear of your good activities regarding the matters of the *avodah* of "Machne Yisrael" and "Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch," and surely you will write to us from time to time regarding this. Thank you in advance.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 51

B"H, 11 Shevat, 5705

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim
Montreal

Greetings and Blessings!

Rabbi Chaim Dovber Ginzburg, may he live, of Vancouver, B.C., writes to us in his letter, among other things, the following:

"Upon my arrival in Vancouver, I found and saw a young bochur who resides here... His origin is from the city of Vienna, the capital of Austria. Due to the war, he was taken, along with other refugees, as a prisoner of war in an internment camp in Canada, in the city of Quebec. It has been several months since he was released from there through the efforts of his relative who lives here in Vancouver. This bochur is truly a *yirei shamayim* and was one of those who frequented the beis medrash in his aforementioned hometown. He comes from a distinguished family; his parents also fled for their lives from the fear of the enemy's sword and succeeded in making their way to America, but their son does not have permission to enter there.

"Currently, this bochur’s material situation is quite precarious. He has no help from his parents, as they are also in dire straits, and in order to find a source of sustenance, he is forced to commit himself to any work. In his spare hours, he engages in secular studies at a school. I see with my own eyes that a danger awaits him here—that he might, Heaven forbid, become *mufkar* like the other young people in the city of Vancouver, whose entire goal is to cast off the yoke and become emptied of all Jewish spirit. Therefore, I have tried with all my might to save this Jewish soul from the fire, and I spoke to his heart that he would be fortunate if he were to travel to the city of Montreal to the Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim. My words made an impression on him, and he agrees to this. In truth, with his fine intellect and his entire path and essence, he is worthy of being attached to the Yeshivah and to ascend higher and higher, until he becomes very great. Therefore, I ask of your honor to please be so kind as to turn to the administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Montreal so that they might agree to accept him into the Yeshivah. If I obtain a proper and positive response regarding this, I will hasten to do everything to send him to the Yeshivah as soon as possible!"

I am certain you will take an interest in this matter **as soon as possible**, and inform us as well of what you have decided in this regard.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**M. Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 52

52

B"H, 11 Shevat, 5705

To the distinguished and honored, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in the work of Hashem, etc., R' Y. [may he live],

Peace and blessing!

We hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Rosh Chodesh Shevat, along with your check for five dollars for the five calendars. As per your request, we have sent you 24 of the new monthly booklets in English, starting from Teves. The booklet for Shevat will appear by Tu B'Shevat.

We are pleased with your decision to exert effort in distributing the booklets, and we thank you for this. Surely, the great benefit they bring to all who read them will soon be evident.

We have just published a "Seder Brachos and Tefillos" with a precise text and a refined English translation. We are sending it to you under your management, and generally for the youth circles over whom you have influence—the price is 15 cents, and for Talmud Torahs, 10 cents.

Scripture states that "man is the tree of the field," and the "vineyard of Hashem Tzevaos is the house of Israel." The fruits are the children—the sons and the daughters. How great is the responsibility of the leader and the gardener into whose hand the Master of the vineyard has entrusted His vineyard! This is why our Sages, of blessed memory, said that the teaching of children is called the "work of Hashem," and how great is the merit of one whom Hashem has appointed to guard His vineyard.

We see that every improvement, even a small one, in the seed, causes great beauty and excellence in the tree that grows from it.

With blessings for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

Chairman of the Executive Committee
