53

B"H, Friday, 14 Adar I, 5705

To the honorable Rav, the G-d-fearing man of action, etc.,
Rabbi N. M. [shlita], Shochet u'Bodek,

Shalom u'Bracha!

We have received your letter containing the list of members for the *Mishnayos b'al peh* society and the *Tehillim* society.

We thank you for your participation in our work, and we hope that in the future you will continue to gather strength to assist us in the work of *zikkui harabim*.

Not long ago, there was a *Mishnayos b'al peh* raffle. We are enclosing your membership card herewith. For the others who registered through you for the *Mishnayos b'al peh* society, we are sending their cards to their respective addresses. The names of the people you listed for the *Tehillim* society have also been sent to Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established.

We have arranged for the *shmuessen* to be sent to the three people whose addresses you provided, and they are surely receiving them on time. We are enclosing the invoice for this herewith.

We would be happy to hear from you regarding your good activities on behalf of *Machne Israel* and *Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch* from the time you wrote your letter to us until now.

It is well known regarding the laws of this week’s *parsha*, *V'atah Tetzaveh*—"to kindle a lamp continually"—that the *Kohen* must kindle the lamps until the flame rises by itself. This concept in the *avodah* of man in these days—it is stated (Pesikta, cited in Yalkut Shimoni, Zechariah 4): "A golden menorah, all of it"—this refers to Yisrael, as it is written, "You are all beautiful, My beloved." And the *Kohen*—meaning one whom Hashem has graced and chosen to serve before Him in holiness (see Rambam, end of *Hilchos Shemitah v'Yovel*)—must strive in the kindling of the lamps, to kindle the "lamp of Hashem, the soul of man" (*ner Hashem nishmas adam*) of those he knows and is acquainted with. He must continue to kindle it until the flame—the *yud* of the light of Torah and *mitzvos*—rises within them by itself, and they will no longer require one to rebuke or arouse them. The measure of the kindling is "until morning"—this is the World to Come, which is entirely morning (Yerushalmi, *Chagigah* 2:1).

With blessings for *l'altar l'teshuvah, l'altar l'geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 54

*[Late Adar Rishon, 5703]*

B"H.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and accomplished Rav, wise, etc., R. E. N. (may he live):

Shalom u’Bracha!

Regarding your question on *Tanya*, Chapter 17, concerning what is stated there—that in truth, it is impossible for *resha'im* to begin serving Hashem without first doing *teshuvah* for the past—you ask whether this means it is impossible for them to be *sur me'ra* and *aseh tov* in practice at all, or if it only means that they cannot reach this through the mode of the "mind ruling over the heart"—where, by contemplating Hashem’s greatness, etc., they would come to perform *mitzvos*—but that they *can* reach this through the assistance of their power of *kabalas ol* and similar forces, which aid the contemplation in the mind.

You bring a proof for the second interpretation from the fact that: a) In worldly matters, such as business, even *resha'im* have a mind that rules over the heart. Therefore, one must conclude that they, too, possess the nature of the mind’s rule; it is just that they are punished, such that, of their own accord, they will not act in matters of *Torah u’mitzvos*. Thus, if one arouses them through another power, they do perform their task. b) If we interpret it to mean that they will never come to perform *mitzvos* (without prior *teshuvah*), then there is no place in this chapter for the discussion of *resha'im*, which explains how the matter is **close** to perform. Instead, the text should have first concluded the explanation of the word "very" (*me'od*) in the verse, and only afterwards written that the verse as a whole does not apply to *resha'im*, because it is impossible for *resha'im*, etc.

As it seems from your letter—since you did not explain your words fully—you wish to say, in answering this difficulty according to the second interpretation mentioned above, that the verse "for it is close to you," etc., *does* apply to *resha'im*, and that is why their matter is explained in this chapter; it is just that they arrive at it through the assistance of other powers for the contemplation in their mind.

Now, although I also agree with the second interpretation—as will be explained below—both of your proofs have a refutation:

a) The fact that *resha'im* do not have their heart in their control is a punishment for their sins regarding *Torah u’mitzvos*. Therefore, the fact that they conduct themselves with rational behavior in other matters is irrelevant here, for why would they be punished in matters of business, trade, and the like? And if one were to say that this punishment is natural rather than a specific spiritual consequence—and the language of *Tanya* does not imply this—and is similar to "once he has committed a sin and repeated it, it becomes for him as permitted," seemingly it is obvious that even in business, etc., it would be evident that the mind is not ruling over the heart **in this regard**. For example, one who withholds his hand from giving *tzedakah* and whose contemplation in his mind is of no avail, will certainly also be recognized in his business as one who "loves money, and he who loves money will not be satisfied with money," and the like.

b) The "assistance of other powers" is not mentioned at all in Chapter 17, and according to the above, the **essential point** is missing from the text.

In any case: Based on what is explained here, the verse "for it is close to you," etc., does not apply to *resha'im*, as it states **explicitly**: "And the Torah did not speak of these dead," etc. Nevertheless, the paragraph "unless it is one who is a *rasha*," etc., belongs precisely in Chapter 17. For there, it explains that by nature and birth, the mind rules over the heart—which is necessary for the interpretation of the verse—and based on this, one might raise a difficulty from the words of our Sages, "The *resha'im* are in the control of their heart" (and this is also the conclusion of the Sages' statement, "The *tzaddikim* are in the control of their heart," which he brought at the beginning of Chapter 17), asking how this is possible, as it is the opposite of nature. He explains that this is a punishment, etc. If so, ultimately it is not understood how the verse says "for it is close to you," etc., since the mind is not ruling, even if it is by way of punishment. Therefore, he concludes, "And the Torah did not speak," etc. He reinforces these words, noting that not only is the matter not **close** to the *resha'im*, but furthermore, **it is impossible** for them to begin, etc.

- And in general, it can be said that he first explained everything pertaining to the **general** matter of "for it is close to you," etc., and only afterwards came to add further explanation, etc., as he wrote at the beginning of Chapter 18.

***

It should be noted, as a parenthetical remark, that there is a hint in what he wrote regarding the matter of *resha'im* here: In the verse "For this commandment," etc., "for it is close to you," etc., there are two interpretations. The simple interpretation—as explained in Chapter 17, and as is implied in *Eiruvin* (54a) and *Midrash Rabbah* at the end of *Parshas Nitzavim*—is that it refers to *Torah u’mitzvos*, the service of the entire year. This service is through *ahavah* and *yirah*, and within them are the two modes of *memale* (filling) and *sovev* (encompassing) within the soul: "With all your heart"—the simple *ahavah* that is "close," which is the subject until Chapter 17; and "with all your might"—which, when it is in a state of concealment, is the matter of *ahavas mesiras nefesh*, the "very close" which begins to be explained from Chapter 18 onwards.

Now, *resha'im* have no connection to this service, both in the simple sense that they are transgressors of His will and are worse than the *kelipos*, etc., and also—for it is written, "But to the *rasha* G-d said, 'What right have you...?'" etc. On the contrary, through their *Torah u’mitzvos*, they add strength, at least for the moment, to the *kelipos*, as he rules in *Hilchos Talmud Torah*, Chapter 4, Halacha 6, and see also *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, Chapter 6, and what is explained regarding this in *Kuntres U’Maayan*, Maamar 7. This is what is meant by "And the Torah did not speak of these dead," etc. See *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, Chapter 7, meaning that their lives are drawn from the place of death, which is also the reason why, through *Torah u’mitzvos*, they add strength to the *kelipos*, as written there in Chapter 6.

The second interpretation of the verse "for it is close," etc., is that it refers to the *mitzvah* of *teshuvah*, as written in the *derushim* on this subject in *Likutei Torah*. In this, too, there are two modes of *memale* and *sovev* in the soul: "close" and "very close." It is self-understood that according to this interpretation, it is relevant to *resha'im* as well. The *teshuvah* discussed in Chapter 17 is the *memale* in the soul, "close," while *teshuvah* of *mesiras nefesh* is "very close"—*sovev*, *mesiras nefesh* that is above *da'as*, *ahavas mesiras nefesh*. It is of these levels that he speaks from Chapter 18 onwards, as is understood from all the aforementioned *derushim*.

***

Let us return to the subject of whether *resha'im*—according to the *Tanya’s* definition of the level of *rasha*—can perform *sur me'ra u’aseh tov* in practice.

It is simple that this is so, and the most conclusive proof is from everyday occurrences, many stories, and the words of our Sages.

Now, not only do they perform *Torah u’mitzvos* in matters where their *yetzer* does not stand against them at all, as discussed in Chapter 15 and the end of Chapter 27, but furthermore, **we see clearly** that they perform *Torah u’mitzvos* even in places where they come to a battle with their *yetzer* and require contemplation in their mind and intellect, without having first done *teshuvah* for their previous deeds. And shall we say that one who falls into sin when he comes to a great and mighty battle with the *yetzer hara*—which makes him a complete *rasha*—is liable at that very moment to do **everything** his *yetzer* incites him to do?! In *Tanya* itself, it is also forced that this is not so, from what is written in Chapter 11, Chapter 30, and elsewhere. Also here, on the spot, it is proven, as he emphasizes in his language: "unless it is one who is a *rasha* **in truth**," etc., and this is a punishment for the **"greatness and intensity of their sin,"** etc.

Regarding the meaning of "a *rasha* in truth," it is explained in *Be'ur Tanya* (in manuscript, and noted upon it that it is by the esteemed Rav R. Sh. G., of blessed memory): "Meaning, similar to what is written in Chapter 1, 'And that which we say in general... if half and half, he is called a *beinoni*, so if the majority are sins, he is called a *rasha*.'" This is puzzling, that he would refer to what is written in Chapter 1, for there he writes that it is only a **borrowed** name, etc., but regarding the **truth** of the matter, etc., and from there, "tzaddik" and "beinoni" can be understood for the name "rasha." One cannot say he intends the place where he wrote the **opposite**. It seems to me that it refers to Chapter 14. The word "in truth" comes to exclude what is written there: "At rare times the evil prevails... he is called a *rasha* at that time... and afterwards the good prevails in him," etc. A proof for this is that for the level of these *resha'im*, it is not appropriate to say "the greatness and intensity of their sin." Perhaps it can be said according to what is written at the end of Chapter 13, that "truth" is only called such if it does not pass and vanish (whether in practice or at least in potential; see *Likutei Torah*, *d'h Ki Tavo*, "And even after prayer, a *reshimu* remains," etc.). Also in the realm of *zeh le'umas zeh*, it is so: a *rasha* in truth is one who is "a *rasha* and it is bad for him" (*rasha* in truth—in practice), or also a *rasha* who regrets, but does not have the strength to overcome the evil (*rasha* in truth—in potential). This still requires study.

***

Now, however we interpret the meaning of "a *rasha* in truth," it requires study, for seemingly, from every sin and transgression, a separating screen is made, since they are against the will of the Holy One, blessed be He, and also through this, he receives his vitality from the chambers of *sitra achra*, the place of death. If so, the reasons that he explained here in Chapter 17—that because of this, the Torah did not speak, etc.—apply also to an ordinary *rasha*. Perhaps it can be resolved by what is written at the end of Chapter 24: "And if the sinner... **at the time of the act**... but after the act of the sin... they return and ascend... and draw close to the holiness of the *nefesh elokis*," etc. He did not mention the performance of *teshuvah*. And in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, Chapter 6: "**At the hour and moment** that he does the evil," etc.

What is written in Chapter 27 and the beginning of Chapter 29 is only regarding the ascent of his *Torah u’mitzvos*, but the body and the *nefesh habehamis* ascend of their own accord.

Now, in the *maamar* "Tza'aku v'Hashem shama" (5631) (brought in the aforementioned *Be'ur Tanya*), it is written in the explanation of Chapter 17 that the fact that in *beinonim* the mind rules over the heart is specifically through the introduction of Torah, which is called "peace," for it makes peace between the mind and the heart. This is "in your mouth and then in your heart" (and he does not go into distinguishing there between his heart being **in his control** and the mind **ruling**). It requires study to interpret according to this the words of the Admur HaZaken, who wrote, "And this matter is very close and easy for every person," and immediately explained the reason: "for his mind is in his control," etc., and "when he contemplates it," etc., "it will naturally give birth," etc., and "the mind rules by its nature and birth," etc., "and it is a punishment," etc.

In the *maamarim* "Ki Karov Eilecha" (5678) and "Anochi Anochi" (5699), it is explicitly explained that they also explained Chapter 17, that in general there are three matters here: their heart is in their control, the mind rules, and they are in the control of their heart, and they are at the level of *tzaddik v'rasha*.

He precedes with "in your mouth and then in your heart"—for in *beinonim*, their service is through contemplation of the attainment of G-dliness and the arousal of *ahavah* and *yirah*—it must be study first, for otherwise, with what will he contemplate and with what will he be aroused? (This is written in the *maamar* "Anochi," but in the *maamar* "Ki Karov," it is explained as written in the *maamar* "Tza'aku").

And let it be known that what is written here, that in *beinonim* the mind rules over the heart and "for it is close to you," etc., speaks of the majority of cases. But sometimes, even though he contemplates, he cannot rule over the heart, as written at length in Chapter 27. And there is more to clarify from Chapter 27 regarding the matter of *beinonim*, for what is written in Chapter 12—that the *beinoni* has never committed a sin in his life, etc., and the name *rasha* is not called upon him even for one hour, etc.—means that from the perspective of his **current state**, there is no *reshimu* of a sin in him, etc., and there is no matter in him that would be a cause for him to commit a sin ever.

But even one who has committed a sin can be at the true level of a *beinoni*. And although this does not seem so from the superficial reading, it is clear from his language regarding *beinonim* in Chapter 27: "And especially when he remembers," etc. Through this, what is written in Chapter 14 will also be resolved: "And the level of the *beinoni* is the level of every person," etc., that every person can be a *beinoni* at any time and at any hour. See *HaTamim*, Part 7, page 3 and onwards regarding this, and I overlooked what is written in the aforementioned Chapter 27.

***

There is more to note: In Chapter 17, he explains the level for whom the matter is **close**, "in your mouth," etc., whereas for other levels, the matter is not close to them. But he does not rule out that as an emergency measure and at certain times, there can be a matter of *Torah u’mitzvos* through contemplation and battle with the *yetzer hara* even for a *rasha* in truth. The expression "it is impossible to begin to serve Hashem" implies a matter of order and consistency, not a matter of temporary or emergency measure. (And perhaps it can be said that the performance of *Torah u’mitzvos* by a *rasha* in truth before he has done *teshuvah* does not enter into the category of "serving Hashem" that he writes of here, since, on the contrary, he adds strength to the *kelipah* through this until he does *teshuvah*, etc.)

For the completeness of this letter, I will transcribe here some further notes on this chapter.

**"And the Torah is eternal"**—seemingly, what does this come to teach us? Perhaps it excludes the possibility of answering that although "this commandment," etc., applies also to our generations like all *Torah u’mitzvos*, it is not "too wonderful," etc., "for it is close," etc., is only for the generation that entered the Land and the like, but in the lower generations, the matter is not close. Nevertheless, they were commanded regarding it, as the Sages say in *Eiruvin* (55a) that if it is in heaven, you must ascend after it, etc. See the end of Chapter 25, and with this it will be understood, etc.

**"To love Hashem, etc.—is fear a small thing, and all the more so love?"**—Seemingly, since in the verse it is not written except "in your heart," perhaps it refers to fear, which also has its dwelling in the heart. See also *Likutei Torah*, *Ha'azinu*, 3, 1. In any case, the force of the difficulty "and all the more so love" is removed. And it is even more difficult according to what is written below, that "to perform it" means the love that brings, etc., and when he contemplates... he will give birth to the love... and this is the whole man, "for today to perform them," etc. And in *Perek Mem-Beis* it is written: "And every person of Israel, whoever he may be, when he contemplates," etc., the fear will be fixed **in his heart** for the entire day, etc., the fear that brings to the performance of His commandments, blessed be He, in *sur me'ra u’aseh tov*. And in the end of *Perek Mem-Gimmel*: "The order of the established service, which depends on the choice of man, must be first the performance of *Torah u’mitzvos* through *yiras Hashem*, etc., and afterwards the light of love will shine upon it." See also *Kuntres HaAvodah*, 3, how the performance of *Torah u’mitzvos* in *sur me'ra u’aseh tov* depends on fear. It is understood that although one must also arouse the love of Hashem, etc., as written in *Perek Mem-Alef*, nevertheless, the aforementioned difficulty remains in its place.

**"And this matter is very close and easy for every person," etc.**—See *Perek Mem-Beis*, where he writes that the soul requires great and mighty labor, doubled and redoubled, etc., and one must contemplate this for a large hour every day, etc., and only then is it in the power of every person to come to *yiras Hashem*. If so, all the more so for love, which requires all the aforementioned, and here he wrote that it is very close and easy for everyone. This requires study.

**"The matter of the mind ruling over the heart."**—The reason for this in the physical sense is mentioned above, "And even the heart receives from the mind, and therefore the mind rules over it by its birth."

The matter of this rule in service—*iskafya*. As explained in the *derushim* that explain the *kelipah* of Amalek: *Torah Or*, *d'h Zachor*, and elsewhere.

This rule is only over the externality of the heart and not over the internality of the heart; see *Likutei Torah*, *d'h V'Hayah Bayom HaHu*, 3.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah*, immediate *geulah*,

**M. Schneerson**

## 55

55

B"H, Sunday, 1st day of Rosh Chodesh Adar II, 5703

To the honored and distinguished, G-d-fearing, man of many talents, etc.,
R. Meir Zalman, may he live and be well, Dr. Muscat,
P.O.B. 176, Marietta, Ohio.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Tuesday of last week, it is surprising that you have directed a claim toward us, as we have never received from you either a letter or subscription fees. I request that you send all correspondence intended for us to our address. Your request will certainly be fulfilled precisely.

The booklets you have now received are booklets that we are sending as **samples**, and it was surprising to us that we have not received a response from you during all this time.

We are now happy to include you, may he live and be well, in the list of subscribers, and you will receive the new booklets regularly, G-d willing. You will surely send the subscription fees, and also endeavor to acquire more readers for them. You, may he live and be well, have surely recognized their great value, and it is appropriate to make the "Shmuessen" and the "Talks" "members of the household" in every Jewish home.

From the pamphlet enclosed herewith, you, may he live and be well, will see the magnitude of the work being done by Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, which stands under the presidency of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, in the field of education, and the various printed materials that have been published. We are also sending you samples of the printed materials that have appeared recently. Surely in your area, too, there is room for the distribution of these printed materials and for the improvement of the state of education in general. In particular, we wish to draw your attention to the matter of "Misibos Shabbos" (a report regarding the work of the "Misibos" in particular is being sent to you), and perhaps you, may he live and be well, would be willing to organize "Misibos Shabbos" in your area.

Having heard of your good reputation, we are confident that you, may he live and be well, will interest yourself with all your heart in the work of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, and we will be happy to hear from you soon regarding what is being done in your area for the sake of Torah-true education.

At the time when Haman arose and sought to destroy, kill, etc., Mordechai, in addition to asking Esther to plead before Achashverosh, gathered—as the Sages relate (Midrash Rabbah, Esther, at the end)—the children of Israel and taught them Torah, specifically the laws pertaining to the time when the Beis Hamikdash will be rebuilt. According to the language of our Sages, through this, Haman’s decree was nullified.

This is to say that in a time of "trouble for Jacob," one of the foundations of the salvation of the entire Jewish people is the education of Jewish boys and girls in the spirit of Torah and Yiddishkeit, and the rooting of the hope of the Geulah—without despair, Heaven forbid—speedily in our days through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, in their hearts. And then "it was turned about," that the Jews ruled over those who hated them, and "the Jews had light and gladness, and joy and honor."

In the hope of hearing from you soon, and with the blessing of "Immediately to Teshuvah, immediately to Geulah."

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 56

56

B"H, 1 Adar II, 5703
Brooklyn

Highly esteemed President, Mrs. B. Shifrin,
And distinguished members of the Zembiner Gemilas Chesed
Ladies Auxiliary,

Shalom u’vrachah!

With great thanks, we acknowledge receipt of your contribution in the sum of $10.00 for the benefit of the Bais Rivkah girls' school on Chester Street, which is one of a series of girls' schools founded by Merkos L’Inyonei Chinuch.

We hope that this is not a one-time or incidental act of assistance, but rather the beginning of a permanent interest and partnership in the important and holy work of the Bais Rivkah school—an institution dedicated to the faithful, Jewish education of Jewish daughters.

Highly esteemed women! In this difficult time for our people, the Jewish nation, we must remember what occurred in the days of the first Haman, who rose up against the Jews.

Those who brought about Haman’s downfall then, with the help of the Ribono shel Olam, were a woman and a man: Esther and Mordechai.

Esther did not look at the fact that she was comfortable and not in danger; rather, she risked her life to save her brothers and sisters.

However, before going to cry out against Haman’s decree, she said to Mordechai: "Lech kenos es kol haYehudim" — "Go, gather all the Jews," so that they might engage in tefillah.

Our Sages tell us that Mordechai gathered tens of thousands of Jewish children and taught them Torah.

In this current time of distress, when another great Haman has arisen, this Haman will also surely have a bitter end, and for the Jews there will be light and joy. But each one of us must work so that this comes about as quickly as possible.

Every Jewish woman must come forward with the slogan: "Lech kenos! Gather together Jewish children and youth! Raise them in a spirit of mesiras nefesh for Yiddishkeit and Torah! We women will, B"H, ensure that the resources to maintain these institutions are not lacking! But let our sons and daughters be Jews—faithful, Torah-observant Jews!"

Through such determination, the downfall of the Hamans of all times comes about very quickly.

Highly esteemed women! Ensure that your daughters also follow in your footsteps by receiving the proper, Torah-true education in the appropriate educational institutions. Ensure that these institutions have the ability to exist and to increase the number of their students, so that no Jewish daughter is left on the outside. In the Bais Rivkah schools, Jewish daughters are raised to be proud, Torah-observant sisters and women—the mothers of the coming generation. Therefore, by helping the Bais Rivkah schools, you are helping to secure our youth, our future. And in this merit, we will be privileged to see the downfall of the current Haman very soon, and to experience true light and joy.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**On behalf of Rabbi Menachem**

**Schneerson**

Chairman of the Executive Committee

**N. Mindel, Secretary**

57

B"H, Monday, Rosh Chodesh Adar Sheni, 5705
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter regarding the matter of Moshe Rabbeinu’s name not being mentioned in Parshas Tetzaveh—and as an **addition** to the printed response—I hereby offer a general overview of the subject, which will naturally resolve the difficulties raised in the sefarim regarding the Baal HaTurim, as well as the point you raised in your letter.

The Baal HaTurim writes at the beginning of Parshas Tetzaveh: "Moshe is not mentioned in this *sedra*, unlike the rest of the Chumash, where from the moment Moshe was born, there is no *sedra* in which he is not mentioned. The reason is because he said, 'Erase me, I pray, from Your book which You have written,' and a curse of a wise man, even if conditional, comes to pass, and this was fulfilled here."

Now, it has been asked against the Baal HaTurim that in the *sedaros* Eikev, Re'eh, and Shoftim—and one must **add** to them Ki Seitzei and Nitzavim—Moshe Rabbeinu’s name is also not mentioned. One could answer simply that the book of Devarim begins with, "These are the words that Moshe spoke," and this applies to the **entire** book. See Megillah (31a), Rashi s.v. *Moshe*: "(In Toras Kohanim) it is stated with the language of 'I will give,' 'I will appoint,' and 'I will send'—one who has the power to act. But in Mishneh Torah, it is written, 'Hashem will strike you,' etc." And in the Ramban on the Torah at the beginning: "Moshe Rabbeinu wrote... as a messenger of the Speaker... and because the matter is so, Moshe is not mentioned in the Torah until he was born... And do not let the matter of Mishneh Torah be difficult for you... for the beginning of that book is, 'These are the words that Moshe spoke'... as a count of words in the language of their saying." See also Likutei Torah, s.v. *Asur L’adam Sheyit'am*, section 2, and the end of section 2 of *Va'eschanan*.

One may add further to the question of the Baal HaTurim: The term "erasure" (*mechiyah*) applies to something that has been written (which already exists in reality), as per the change in the language of the verse (Tehillim 69:29), "Let them be erased... let them not be written." See Rosh Hashanah (16b). Moreover, we find that even the **mode** of existence is relevant, as per the ruling (Rambam, Hilchos Shabbos 11:15): "One who erases is not liable unless he erases writing that stands upon something that stands." It is difficult to reconcile this with the ruling (ibid., 11:5) that one who erases the letter *Aleph* in order to write a *Beis* is liable—

—Unless, because Above there is no lack of potential for action, perhaps one could say that "erasure"—by the Hand of Heaven—applies even to something that has not yet been written, but is at least destined to be written.

From this answer, the question is understood: the reason it is not mentioned there is not because Moshe’s name *must* be mentioned there (even though the language of the Baal HaTurim is difficult according to this), which is why there is no difficulty regarding Bereishis, and likewise no difficulty regarding the other *sedaros*—aside from the aforementioned reason—but also because there is no **necessity** for Moshe’s name to be mentioned there. However, in Parshas Tetzaveh—even though its beginning comes in one continuation with "Hashem spoke to Moshe" from the beginning of Parshas Terumah, its end, "And you shall make an altar for burning incense," etc., is a separate matter. Initially, the vessels of the Mishkan and the priestly garments were explained, all of which were ready by the 25th of Kislev or Rosh Chodesh Adar (as stated in Tanchuma, end of Parshas Pekudei, and Yalkut Shimoni, Melachim 6). Afterward came the Parshah of the *Miluim* (investiture), whose subject matter is at the end of the month of Adar, and then He returned and commanded regarding the incense altar, which was made together with the other vessels of the Mishkan! If so, seemingly there should have been a separate speech for this. The practical difference between a separate speech and a continuation of the previous speech, even with an interruption in between, is that there must be a "calling" (*keriah*) preceding it, as stated in Sifra at the beginning of Parshas Vayikra (that by way of comparison, one can learn that even for the speeches that preceded the Tent of Meeting, there was a calling preceding the speech)—similar to Shemos (33:19-21), "And He said... and He said... and He said," because they are three distinct matters.

To this comes the resolution that this is the fulfillment of what he said, "Erase me, I pray," etc., and therefore the speech was not written, or because of this the speech was not designated [as a separate speech]. This still requires further study.

There are those who say that Parshas Tetzaveh was stated before the incident of the Golden Calf (Zohar Vol. III, 195a; and in Ramban and Ibn Ezra at the beginning of Parshas Terumah it also implies this), and if so, the erasure was of something that was in actuality. Others say it was stated after the incident of the Golden Calf (Tanchuma, Terumah 8; Rashi, Shemos 31:18), and if so, the "Erase me" was regarding something that needed to be written, even though it was still only in potential.

**Notes:**
1) Regarding the fact that the incense altar is mentioned at the end, the commentators on the Torah have already addressed this (see Ramban and Sforno ad loc.). According to *Chassidus*, it may be said that the incense altar represents the inwardness of the heart (*"And you shall draw water"*), which is higher even than the *mochin* (intellect), even though it is found in the body—the sanctuary of the Mishkan and the Beis Hamikdash—and not in the head—the Holy of Holies of the Mishkan and the Beis Hamikdash—and the *avodah* in this is the *yechidah* in the soul. It is not of the same nature as the other matters of the Sanctuary—and especially according to what is written in the *maamar* s.v. *Mizbe'ach Adamah*—notes on the book of Shemos, apparently by the Tzemach Tzedek—and in the *maamar* s.v. *Zeh Yitnu* (5658), that the earthen altar and stones are the external aspects of the heart and the illumination of the inwardness of the heart, while the incense altar is the essential inwardness of the heart, not merely the illumination of the point—as is explained regarding their nature in Likutei Torah, s.v. *Ki Seitzei* (the second), sections 2-3.

2) When was Parshas Terumah and Tetzaveh stated? Seemingly, it is a dispute in Zevachim (115b). Rabbi Yehuda ben Lakish says this is the Parshah of the Firstborns, and if so, the Parshah of the Mishkan, in which it is stated, "And you, bring near to yourself Aharon your brother," etc., was stated after the incident of the Golden Calf. Thus, one must say that in this there is no "earlier or later" (chronological order), and Rabbi [Yehuda HaNasi], who says this is the Parshah of the *Nesiyim* (princes), must say that the *parshiyos* were not written in their chronological order. Moreover, we have heard the opinion of the Zohar (Vol. II, 224a) that even Parshas Vayakhel and the bringing of the donations for the Mishkan were before the incident of the Golden Calf, and this is difficult because of what is written there (195a), "Afterward... immediately, 'And Vayakhel...'," and the commentaries on the Zohar are not before me.

3) To explain the reason that "Erase me" was fulfilled specifically in Parshas Tetzaveh because the 7th of Adar **always** falls in this week, as per the language of your letter, is impossible, for this is not the case. This year will prove it. It could be said that it is because **usually** it will be so.

Alternatively, it may be because in this Parshah alone is Moshe hinted at at its very beginning, to teach that the erasure is only because of the error that emerged, etc.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*.

## 58

B"H, Tuesday, 2 Adar II, 5705
Brooklyn

To the distinguished and honored, who engages in the work of Hashem, [name omitted], may he live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from last week regarding your explanation to your students of the verse in *Bereishis* (41:40), *v’al picha yishak kol ami* ("and at your word shall all my people be ruled"), interpreting *yishak* as derived from the word for "kissing" (*neshikah*), and citing in support the commentary of *Bereishis Rabbah*, *Ibn Ezra*, and *Baal HaTurim*. Your reasoning is that one should not confuse the mind of a beginning student with a new interpretation when a word can be explained according to the student’s initial understanding. There are those who object to this, since *Rashi* explains *yishak* as "shall be sustained," from the term *ben meshek beiti* ("the steward of my house"). You did not clarify in your letter the reason for the objectors' stance, but it appears to be because *Rashi* interprets it differently.

In my opinion, it is clear that this is not a sufficient reason at all, as it touches only upon the *peshuto shel mikra* (the literal meaning of the verse) and is not a matter of *halacha*. *Rashi* himself wrote his perspective on this. For example, in *Bereishis* (33:20), and the words of Torah are "like a hammer that shatters the rock," dividing into many meanings. His grandson, the *Rashbam*, testified to this in his commentary on *Bereishis* (37:2): "And also my mother’s father, our teacher Shlomo... admitted to me that if he had had the time, he would have needed to compose other commentaries according to the literal meanings that are renewed every day." There is no need to elaborate on such a simple matter. All of this concerns the question of whether one may choose the commentary of *Ibn Ezra* or the like in a place where *Rashi* interprets it differently.

However, regarding the explanation of the literal meaning of the verse *v’al picha yishak kol ami*, it is worth examining.

For *Targum Onkelos*, *Targum Yerushalmi*, and *Rashi* all explain *yishak* as "shall be sustained."

The *Targum*—as the *Aruch* understood it in the entry *neshek*—the *Ibn Ezra* (who notes that the interpretation of "kissing" is a far-fetched one, even though he cites *Tehillim* 2:12 regarding the custom of kissing the king, and see *Bereishis Rabbah* ch. 70 regarding a "kiss of greatness"), the *Rashbam*, and the *Radak’s Sefer HaShorashim* all explain it from the term *neshek* (armaments/supplying). All of these are the leading **literalists** of the *Mikra*. As for the term "kissing," I have not found it thus far except in *Bereishis Rabbah* and the *Zohar* (Vol. I, 196a). It is understood that both the *Midrash Rabbah* and the *Zohar* are interpreting it also by way of *remez* and *drush*. Likewise, what the *Baal HaTurim* wrote is to explain the *remez* of the *Masorah*, that the word *yishak* appears twice in the *Tanach*, and it is not a necessity that their meaning be identical in both places. An example in this *sedra*: later (43:34) regarding the word *mas'as*, where the *Baal HaTurim* cites the *Masorah*: "Two in the *Masorah*: *vayisa mas'as* (and he took portions), and *mas'as shav umiduchim* (a burden of vanity and incitement)," even though here the meaning of *mas'as* is a portion or gift, and in *Eichah* it is a prophecy.

Now, as to why they objected, as mentioned above, to the interpretation of *yishak* as "kissing," it seems to me that it is because then the verse must be explained in one of two ways: 1) *Al picha*—at your command—*yishak*—for me, for Pharaoh—*kol ami* (all my people), and as written in *Matnos Kehunah* in the commentary on *Bereishis Rabbah* 91. According to this, the verse is elliptical, missing the word "for me." 2) *Al picha*—you—*yishak* (shall kiss) *kol ami* (all my people). But the expression **"al"** (upon/at) is not found in the text, only *vayishak lo* (and he kissed him)—and in *Iyov* (31:27), *vatishak yadi lefi* (and my hand kissed my mouth)—even though it is found in the language of the Sages in *Mishnah Rosh Hashanah* 2:7, "and they kissed him on his head," and in the *Baraita*, "they kiss upon the hand" (*Berachos* 8b).

Therefore, in my opinion, one should explain *v’al picha yishak kol ami* either from the term *meshek* as *Rashi* does, or at the very least from the term *neshek*, even though it is not found elsewhere without the *nun*. And one should explain to the students that only a small remnant of our language remains in the books of the *Tanach*—and in the language of the *Rambam* in his introduction to *Sefer HaMitzvos*, "the language of the books of prophecy... is sparse in our hands"—and therefore many words and expressions are found in them only once.

Surely it is known to you that starting from *Rav Saadia Gaon*, they enumerated his book and occupied themselves with the interpretation of individual words found in the Holy Scriptures. See the bibliography in *Otzar Yisrael*, Vol. 2, entry *Bodedos*.

With the blessing of "immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to *Geulah*,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

We hope that we will have a few *Luchos* (tablets/calendars) with us these days, and then we will send you the twenty to the address you indicated.

In the *Peshitta* (Syriac translation), the verse is translated: "And at the word of your mouth, all the people shall receive judgment." Similarly, in the *Septuagint* and the *Vulgate*, they translated it as "shall obey."

If so, this explains the **intent** of the matter and is not a precise translation of the word, but this too is closer to the interpretation of the term *meshek* or *neshek* than "kissing," for according to the latter, it is a matter of honor and not of obeying his command. *Noach*

## 59

[3 Adar Sheni, 5703]

To the esteemed... [Name], may he be a light unto the Jewish people,

Allow me to approach you with the following request:

There is a bochur currently serving in the army in Washington by the name of... The father of this bochur is a G-d-fearing man, and the bochur himself is soft-hearted and receptive to positive influence. He also has a little free time each day from his duties. It is possible, with the help of Hashem, to influence him to put on tefillin and to eat kosher food, even at his place of service.

The aforementioned bochur will be visiting you, and I therefore ask that you draw him close, both physically and spiritually, and also inform us regarding the results of your influence. Many thanks in advance.

And while we are speaking regarding an individual soldier, perhaps it is within your ability to speak with other people whose hearts have been touched by the fear of Hashem, and to establish a committee to provide kosher food for the Jewish soldiers located in your city. In several large cities, such committees have already been established, and with the help of Hashem, they have succeeded in saving many of the children of Israel from eating non-kosher food.

It is understood that we stand ready to assist you, with the help of Hashem, to the extent possible.

To conclude with a matter related to the weekly parsha, I will transcribe a question that occurred to me these days. There are two opinions regarding when the parsha of Terumah and Tetzaveh was stated: whether it was before the incident of the Golden Calf (Zohar Vol. III, 195a) or after it (Tanchuma, Parshas Terumah, and Rashi). This is like the dispute between Rabbi Yehuda ben Lakish and Rabbi in Zevachim (115b). However, in Zohar (Vol. III, 224a), it is implied that even the bringing of the donations for the Mishkan was before the incident of the Golden Calf, and this requires further study.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 60

[4 Adar Rishon 5703]

For your Bar Mitzvah celebration, I send you my blessings: that on this day, when you have become a *gadol*, you may go from strength to strength in your studies and your conduct, and that your parents and grandparents—may they live—may derive much *nachas* and *oneg* from you.

In the days of **Mordechai**, when the Jewish people were in exile, Haman the Agagite sought to destroy all the Jews. What did Mordechai do? He gathered the youth of Israel and taught them Torah, and through this, the decree was nullified.

When the Jewish people were upon their own land, with every man under his vine, **Ephraim and Judah** as one nation in the land, and Shlomo ben David as their king at their head, and he built a House for Hashem—our Sages decreed that students should not be interrupted from their Torah study even for the building of the *Beis Hamikdash*!

For the Torah is a tree of life to those who hold fast to it. Through the power of the Torah of Moshe, which he commanded at Chorev to all Israel—statutes and ordinances—and through the observance of its *mitzvos*, we will stand firm against all who rise against us in exile. And we will soon merit the great day of Hashem, which will turn the hearts of the fathers to the children and the hearts of the children to their fathers, and He will redeem us through Moshiach **Menachem**, who restores our soul.

Be strong and courageous in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of *mitzvos*!

***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 21, p. 4.

**For your Bar Mitzvah celebration:** See also Letter 151 below.

## 61

[Friday, 5th of Adar II, 5703]

Our very dear friend, the esteemed Rabbi Moshe Yitzchak Hecht, has shared with us with great enthusiasm the news of your decision to put on tefillin every weekday.

From the depths of our heart, and with a feeling of ahavas Yisrael, we greet you on this most important step.

A head upon which tefillin are placed thinks like a Yid; the heart near which tefillin rest feels like a Yiddishe heart; and a hand that is bound by tefillin is far from evil deeds, and instead performs only good deeds.

Torah and mitzvos are our life. Your putting on tefillin is a blessing for you and for your family; it is a benefit for our entire people and a protection for the land in which we find ourselves.

Mitzvah goreres mitzvah—from one mitzvah, one arrives at another, and so on.

We wish you that you should grow more and more, spiritually, and that you should be healthy and successful materially as well.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

62

B"H, 9 Adar Sheni, 5703

To the esteemed Rabinowitz family, may they live:
Boston

Peace and blessing!

I wish to express my deepest condolences on your great loss—the passing of your father and husband, the esteemed Chassid, famous for his praise, our friend, a G-d-fearing man, R' Dovid Meir, of blessed memory.

We had in him a personal, devoted friend to all the institutions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, and his memory will remain deeply etched in everyone’s hearts.

May the Omnipresent comfort you among the [other] mourners of Zion and Jerusalem.

Esteemed Rabinowitz family:

Since there is currently a great shortage of Tanya copies, and we are faced with the urgent necessity of reprinting the Tanya in the immediate future, I would like to propose that you establish a fund in the name of your late father and husband to sponsor the printing of the Tanya in memory of the soul of the late Rabbi, R' Dovid Meir, of blessed memory.

I do not need to explain to you the importance of this matter and the great *nachas ruach* that you will thereby provide for the soul of the great departed. Our friend, the esteemed Chassid, a G-d-fearing man, R' Yisroel, may he live, Jacobson, will personally provide you with further details, and I hope that you will give this matter your serious consideration.

With blessings for long life and years, and may Hashem wipe away tears from off all faces.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

**Loss... R' Dovid Meir:** On 2 Adar Sheni.

63

B"H, Wednesday, 10th of Adar Sheni, 5705
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Honorable Rabbi, the renowned Chassid, scholar of good things, scion of noble lineage, etc., our teacher Rabbi Yehuda Leib Shlita Eliezarov, Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letters to Machne Israel and regarding the Sefer Torah for the welcoming of Moshiach, along with the lists of participants in the Mishnayos Baal Peh society and the Sefer Torah:

1) The intention in founding the Mishnayos Baal Peh society was not that only yeshiva students should learn Mishnayos by heart, but that it should encompass **all** of the House of Israel. We must conduct a campaign so that **everyone** capable will participate in this society by learning their portion by heart—which amounts to about three to five chapters a year (approximately one Mishnah a week)—and review what they already know while walking **outside**, standing in their shop, sitting on the train, or at any other opportunity. This is to purify the atmosphere. Surely, you have already received the collection of letters from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe Shlita, and you should see his sicha regarding this.

We are confident that if you organize your campaign according to the above, you will find hundreds of people, including businessmen (who are the primary ones for the work of "finding you outside"), and it is also known from the virtues of businessmen explained in Chassidus—some of the sources are noted in the *Biur* to the *Maamar* "Mayim Rabim" in *Likutei Torah* for Gimmel Parshiyos—who will participate in the society. It should be noted that it has been decided that the *siyum* will be shared by all members and will take place on the day after Shavuos 5705, G-d willing.

2) You are correct that in order to expand the work of "Machne Israel" in our Holy Land, it is necessary and required that someone travel to all the settlements, etc. However, to our regret, we do not yet see a way to take such expenses upon ourselves. Surely, with proper searching, you will be able to find in every city and settlement local residents who will occupy themselves with all the matters of Machne Israel and the *Kupat Rabbeinu* (Keren Pikuach Nefesh), and they themselves will be the representatives of the *Machane* on the spot.

3) We have received the receipts from the Global Tehillim Society, but it is impossible to give them to the donors because the name of the *Kollel* is also mentioned there. Surely it is known to your honor that here, extreme caution is required in all matters involving money so that there is no room for even the slightest criticism. Therefore, I ask that you please print receipts for the *Chevra Tehillim* **separately** and send them to us as soon as possible.

4) Enclosed is a list of members of the *Chevra Tehillim*. It would be appropriate to create a sort of certificate—on thin paper—for each of the Tehillim groups registered here, and send them to us after they have been signed, of course, and we will deliver them here to their owners.

5) Everything published regarding the affairs of the *Machane* and the *Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch* is sent from here to there from time to time, and it surely arrives in due course.

To conclude with a matter of Torah and regarding the above: Seemingly, one can bring further proof for the relevance of purifying the atmosphere specifically to businessmen. The concept of "atmosphere" in avodah and in the human soul is explained in many places in Chassidus, including *Torah Or*, *Yud*, *Maamar* "Nach Mitzvah L'haniha," that it is the matter of the letters—the "inanimate" (domem)—relative to the intellect, and *mitzvos* relative to Torah. It is understood that "bad atmosphere" (which is much worse even than the "dense atmosphere" mentioned in *Likutei Torah*, *Maamar* "Al Kein Yomru HaMoshelim," Chapter 3; see also the *Maamar* "Hasket V'shma Yisrael," 5733—though it seems there it does not distinguish between dense and bad; regarding "bad atmosphere," note *Nazir* 54b, "the atmosphere of the lands of the nations," *Sanhedrin* 109a, "the atmosphere of Migdal") is the "inanimate" letters, the work of the *Sitra Achra*. One must purify the atmosphere through *ketores* (incense), which is to remove a bad odor, as written in the *Maamar* "Se'ir Izim," 5704 (see *Moreh Nevuchim*, Part 3, Chapter 46, on the reason for the mitzvah of *ketores* being to remove bad odor; and in *Zohar*, Vol. 3, 210a and b, that *ketores* is to remove the *zohama*—though it is a difficult question that in the *Zohar* and in the *Maamar* "Se'ir Izim" it refers to the *ketores* before *davening*, and see *Shaar HaKollel*, Chapter 3, Section 12, but in *Torah Or* and *Ohr HaTorah* below, it also refers to the *ketores* after the *Tamid*). This refers to practical *mitzvos* in general, as explained in the *Chanukah* discourses, *Maamar* "Koh B'Kislev," and noted in *Ohr HaTorah*—which is the level of businessmen. Specifically, it can be said that this is the speech of the letters in Torah, in which there are the two virtues: of Torah and also of *mitzvos*. This is unlike practical *mitzvos*, which require guarding, as written in *Likutei Torah*, *Maamar* "V'zos HaMitzvah" and *Maamar* "Acharei Hashem," and its *Biur*, and there in the *Maamar* "Lema'an Tira," "guard this, this is the Mishnah, etc." And in this aspect, in Torah, it is the breath of speech that the Mishnah speaks, etc. And "breath produces breath."

In a deeper sense, perhaps it can be said that the purification of the atmosphere is only a matter of preparation for the complete Redemption (and it is also known that the "ingathering of the exiles," which are only gathered in the merit of the Mishnayos, still have a number, but there will be the generation of Moshiach and the World to Come, which have no number), as explained at length in the *Maamar* "Ve'eleh Shemos" by the Mitteler Rebbe. It can also be understood through the above: the letters of Torah are called "horses," and "the horse upon which the King rode," and the acceptance of the Torah in the days of Achashverosh (*Shabbos* 88b). Thus, through the preparation of the "horses," we will merit, speedily in our days, the fulfillment of "and be like a gazelle or a young hart," and "Achashverosh" merited "I will hasten it," as explained in the additions to *Torah Or*.

With the blessing of "Immediately to Teshuvah, Immediately to Redemption,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 64

By the Grace of Hashem, Thursday, the day the Megillah is read, 11 Adar II, 5705

To our dear friend, the eminent Torah scholar and Chassid, a man of valor in the army of Torah, the Temimim, may they live, and among them R’ Moshe Eliyahu, may he live, Montreal, Canada.

Peace and Blessing!

I will begin by asking forgiveness for not replying **in writing** to your letter until now. The reason for this is the great preoccupation with arranging the *Luach* for Chassidim of Chabad, which is being published these days. As for a verbal response, our friend, the eminent Torah scholar and Chassid, etc., R’ Shmuel Levitin, surely delivered it in its proper time, and the telegram was certainly received on time as well. I am writing now to atone—in the manner of a gesture of goodwill and a gift—for the above, and so that this may also serve as a sort of *farbrengen* for the days of Purim that are approaching.

The Mishnah states: "The Megillah is read on the 11th, 12th, 13th, 14th, or 15th, etc.," as the villagers advance the reading to the day of assembly. In terms of *avodah* according to *Chassidus*—and see the explanation of this entire Mishnah in *Magid Meisharim* by the Beis Yosef, Parshas Vayeikel—the matter is as follows:

The Megillah’s subject is the story of the miracle, a conduct that is above nature. However, the miracle of Purim was "clothed" in nature. The distinction is explained in the *maamarim* of Purim, *Biurei HaZohar* on *Vayikra*, and *Podeh B’Shalom* (5688). In *avodah*, the distinction can be categorized as follows: *avodah* that is according to *taam v’daas* (nature); *avodah* that begins above *taam v’daas* through the intensity of the *ratzon*, but in matters that are subsequently drawn down into *taam v’daas* because the *ratzon* compels the intellect (a miracle clothed in nature); and *avodah* that is entirely above *taam v’daas* (an open miracle). See the *maamar* entitled *Ve’atah Im Na* in *Parshas Ki Sisa* (5678), which explains that even within miracles that are above nature, there are levels. One may note the expression of our Sages: "A miracle and miracles of miracles" (*Berachos* 57a), "a miracle within a miracle" (*Shemos Rabbah*, end of *Va’eira*), "when Aharon performs miracles through him," "that I—Moshe—performed miracles through him," and "that the Holy One, Blessed be He, performs miracles" (*Shemos Rabbah*, end of *Beshalach*). One could say the distinction is the conduct of *chayah* and *yechidah*, or the *mesiras nefesh* of Avraham and Rabbi Akiva.

Reading the Megillah is *pirsumei nisa* (publicizing the miracle) in the world, drawing this conduct into daily life. This conduct of *kabbalas ol* (accepting the yoke), without considering *taam v’daas*, can exist on five levels: if it concerns only the actual deed (*poel mamash*), or also regarding the emotions (*midos*), intellect, assumptions, and one’s primary concepts, the essence of the *ratzon* and the *nefesh*. These are the four letters of the Name *Havayah* in the *nefesh* and the *kotzo shel yud*. It is known that regarding the Names, "nature" and "miracle" correspond to the Name *Elokim* and the Name *Havayah*.

This is the meaning of "The Megillah is read on the 11th... until the 15th." For ten days—ten *tefachim*—downward, in physical *asiyah*, the *Shechinah* did not descend below ten (*Sukkah* 5a), and the *Reshus* is only up to ten (*Shabbos* 7b). The reading of the Megillah, which is a miracle and not nature, begins from the 11th.

A place that has ten *batlanim*—all ten powers of the soul—who are "idle" from their work, meaning they are always found in the *beis medrash* for *tefillah* (see *Megillah* 5a and the Rambam’s commentary there), a connection with the Holy One, Blessed be He, is called a "city" ("Great is Hashem in the city of our G-d"). They read on the 14th, meaning that the drawing down of this miraculous conduct is in all four of the aforementioned levels, since they are all as they should be. But they do not read on the 15th, because one must be wary of the enemy, since regarding the essence of the *nefesh*, the *kotzo shel yud*, one does not know which way one is being led (*Likkutei Torah*, *Kitzur D’Lo Sashbit*, *Tefillin* of *Mitzvas Aseh* 253). This is unlike a "walled city," where the *makif* (encompassing light) is also complete for him—they read on the 15th, the *kotzo shel yud*.

(The *maamarim* of the *Tzemach Tzedek*, *Megillah*, Vol. II, p. 322, state: "The Megillah is read from the 11th until the 15th, which is the revelation of the Name *Havayah*, etc. In the Name *Havayah* of four letters, the *yud* shines on the 14th, but on the 15th, in cities surrounded by a wall and in Shushan, the *kotzo shel yud* also shines," end quote.)

However, when there are no ten *batlanim*, and according to what we have explained, his *avodah* has a hold in *taam v’daas* (nature) and he is not a permanent resident of the "city of our G-d." Therefore, he requires a "city dweller" to read the Megillah for him—to draw down miraculous conduct into the life of his soul. The reading can take place on the 11th, so that he is influenced to have his *avodah* regarding the actual deed be above *taam v’daas*, or on the 12th, also in his *midos*, etc. This depends on when the "day of assembly" falls, when they gather in the towns for judgment, for the ascent from the level of a "villager" to the level of a "city dweller"—even if only for a time—must come through judgment and additional refinement beforehand.

The Gemara explains how it is possible for a city dweller to read for—and draw down into—the villagers. What connection is there between them? As is known, the vast difference in value between *Atzilus* and *Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah*, or between the *chochmah* of the soul and the other powers. The Gemara answers (*Megillah* 4b) that they supply water and food to their brethren in the towns, meaning that by refining and preparing physical matters so that they are on the level of the city dwellers (and the levels of this are explained: Canaanite slave, *eved ivri*, *amah ivriyah*—*Sefer HaMitzvos*, *Mitzvas Ye'ud*), they become "their brethren"—a term of *ichui* (binding/joining)—and consequently, the city dweller reads the Megillah before them.

The final ruling (*ibid.* 2a) is: When does this law of villagers apply? "At a time when the years are in their proper order," etc. This can be understood along the lines of what is explained in the *maamarim* of Rosh Hashanah in *Chassidus* regarding *Teki'as Shofar* and taking the *Lulav* on *Shabbos* in the *Beis HaMikdash* versus the provinces. This is because "they look at it"—also regarding the prohibition of *chametz*, and the possibility that they might stumble by eating *chametz* on *Pesach*. In *avodah*, for such a simple level, they were obligated to read on the 14th as well—to draw it down into their entire stature.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *Geulah*.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

## 65

B"H, Thursday, 11 Adar II, 5705

To our dear friend, the outstanding avreich, G-d-fearing and distinguished, the Tmimim, Rabbi M.Z. (may he live and be well),

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters, please accept my apologies for the delay, which was caused by my preoccupation with arranging the calendar for Chabad Chassidim that is being published these days.

1) We wrote to you some time ago regarding the founding of "Beis Rivkah," and it is a great wonder that you pass over this entire matter in silence. From our friend, the distinguished Rabbi R.S.L. (may he live and be well), we also have not heard a sufficient reason for delaying the matter for so long. Every day that passes is an irretrievable loss. How many girls and young women could have been helped in the meantime—regarding themselves, by becoming observant of Torah and mitzvos, and regarding their influence on others, by becoming a model and symbol through the change in their conduct brought about by the proper education in Beis Rivkah. Especially according to what is explained in Chassidus, even if through this education a single girl were to perform one additional mitzvah during this entire time beyond what she was accustomed to, through this she would be united in absolute unity with the Ribono shel Olam. This unity above is eternal, forever and ever. Although one must understand how this is so, the Alter Rebbe testifies that it is indeed so, and it is also a known halachic ruling that a person should see himself and the entire world as balanced, and through one mitzvah, etc. (Rambam, Hilchos Teshuvah 3:4). So, for when are we putting this off? It is not, G-d forbid, that I wish to offer rebuke or words of admonition, but your attitude toward this entire matter is a wonder to me. I am writing this in my letter to you, as you were the one who responded to this question on behalf of all the Tmimim.

2) Please be so kind as to inform us what the final outcome was regarding the bochur... Munkover. Regarding this, too, one must note the same as mentioned above in question 1. Is the matter of providing for and supporting one young man truly so difficult that it cannot be resolved?

3) The instructions regarding the method of shipping the packages were delayed; in the future, they will be sent as I wrote.

4) Your request to the holy charity fund and the funds were delivered in due time, as were the funds for Rabbi A.P. (may he live and be well). The account is enclosed. It is surely unnecessary to urge him regarding the settlement of the debt, as the lack of funds is currently delaying the printing of certain items.

5) A great request to continue the list of memoirs and to return to me the *Reshimah* that I sent you to copy.

6) What were the results of distributing the *sichos* at the high school?

I will conclude with the custom of the day, a remembrance of the mitzvah of *machatzis hashekel*: equality—the rich shall not give more and the poor shall not give less; all are equal. Through the *machatzis hashekel*, the shekalim of Haman were nullified (Megillah 13b), for his decree was also against all the Jews equally, from the youth, etc.—see the *sicha* of Purim 5701 regarding this—and they were saved because they were in a state of *mesiras nefesh*, in which all are also equal, for even the "head of the yeshiva," etc.—as written in *Tanya*, Chapter 19 and 20—and all are as nothing before Him, may He be blessed, and they do not know it. May the Ribono shel Olam merit us to see the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu, who will come when he is not expected (Sanhedrin 97a), and as written in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Section 4, that this is the revelation of the aspect of the point of the inner heart. From this perspective, all of Israel, from the greatest to the smallest, are all equal, and one Father for all of them, as written in *Tanya*, Chapter 32 (unlike from the perspective of their source in *Ohr Ein Sof*, where they differ in their greatness and level).

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 66

*[12 Adar Sheni, 5703]*

...The good news that reached us regarding your dedication to everything concerning the education of Judaism has prompted us to approach you with this letter.

You have surely heard of "Machne Israel," which was founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe shlita, and which, with the help of Hashem, has already accomplished much for the strengthening of Judaism, such as the observance of Shabbos, the study of Torah, Taharas Hamishpacha, the wearing of Tefillin, and the like.

Machne Israel is doing much for the spiritual welfare of Jewish soldiers.

Through Machne Israel, a Mishnayos-ba-al-peh society was also established, which distributes portions of Mishnayos to its members by lot—a certain number of chapters per year—to be learned by heart and reviewed at every opportunity: while walking outside, while standing in a shop, while traveling on a train, etc.

We are sending you, in a separate envelope, articles that explain the purpose and activities of Machne Israel. Surely, in your location as well, there is a broad field and work to be done in all areas of Machne Israel’s mission, and we look forward to your letters bringing good news of your activities in the aforementioned matters.

Regarding the days of Purim in those times, our Sages explained (Megillah 13b) that the shekalim of Israel, which they would give every year as a half-shekel, nullified the shekalim of Haman that he gave to Achashverosh to destroy the Jews.

Now, the half-shekel was given to lay the foundation for the first Mishkan of Hashem that existed among the Bnei Yisrael—namely, the sockets (adanim) for the Mishkan—and later they were used to purchase the communal offerings. In both instances, "the rich shall not give more and the poor shall not give less."

This means: when Haman arises and wishes to "destroy, kill, and annihilate," the advised counsel is: "Go, gather all the Jews." And how and in what way can all Jews be united with the appropriate awakening? It is by laying the foundation of the Beis Hamikdash that exists within the heart of every single Jew—the *pintele yid* that is in everyone, regardless of affiliation. For in this, everyone is equal: the one rich in knowledge and the most simple and unlearned. And when one lays this foundation, then one awakens the *pintele* and builds a magnificent Beis Hamikdash; one sees that every Jew is a holy sanctuary where the Ribono shel Olam rests. One only needs to know how to awaken it.

With blessings for a happy Purim, and for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Geulah.

B"H, Erev Shabbos Parshas Parah, 5705

Peace and blessing!

In a separate envelope, we are sending you twenty copies of a letter from the Rebbe shlita to one of those involved in the committee for propaganda regarding Chareidi education.

For reasons known to us, we authorize the distribution of the aforementioned letter only among those participating in the work of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch through their efforts in the field of propaganda regarding education, the establishment of "Shabbos gatherings" and their guidance, the distribution of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch publications, and the like.

Please inform us of the list of individuals to whom you have given the aforementioned letter, including their addresses and the specific ways in which they participate in the work of the Merkos.

If you require additional copies of the aforementioned letter in order to distribute them according to the aforementioned conditions, please let us know, and we will send them to you, G-d willing.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah.

## 208

208

B"H, Friday, 4th of Nissan, 5705

To our dear friends, the distinguished activists,
The members of the Chabad Ladies Auxiliary
in the city of Newark, N.J.
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

We gratefully acknowledge receipt of the sum of two hundred dollars ($200) as a contribution toward the expenses of publishing the "bentsherl."

The magnitude of the zechus of participating in such a mitzvah is immeasurable.

Through this bentsherl, Yiddishkeit is being strengthened for thousands of Jewish children, B"H. The millions of brachos that will, G-d willing, be recited from this bentsherl will serve as advocates for all those who have helped in this endeavor.

We hope that your donation is not a one-time occurrence, but that you will seek, with all your capabilities, to continue helping the Merkaz L’Inyonei Chinuch in its wide-ranging educational work.

Furthermore, knowing your great dedication to Yiddishkeit and your strong energy, we also hope that you will not content yourselves merely with fundraising, but will also do everything possible to attract as many children as possible to receive a genuine Jewish education at the "Beis Sarah" school in Newark, as well as all other work necessary for the flourishing of the school, B"H.

In this month of Nissan, the month of Geulah, we must all remember, more than ever, what our Sages tell us regarding the Geulah:

It was in the zechus of the righteous women that the Jews were redeemed from Mitzrayim. They were the ones who raised the generation of hundreds of thousands of Jewish children—children who, from a young age, "saw" the Ribono shel Olam and recognized the miracles through which He sustains and strengthens His people. And at Krias Yam Suf, when the Mitzriyim, the enemies of the Jews, were all drowned, and the Jews remained whole and continued, under the leadership of Moshe Rabbeinu, on the way to Eretz Yisrael, it was these children who were the first to cry out: "This is my G-d and I will glorify Him, the G-d of my father and I will exalt Him." This was the first song that the entire Jewish people sang together.

At the time of the Geulah Shleimah, speedily in our days, the Jewish people will again—as the Midrash relates—sing a "new song." Let us, then, prepare all Jewish children so that they may be able to proclaim with pride:

**"Zeh Keili" — This is my G-d — "Ve'anveihu" — through our good conduct during the time of Galus, He will now establish His dwelling, the Beis Hamikdash.**

We wish all your members a kosher and happy Pesach, and success in your work.

With the blessing of "Immediately to Teshuvah, immediately to Geulah,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Vaad Hapoel

## 69

[6th of Nissan, 5703]

...To conclude with a matter concerning the month:

Our Sages of blessed memory stated (Rosh Hashanah 10b): "It is taught: Rabbi Eliezer says... in Tishrei they are destined to be redeemed; Rabbi Yehoshua says... in Nissan they are destined to be redeemed" (and see there 27a in Tosafos, s.v. *keman*). The Gemara explains their reasoning: Rabbi Eliezer derives it from the word *shofar* used in connection with Rosh Hashanah, as it is written, "Blow the *shofar* at the new moon" (*Tehillim* 81:4). Rabbi Yehoshua derives it from the "night of watching" (*leil shimurim*) mentioned regarding the Exodus from Egypt—a night that has been watched and awaited from the six days of Creation.

It may be suggested that their dispute regarding the **time** of the redemption corresponds to their dispute regarding the **state of the soul** of Bnei Yisrael at that time, in their fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos. This is found in Sanhedrin (97b): Rabbi Eliezer holds that Yisrael are redeemed when they repent **of their own accord**—which is also the hint of the *shofar* of Rosh Hashanah. As the Rambam elaborates in *Hilchos Teshuvah* (Chapter 3, Halacha 4), this is generally the concept of the month of Tishrei. As our Sages of blessed memory said (*Vayikra Rabbah* 29:1): "Blow the *shofar* at the new moon—if you have improved (*shifartem*) your deeds... [so that they may] ascend in the scales... Tishrei, Tishrei, and You shall forgive and atone for the sins of Your people."

Rabbi Yehoshua holds that even if they do not repent of their own accord, they are redeemed, for Hashem appoints for them a king whose decrees are as harsh as Haman’s, and he turns them to the good. This is like the Exodus from Egypt, where they were redeemed in the merit of the receiving of the Torah (*Shemos Rabbah* 2:5), and our Sages of blessed memory said (*Shabbos* 88a) that Hashem coerced them [to accept the Torah]... hence, this is a protest [against the obligation].

It may be suggested that this is the precision in the language of the Gemara in Rosh Hashanah (ibid.), "watched and awaited **from the six days of Creation**," for these three words are seemingly superfluous, but they are there to hint that it is not dependent on the avodah of man of his own accord.

One may note what is written, "These are the generations of the heavens and the earth when they were created... and there was no man to work the ground" (*Bereishis* 2:4-5), and our Sages of blessed memory said (*Bereishis Rabbah* 13:1), "And there was no man—to make the creatures serve Hashem."

However, there is a great difference between then and now. For at the time of the giving of the Torah, they were not yet commanded, and therefore they had the excuse of coercion and a great protest. This is not the case now, when they are commanded. Even when the teshuvah comes through a harsh king, since it is because Hashem has appointed him over them, regarding this they said that he surely does so with a whole heart. As the Rambam explains (*Hilchos Gerushin* 2:20) the reason: "One whose evil inclination has overpowered him to nullify a mitzvah... and he was beaten until he performed it... this is not considered coerced... since he desires to be of Yisrael and desires to perform all the mitzvos..."

With blessings for a kosher and happy holiday, immediately for teshuvah, immediately for Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 70

*[Nissan 5703]*

...And in this month of redemption: Our Sages of blessed memory state (Rosh Hashanah 10b and elsewhere) that in Tishrei the Jewish people are destined to be redeemed (see also there 27a, Tosafos s.v. *keman*). They explain the reasoning: Rabbi Eliezer derives the concept of the shofar from Rosh Hashanah, while Rabbi Yehoshua derives it from the "night of watching," which is guarded and destined for redemption from Egypt.

It may be said that they follow their respective positions in Sanhedrin (97b): According to Rabbi Eliezer, they are redeemed because they perform teshuvah of their own accord—I have since seen that this is stated in *Siman Maharid*—and this is also the derivation from the shofar of Rosh Hashanah, and in accordance with what the Rambam writes in *Hilchos Teshuvah* (Chapter 3, Halacha 4). See also *Vayikra Rabbah* (Chapter 29): "Shofar—if you have improved (*shifartem*)... Tishrei, and He will forgive and atone..."

Rabbi Yehoshua holds that even if they do not perform teshuvah, the Ribono shel Olam will appoint a king whose decrees are as harsh as Haman’s, and He will bring them back to the good. This is similar to the Exodus from Egypt, where they were redeemed in the merit of the receiving of the Torah (*Shemos Rabbah* Chapter 3). Our Sages of blessed memory state (Shabbos 88a) that He held the mountain over them like a cask, and from here there is a "great protest" against the Torah.

It is known that there is the concept of *Olam, Shanah, Nefesh* (World, Year, Soul). The above applies to *Shanah* and *Nefesh*. It is possible to say that regarding *Olam* (the world), the distinction is simple: according to Rabbi Eliezer, they must be worthy, and thus it is a matter of *achishenah* (hastening the redemption). According to Rabbi Yehoshua, it is possible even if they are not worthy, in the time of *be'itah* (in its due time). The practical difference regarding *Olam* is explained in *Torah Or*, in the *maamar* s.v. *Ad D’lo Yada*, and in *Shaarei Orah*, in the *maamar* s.v. *Yavi’u Levush Malchus*.

However, this is not comparable to the "great protest" at the giving of the Torah, because then they were not yet commanded, and there was a claim of coercion. This is not the case now, when they are commanded; through the coercion, they act **with a whole heart.** As the Rambam explains (*Hilchos Geirushin* Chapter 2, Halacha 20), regarding one whom his *yetzer hara* pressured to nullify a mitzvah, and he was beaten until he performed it—he is not considered coerced, since he wants to be part of Yisrael and wants to perform all the mitzvos.

With blessings for a kosher and happy holiday, for immediate teshuvah and immediate redemption,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 71

B"H, Sunday, 13 Nissan, 5705

To our dear friend, the outstanding avreich, G-d-fearing and esteemed,
The Temimim Rabbi Menachem Zev, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letters:

1) Regarding "Beis Rivkah": It is well known how occupied you are with these communal matters in which you are involved, which stand at the pinnacle of the world, and which one cannot, G-d forbid, neglect even in the slightest.

However, considering that the establishment of schools for girls on the foundation of holiness is, in this time and in these places, a matter of *hatzalas nefashos* for the daughters of Yisrael—and furthermore, that the education of girls influences to a great extent the education of their brothers, the spirit of their families, and the purity of the atmosphere in the Jewish street in general—taking all of the above into account, I do not know if the matter can suffer delay.

And who among you knows if you are not the only ones in your country, of those known to us, to whom one can turn with such a proposal?

As long as you have not yet succeeded in establishing a school for girls, it is appropriate at the very least to endeavor to arrange Shabbos gatherings for girls, as this is easier. Experience has shown that these gatherings subsequently influence their friends to attend "Beis Rivkah," and in general, to change their conduct for the better.

2) Regarding the bochur from Vancouver: I do not know the reasoning behind their rejection of the matter (and although I am not on-site, nevertheless, my opinion does not agree with them **at all** on this; however, I have always avoided the approach of "accept my opinion," and even in this case, it is the same). But, in any event, you must reply to the Rabbi who wrote regarding the aforementioned with a polite letter, including a reason that would be acceptable to others as well, as to why his request was declined. "Let the honor of your colleague be as dear to you as your own," etc.

3) His request regarding the printing matters has been fulfilled, and likewise, the funds that were received (50 shekel) have been distributed according to his instructions.

4) In the writing of the Sefer Torah, we are, with the help of Hashem, already at *Parshas Haazinu*, and therefore anyone who wishes to participate in the letters must hasten to do so. For example: even among his fellow Temimim, there are those who have not yet registered!!
