## 72

B"H, Thursday, 8th of Iyar, 5705
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding the weekly parsha, one may offer an insightful interpretation of *Emor*: "Speak and say" — to warn the adults regarding the children:

In three places (Yevamos 114a), the Torah comes to warn the adults (in terms of maturity) regarding the children (in terms of maturity). They are:

**Blood** — For even if they are immersed in the desire to consume it (as per the words of Rabbi Yehuda, Sifri cited in Rashi on Devarim 12:23), one should not say, "What good will my efforts in proper education do, since he is so invested in the cravings of his heart?"

**Forbidden creatures (shkatzim)** — Even if the one who eats them does so only to anger his Creator (Horayos 11a), as his soul itself finds them repulsive; even so, one might think, what hope is there in speaking to him?

**Tumah of Kohanim** — Where the matter of purity and impurity is not something that can be explained through intellect (Rambam, end of Hilchos Mikvaos), and it pertains only to the Kohanim whom Hashem has chosen to stand and serve before Him. In this case, the educator might say, "How can I explain such matters?" — especially since the child might answer him, "I will be like all the nations, and I have no desire to be a kingdom of Kohanim and a holy nation."

Therefore, the Torah warns us not to despair. Regarding every single Jew, whoever he may be, we are cautioned to exert every possible effort to set him upon the truth and to awaken the point of Yiddishkeit that resides within him.

This is especially true regarding actual children, who are like clay in the hands of the one who educates them.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

#### ***72***

Printed in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 2, p. 679. See also below, Letters 152-153; Likutei Sichos, Vol. 7, p. 147.

## 73

B"H, Tuesday, 20 Iyar, 5705

To our dear friend, the outstanding avreich, G-d-fearing and wholesome, etc.,
Rabbi Hatamim
R' Menachem Zev Gringlas, may he live

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 26 Nissan, your postcard of 27 Nissan, and your letter of 8 Iyar:

1) We share in your joy regarding the purchase of the building for the Yeshiva, and we send you our heartfelt blessings.

2) We were pleased to read in your letter about the good activities that have been carried out, with the help of Hashem, in your educational work in general, and in particular regarding the addition of students to the Yeshiva, the positive impression from the public meeting, and the founding of "Misibos Shabbos" for boys and girls.

3) It is very good that you have already begun to discuss the founding of "Beis Rivkah," and let us hope that the good will shall, with the help of Hashem, be brought from potential into action as soon as possible.

4) Regarding the order of conduct for the Misibos Shabbos, you can learn from the album we sent you, from the report on Misibos Shabbos that they sent you previously, and from the instructions for the counselors (male and female) that we sent you.

If you have detailed questions, please write to us about them.

5) We have noted to send you the printed materials in the quantity you requested.

6) We were happy to hear that, with the help of Hashem, R' R.Y. Weinberg, may he live, succeeded in founding "Mazhiri Shabbos," and we also read what was written in the newspaper regarding its activities.

Surely you will inform us frequently of everything being accomplished by "Mazhiri Shabbos."

7) We were pleased with your report regarding the activities of R' Aharon Klein, may he live, R' Nosson Pellig, may he live, and R' Eliezer Silver, may he live.

8) The tickets for visiting the "Misibos Shabbos" that you printed and sent us as a sample are indeed pleasing to us, but we do not understand how they can be used on Shabbos. Even if the distributors announce at the time of distribution that they should not be brought on Shabbos, forgetfulness is common even among the distributors, and the recipients of the tickets are liable—as is always the habit with entry tickets—to bring them on Shabbos.

Beyond all this, there is reason to be concerned due to the *maris ayin* (appearance of impropriety) for those who see the tickets and do not know the answers to the questions that arise because of this.

9) R' Glustein, may he live, delivered eleven dollars and 50 cents for the Sefer Torah.

10) Regarding the "Sichos" that were published back in Riga and Warsaw, please inform us which ones you are referring to, so that it will be easier for us to determine if it is possible to obtain them.

11) R' Eliyahu Nachum Borenholtz, may he live, a bookseller in Toronto, wrote to us among other things that it would be worthwhile for someone to come there for a period of time to strengthen the matter of *taharas hamishpachah*. Perhaps it is possible for you to look into this matter...

## Ad

28 Iyar, 5703

To the Editorial Board of *Chaver*,

Peace and blessing!

For the Shavuos and jubilee issue of *Chaver*, I would like to write a few words.

The festival that bears the name "Shavuos"—because "seven weeks shall you count"—is such that the day of the festival itself is not counted. Rather, one must count all the days leading up to it, and only then is it the festival. This is one of the distinctions of the *Shalosh Regalim*: *Chag HaMatzos* and *Chag HaSukkos* are connected in the Torah to a specific date in the month, whereas Shavuos is designated in the Torah as the fiftieth day from the beginning of the count (see *Rosh Hashanah* 6b).

What can we learn from this?

***

Shavuos is the festival when the Ribono shel Olam gave us the Torah.

Before *Matan Torah*, people also studied Torah; for the first Jew, Avraham Avinu, was already an elder sitting in the *yeshiva*, as were all the generations after him (*Yoma* 28b). However, at that time, they were *eino metzuveh v’oseh*—they studied with their own powers. Not yet having the *tzivui* (commandment) for it, they could only ascend according to their own limited capacities. Even those who possessed great powers would ascend higher and higher, yet always with a limit, for every created being is inherently limited.

When *Matan Torah* arrived, the Ribono shel Olam said (*Shemos Rabbah* 12:3): "The lower realms shall ascend to the upper realms, and the upper realms shall descend to the lower realms, and I am the Initiator." Through the fact that **"I am the Initiator"**—that I give Myself to you through the Torah (*Shemos Rabbah* 33:1)—you will be able to ascend higher and higher, without limit.

And furthermore—after *Matan Torah*, everyone can attain this, whether one is small in knowledge or great in knowledge, because every Jew has his portion in the Torah.

This is why it is also called *Matan Torah*—the language of a gift (*matanah*)—because such a Torah, with the *maor shebaTorah* (the light within the Torah), can only be received as a gift, not achieved through one's own efforts alone.

- This also helps us understand why Moshe Rabbeinu on Har Sinai was learning Torah and forgetting it, until finally, the Ribono shel Olam gave it to him as a gift (*Shemos Rabbah* 41:6; see also *Alshich*), even though we know (*Yoma* 28b) that "from the days of our forefathers, the *yeshiva* never ceased from them; there was a *yeshiva* with them in Mitzrayim," and Moshe had studied Torah for many decades prior. -

However, a gift is not given to just anyone; one must be worthy of it, and "if one does not provide satisfaction to the Giver, He does not give him the gift."

How did the Jews merit this gift?

Through the *kiyum* (fulfillment) of Torah and *mitzvos* by their forefathers, for in the merit of the forefathers the Torah was given (*Shemos Rabbah* 28:1). The preparation was the fact that the Jews left Mitzrayim—the "nakedness of the land"—and counted the days, waiting for when they would receive the Torah and preparing themselves for it (*Midrash* cited in *Ran* at the end of *Pesachim*; see also *Zohar* Vol. III, p. 97).

***

And this we must always remember: one must remember that when studying Torah, one is studying the *Toras Hashem*, and there must be the *beracha* "who gives the Torah" (*nosain haTorah*)—in the present tense. The Ribono shel Olam is giving the Torah right now, at this moment, and as a gift, just as at *Maamad Har Sinai*. Therefore, it must be "just as there it was with awe, with fear, with trembling and quaking, so too here it must be with awe, with fear, with trembling and quaking" (*Berachos* 22a). One’s *yiras chet* (fear of sin) must precede one’s wisdom, for only then is one’s wisdom sustained (*Avos* 3:9). Then, one must count, labor, and illuminate the forty-nine *shaarei binah* (gates of understanding) that a person can reach with his own powers. Through all this, he merits the "counting of fifty days," so that in his Torah study, "the Divine Presence is with him, and the *halacha* follows his view in every place" (*Sanhedrin* 93b); he learns and is directed toward the ultimate truth. And in the *avodah* and knowledge of Hashem, he is granted lofty illuminations from above [see *Ran, Nedarim* 38a; *Ramban* at the beginning of his commentary on the Torah, and elsewhere. And even though our Sages said (*Nedarim* ibid.) "He lacked one, as it is written, 'You have made him a little lower than the angels,'" it has already been said (*Avodah Zarah* 5a), "Had they not sinned... I said, you are angels"].

***

In setting the goal for the founding of the periodical *Chaver*—to reach even those homes that have until now been far from *Yiddishkeit*—one must remember: no matter how far a Jew may find himself, and no matter how deeply he may have fallen, he can emerge from "darkness to a great light." One must not despair of him, and one must tell him that he, too, must not despair.

One must tell him that "I am Hashem your G-d, who brought you out of the land of Mitzrayim"—the Ribono shel Olam Himself helps him and pulls him out of his coarseness, just as He took the Jews out of the forty-nine gates of impurity in Mitzrayim.

One must tell him that he only needs to awaken his *ratzon* (will), his *nekudas pnimius haYahadus* (the inner point of Jewishness)—the *pintele Yid*—and he will ascend higher and higher. Eventually, after traversing everything he can reach with his own powers, he will receive as a gift from above that "they sanctify him greatly from above" (*Yoma* 39b), and there will be "freedom from suffering, freedom from *galus*."

With wishes for success in your work, and with the blessing of receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness, immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to *geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

76

B"H, 3rd of Sivan, 5705

To the distinguished Rabbi and Chassid, the wise and learned, etc.,
The Tamim
Rabbi... may he live

Greetings and blessings!

Based on what I have heard regarding your person and essence, I am writing without preamble. You are surely aware of the details regarding the work of "Machne Israel" and "Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch," which were founded by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, some time ago. Many of the details of their work and their branches have been explained in *HaKria VeHaKedusha*, in the sichos of the Rebbe, shlita, in the volume *Hayom Yom*, and elsewhere.

It is self-evident that it is not the founder’s intention that Machne Israel and Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch be satisfied with working only in the United States and Canada. Rather, the intention is that people be found who are suited to the spirit of the aforementioned program in various locations, and that these individuals should take upon themselves the work in their place of residence, both personally and by stirring their acquaintances to assist them.

We have written to you several times regarding work in these areas, but we have not been privileged with a response. Since the time is appropriate, I am writing once again regarding the following:

1) The completion of the entire Shas Mishnayos by heart is scheduled for Sunday, the 15th of Sivan, at which time a lottery will also be held for the coming year, which concludes after Shavuos, 5706. The purpose of the *Chevras Mishnayos Be'al Peh* was explained well in the second volume of the collected letters of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, which surely reached you some time ago. Because of the distance, and since it is impossible to stir everyone from here, we suggest that you take upon yourself the recruitment of members for this society. You should divide the entire Shas Mishnayos among yourselves, whether in collaboration with our friends, Anash, in Manchester—who did the same last year—or as a separate group, in such a way that you schedule the completion for the same day, after Shavuos, 5706. We would appreciate it if you would inform us of your positive actions regarding all of this.

2) Over time, we have had several publications here, and the intention here too is that they spread among the widest possible circles. The precision in the expression "your wellsprings shall spread outward" (*yufutzu mayanosecha chutzah*) is well known—*chutzah* specifically (see the sicha of Simchas Torah 5690, section 32). Our suggestion to you is to take upon yourself the effort of finding a suitable person to engage in their distribution and sale (so that it does not become "a physician who charges nothing, is worth nothing"), so that in this way they will reach distant people as well. In order not to delay the matter, we are sending for now—in your name—ten of each type. Please inform us of their receipt, and we thank you in advance if you respond promptly to all of the above.

You surely remember your letter to me regarding the subject of Tzimtzum. Consider this: if one were to be in this place and at this very moment, truly with him: his Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, the Baal Shem Tov, the Arizal, Rashbi at the time of the Idra, Rabbi Akiva at the time he expounded on the *Maaseh Merkavah*, or the like, as he is in the Holy of Holies, etc., etc., up to Moshe Rabbeinu at the moment of the Giving of the Torah—would he not have no grasp of place or existence at all? Yet, the teachings of Chassidus have come and concluded that the Tzimtzum is only in the light, and not, Heaven forbid, in the Source of the Light (*Maor*). The *Maor* is present now, right here, just as He is present in the Holy of Holies of the World of Asiyah, at the moment of the Giving of the Torah on Mount Sinai, in the World of Atzilus, and in the worlds of the Ein Sof just as He was before the first Tzimtzum, when the light of the Ein Sof filled all of existence!

With blessings for the receiving of the Torah internally, immediately to Teshuvah, immediately to Geulah,

Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 77

B"H, Friday, 8 Sivan, 5703

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, wise and elevated, etc.,
Rabbi Y. HaKohen Katz, may he live

Greetings and blessings!

You have surely received in good time the sichos that were sent to you according to your order while you were here, and I have also endeavored to ensure that they reach the necessary places.

How great is the matter of *mezakeh es harabim*—it is certainly unnecessary to elaborate on this. Therefore, we hope that in the future as well, you will be active in this area, and gradually expand the work by drawing in other people who will assist you in this.

I heard from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, that the Alter Rebbe once said: Torah is G-dly and spiritual, yet the first mitzvah to be written in the Torah is the mitzvah of *pru u'rvu*? Rather, what is the meaning of this? The Torah is *deracheha*—and the order within it—is *darchei noam* (ways of pleasantness); the first mitzvah is: A Yid must want there to be another Yid. End quote.

With wishes for a *chag sameach* and for the receiving of the Torah *b'pnimiyus* (in an internalized manner),

And with the blessing of *l'alter l'teshuvah, l'alter l'geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 78

B"H, Friday, 8 Sivan, 5705

To our esteemed friend, the great Gaon, the great Chassid, renowned for his praise, G-d-fearing, who dwells in the tent of Torah, possessor of noble character traits, etc.,
Rabbi Menachem Zvi Rivkin, shlita
Manchester

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from before the festival:

1) Your request for a blessing has been conveyed to my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, and you will surely receive a direct response.

2) In the writing of the Sefer Torah for the welcoming of Moshiach, they have already reached Parshas Haazinu. Therefore, anyone who wishes to participate—while the writing is still in progress—must hasten to do so.

3) The completion of the study of Shas Mishnayos by heart has been set for Sunday, 15 Sivan. At that time, a raffle will also be held for the coming year—until the festival of Shavuos, may it come to us for good. Surely, your honor, with the help of our friends, may they live, who are in your vicinity, will also organize among you the division and study of Mishnayos by heart, with even greater intensity than last year.

Let it be known that the intention of reviewing Mishnayos by heart is not only for yeshiva students and those who dwell in the tent of Torah, but for **all** of the House of Israel. That is to say, even those occupied with business should memorize a few chapters, and as they walk outside, stand in their shops, or similar situations, they should review them in order to purify the atmosphere. You have surely already received the second collection of letters from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita; please see his sicha there regarding this.

4) We have sent to your honor over time several printed materials published here by "Kehot," and they have surely arrived on time. We will also send you more copies of the "Seder Brachos and Tefillos" as per his instruction. We would be very grateful if you could inform us of their receipt, and also if you have sent—and how many—remittances to Eretz Yisrael.

In this regard, it would also be very good if you could organize, through those who do His will, a committee for the distribution and sale of these materials. The committee would inform us how many copies of each type to send, and would handle their distribution and sale.

5) *HaTamim*, issue 8, has been sent to you as per your request, as has the *Hayom Yom* collection.

I will conclude with the wish that through the feeling of the inwardness of the time of the giving of our Torah—in which there is no change, and just as it was then with awe, etc., so too now with awe, etc.—and through the matter of the festival of Shavuos, which depends on Sefiras HaOmer (which, according to most Poskim, is only Rabbinic in our time, because the effect of the *avodah* of *birurim* will be **revealed** only in the time to come, at the completion of the *birurim*; and because it exists even now, some say that Sefiras HaOmer is Torah-ordained—see *Tanya* ch. 46, *Torah Or* end of Parshas Bereishis, and elsewhere), we will merit the festival of the First Fruits when the Beis HaMikdash is rebuilt, speedily in our days.

Immediately to Teshuvah, immediately to Geulah.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 59

B.H., Tuesday, 12th of Sivan, 5705

To my friend, the distinguished scholar, G-d-fearing, etc.,
Rabbi A. S. Shuv,

Greetings and blessings!

Please forgive the delay in my response to your letter, which was due to various circumstances. I am writing now regarding the following:

The completion of the *Shas Mishnayos* by heart has been scheduled for Sunday, the 1st of Sivan. At that time, a distribution will also be made for the coming year—that is, until the upcoming *Shavuos*, may it arrive for good. It is our hope that you, together with our friend, the distinguished Rabbi and Chassid, etc., Rabbi M. T. and all of *anash*, will organize a distribution of *Mishnayos* by heart in your area for the coming year, with even greater enthusiasm than in the past.

Over the course of time, we have sent to your camp [the materials] printed here by us. These were sent to the address of the distinguished Rabbi and Chassid, etc., Rabbi M. T., with the earnest request that he assist in this, and that he also encourage all those involved to exert effort in their distribution and sale through a special committee of energetic young people for this purpose, or in another manner suitable to the conditions of your location. May it be the will [of Hashem] that the prophecy, "Your wellsprings shall spread outward"—specifically—be fulfilled among you, and that our righteous Moshiach may arrive.

We have written regarding the above to Rabbi M. T., and it surely reached him in due time. "Each man shall help his fellow," and may Hashem’s desire succeed through their hands.

Regarding your Torah insights, in what you wrote concerning the details of *melikah* (the ritual pinching of a bird sacrifice)—your words are pleasant and sweet.

Based on the teaching of our Sages that words of Torah are "like a hammer that shatters rock," there are many facets to Torah.

One may also explain—briefly—the concept of *melikah* in the *avodah* of man, according to what is explained in the teachings of Chassidus.

*Melikah* is performed from the nape of the neck (*oref*). This means that one begins by separating the head from the body—and specifically the heart—from the nape, and only afterward does one reach the *simanim* (the windpipe and esophagus).

In *avodah*, there is a distinction between "face" (*panim*) and "nape" (*oref*). *Panim* is *avodah* that is according to *taam v'daas* (intellectual understanding), where the heart and its *midos* are guided by the instructions of the intellect in the head.

*Oref* (nape) relates to "stiff-necked" (*kesheh oref*), where one must utilize the concept of *kabbalas ol* (acceptance of the yoke) and force the heart against its will, so that its conduct will be as it ought to be.

"Bird" and "beast" in *avodah* represent *beinonim* and *resha'im* (fish represent the level of *tzaddikim*, as explained in many places; for within man himself there are three levels: *tzaddikim*, *beinonim*, and *resha'im*—these being the *nefesh habehamis*, the *nefesh hasichlis* and the body, and the *nefesh ha-Elokis*, and this level was explained in the previous letter). Now, it is explained in *Tanya* (Chapters 12, 13, and elsewhere) regarding the true definition of a *beinoni* and a *rasha*, that even the *beinoni* has never committed a sin in his life, and the evil in the left chamber cannot bring its desire from potential into action because the intellect is dominant over the heart. Nevertheless, the evil remains in its strength and might—and, on the contrary, it strengthens over time. Therefore, there is a need for the "nape"—the power of suppressing one's *midos* without entering into intellectual arguments with the evil, [acting] completely and readily. This is especially true since there are times when one experiences a "clogging of the heart" (*timtum halev*), and the light of the *neshamah* and the intellect does not shine as brightly. The only advice for this is to "beat" and "roar" at the *yetzer hara* (see *Tanya*, Chapter 27). Needless to say, this applies to the "beast"—the *rasha*, whose evil has a grasp even on the letters of his thoughts, speech, and action; the "inanimate" (*domem*) within the soul, which requires the *kabbalas ol* of the "inanimate" in *avodah*. If, before he has slaughtered the beast, the power of *kabbalas ol* ceases in him, the beast is a *treifah* (see *Chullin* 19b).

Now, this applies to the "outside." But when one offers a bird as a sacrifice in the *Beis Hamikdash*—where souls are nullified like a candle before a torch, having no other will or desire at all, which is the concept of internal prostration—there must be an *is'arusa d'lesata* (awakening from below) that is akin to the *is'arusa d'le'eila* (awakening from above). His *avodah* is also in the category of "face" in its entirety, according to his level (unlike the beast, for "according to the camel is the burden"). Therefore, he performs the *melikah* from the nape, and only the "face" remains. Then he finishes with the *simanim*. This must be done by the *Kohen* himself, and not through a messenger, because "the *Kohanim* are the messengers of the Merciful One," and a messenger is like the sender. For through *avodah* in the category of "face," a union of "face-to-face" is achieved. With this, we can understand why *shechitah* is valid when performed by a non-priest (*zar*), whereas *melikah* is not. Since the destruction of the *Beis Hamikdash*, there is a semblance of this during *davening* and Torah study, for the synagogue and the *beis medrash* are called a "miniature sanctuary" (*mikdash me'at*).

An explanation and foundation for the above can be understood from what is written in *Tanya*, Chapter 12: "Each at designated times, such as during *Krias Shema* and *davening*, which is a time of *mochin d'gadlus* (expanded consciousness)." And in Chapter 13, "And in the Torah of Hashem is his desire," etc., like during *Krias Shema* and *davening*. There, at the end of the chapter, it is proven that the love of the *beinonim* during *davening* is akin to the *avodah* of the *tzaddikim* (see *Torah Or*, *Maamar Mizmor Shir Chanukas*, section 2, the *drushim* on *Amalek*, and elsewhere).

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah,
