## 81

81

B"H, Sunday, Erev Rosh Chodesh Tammuz, 5703

To the honorable Rav and Chossid, the distinguished and exalted, etc., Rabbi Ch. B. (may he live),

Greetings and blessings!

I am writing to you now to inform your honor that last week, a *siyum* of the entire *Shas Mishnayos* was held here, organized by the *Chevras Mishnayos* under the auspices of "Machne Israel." Following the *siyum*, the *Shas* was also distributed for the coming year (5704–5705). Once again, we come to encourage all our friends—and in general, all those who study and cherish Torah, and your honor in particular—to participate in this *chevra*, and to publicize among all their acquaintances and friends the matter of purifying the atmosphere through the letters of Torah.

— It is possible to find in the *nigleh* of Torah a hint and connection between the "atmosphere" (*avir*) and the review of Torah *ba'al peh* (orally). In *Sanhedrin 109a*, it says, "The atmosphere of the city makes one forget..."—a bad sign for **Torah.** The concept that "the atmosphere of Eretz Yisrael makes one wise" (*Bava Basra 158b*) relates to understanding and comprehension. —

Please endeavor to have them join this *chevra* as well, and to review *Mishnayos* by heart, "when you walk on the way," etc., as explained at length in the *sichos* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, on this subject. Furthermore, through the participation of these reviewers in one *chevra*, there is the added merit that "the many who perform a mitzvah are not comparable to the few," etc.

I ask for your honor’s forgiveness for not having answered your letter in a timely manner, due to various pressures and circumstances. Although time is still not very accommodating, I will nevertheless provide some comments regarding what was written in your letter.

1) Regarding your honor’s dissatisfaction with the answer provided concerning the *Maseches Sofrim* (Chapter 2, Halacha 5), which suggests that the two reasons [for the *mitzvah*] elevate the sanctity—similar to "days that have passed" and "days that are entering" being treated as one—even though in *Shabbos* (21b) this is a dispute between *Amoraim*: I wrote that we find similar instances elsewhere, such as in *Berachos* (59a and there), "Therefore, let us say both," and in *Bava Basra* (75a), "Let it be according to this and according to that." Your honor did not find it appropriate to equate them, because in *Berachos* and *Bava Basra* both reasons are necessary, as the *Maharsha* and *Tosafos Yeshanim* write there, whereas in *Maseches Sofrim*, one of the reasons should suffice. If this is the only objection, it is not a strong one, for even here it can be said that *Maseches Sofrim* holds that several arguments necessitate both reasons.

(Even though in *Shas* it is somewhat implied that they do not hold this way, and just as in the case of *Berachos* and *Bava Basra*, one *Amora* disagrees with the other, yet we conclude with both.)

The gates of reasoning are not locked, and I will bring only a few: For someone who begins to light in the middle of Chanukah, based on the reason of "days that have passed," it is obvious that he lights like everyone else. Based on the reason of "elevating in sanctity" alone, one could perhaps be in doubt regarding this law (see *Orach Chaim*, end of 672). The reason of "elevating in sanctity," etc., **decides** that we should light corresponding to the days that have passed and not corresponding to the days that are entering. "Elevating in sanctity" primarily negates only the possibility of decreasing. It must be so, for otherwise, it would be difficult: why is the law of "adding and increasing" only a *hiddur* (beautification) of a *hiddur*, and why was the *mitzvah* not established from the outset in this manner of "adding and increasing," even though we derive it from the verse "elevating in sanctity," etc.?

"Elevating in sanctity" is derived from a verse, while "corresponding to the days," etc., is merely a logical deduction.

2) Regarding the difficulty you raised from Rabbi Yehuda, who says in *Taanis* (29a), "Had I been in that generation, I would have established it on the tenth, because the majority of the Sanctuary was burned on it." Yet, Rabbi Yehuda holds in *Bava Kamma* (22a) that "fire is [the responsibility of the owner] because of his arrow," and the *Nimukei Yosef* explains that this means the entire act of the igniter is completed at the moment the fire is lit. If so, even regarding the destruction of the Temple, since they ignited the fire on the ninth, the act was completed then; why did he want to establish it on the tenth?

Regarding the actual logic of the *Nimukei Yosef*, there is much to discuss, and this is not the place. But regarding the above, I did not understand the difficulty. In *Taanis*, they are discussing on which day *Bnei Yisrael* should mourn for their tragedy, and it has no bearing on the question of when the participation of the heathens was completed. For example, if one strikes his fellow and he dies after several days because of the blow, it is obvious that his relatives mourn on the day of death, not on the day of the striking.

3) Regarding what you wrote—that in the destruction of the Temple, since it was the fire of the Holy One, He has the power to "take back His arrow" at any time: one should note from *Rosh Hashanah* (18a) that a decree that has an oath attached to it cannot be torn up. Such was the case with the destruction of the Temple, for this is what the verse "your iniquity is inscribed" refers to, as brought there. This is also stated explicitly in *Pesichta d'Eicha Rabbah* (24): immediately, the Holy One **swore**, etc. Even if you say that Rav in *Rosh Hashanah* (ibid.) disagrees—(and it is a matter of study how Rav would interpret the verse "inscribed in the writing of truth," which refers to a communal decree; see *Yevamos* 105a)—

The matter was dependent on *teshuvah* (and in *Rosh Hashanah* 31b, "and the Holy One was delayed," etc., perhaps they would repent), and everything is in the hands of Heaven except for the fear of Heaven (*Berachos* 33b).

Perhaps it can be said, according to your honor's logic, that this is a secondary reason why He does not "take back His arrow," but it is not that the act of shooting the arrow (igniting the fire) itself is in a manner that He cannot take it back.

4) Regarding your question: from where do we know in the miracle of Chanukah that already on the first day the oil had the power to burn for eight days? Since this is a miraculous matter and the laws of nature do not apply, one could say that the miracle was renewed every moment or every day (this seems to be your intent, even if not explicitly stated).

There are several answers to this: a) I wrote that if we say that through the miracle it was brought about that the oil had the power on the first day to burn for eight days, the opinion of *Beis Shammai*—that we light corresponding to the days that are entering—is well understood. Seemingly, it is not understood what the "days that are entering" have to do with lighting upon them on the first day. Your honor comes and objects that we do not say this, and if so, the opinion of *Beis Shammai* will not be understood. b) All the factors that necessitated the eight-day miracle (purification, pressing the oil on the first day, the four-day journey to go and the four-day journey to return, etc.) were already present on the first day and were not renewed later. For the following year, it was revealed that the nature of the miracle was that there would be no interruption in the lighting of the candles, and this manner and intent existed on the first day; they had no place to rest except upon the cruse of oil. c) Why multiply miracles unnecessarily? For example, in the miracle of the cruse of oil, it did not run out (I Kings 17). He who commanded the oil to burn should command the vinegar to burn (*Taanis* 25a), etc. Shall we say that the miracle was renewed every moment? Furthermore: if you say so, it would be difficult why it would burn during the day (there in *Taanis*), for "a candle in the daytime," etc. Also, from where do we know that "a good measure is swifter to come than a measure of punishment" (*Shabbos* 97a)? It should be noted that in *Berachos* (54a), Lot's wife is listed in the same category as the stones of Elgavish, and it is understood that there is no proof from there, only a mere hint. This requires further study regarding the plagues of Egypt, where some ceased on their own and some through prayer.

5) Regarding what I wrote in my previous letter in answering the *Beis Yosef*—that they divided the oil in the cruse into eight parts—it requires study from *Zevachim* (88a) that "vessels are only sanctified when full." If so, the lamps of the Menorah were not full. I have since seen that I was mistaken, for the oil for the Menorah was not sanctified by the lamps of the Menorah, but rather by the measure of half a *log* that was in the Temple, as stated in *Menachos* (85b). It must be so, because even every day the lamps of the Menorah were not full, as they held more than half a *log*, as is proven there (89a), which says they measured from top to bottom.

It is a wonder for what purpose the lamps of the Menorah were larger than half a *log*. It can be said based on what is written in the *Yerushalmi*, brought in *Tosafos* (s.v. *v'shi'aru* there), that if they found only a thick wick, they would add to the measure of oil.

6) Regarding your observation that since lighting is not an *avodah* (service) (*Yoma* 24b), and according to the Rambam it is valid even *l'chatchila* by a *zar* (non-priest) (*Biyas Mikdash* 9:7), why is the Menorah only inaugurated through lighting (*Menachos* 49a)?

Seemingly, the reason is explained: the concept of inauguration is the beginning of the use of this vessel for its purpose (see Rashi on the Torah, *Shemos* 28:41). The purpose of the Menorah is simple, as stated in many verses: to light the lamp continually. Therefore, it is obvious that its inauguration is the lighting of the candles. The *Mishnah* merely specified that it is specifically at twilight. The Rambam (*Temidim U'Musafim* 3:11) added to the language of the *Mishnah*, "and not the Menorah except through the lighting of the seven candles," based on the Gemara (there 50a) that the main thing is that there must be *hatavah* (preparation) in the morning. If so, it makes no difference when the arrangement of the candles took place—

—which is also an *avodah*, as it is written, "Aaron shall arrange it" (*Shemos* 27:21, *Vayikra* 24:3), and as it is stated in *Yoma* (24b), "there is the placing of the wick," etc., "there is the placing of the oil"—

—whether in the morning or in the evening, provided that the lighting is in such a manner that the *hatavah* will be in the morning.

The fact that lighting is not an *avodah* is not because the illumination of the candles is not an important thing, but because the **human** action in this is not significant, for there is no toil of human hands in it, as written in *Tosafos* (s.v. *hadlakah* in *Yoma* there), because the rising of the flame, which is the purpose of the Menorah, is **by itself.** If so, it does not relate to the inauguration of the Menorah.

7) Your honor also wrote that according to what is stated in the *Yerushalmi Shekalim* (4:2), that the Table, the Menorah, the Altars, and the Curtain are indispensable for the sacrifices, and in *Megillas Taanis* (15) it says that the Hasmoneans were occupied with building the Altar and it was finished on the eighth day; if so, there was no Altar then, and consequently, the *hatavah* of the Menorah was nothing, and certainly the lighting then was only a *mitzvah* in general without any connection to *avodah*. Thus, there is no law that "vessels are only sanctified when full," and this also removes the common question: why was a miracle needed, since *tumah* (impurity) is permitted in a communal setting? This is because then the lighting was a *mitzvah* and not a sacrifice.

It is a wonder, for *tumah* and *Shabbos* are derived from the same verse, as stated in *Toras Kohanim* (Parshas Emor), brought in Rambam (*Hilchos Temidim U'Musafim* 3:10). If so, according to this, how did they light the Menorah then on *Shabbos*? In many places, it is implied that they lit for eight consecutive days. Furthermore, it is difficult: how could they use a Menorah designated for *avodah* in a matter that is not *avodah*? However, regarding this, it can be said that since they made a new Menorah, as stated in *Rosh Hashanah* (24b), and a holy vessel that has not yet been used by the Holy One may be used by a commoner (*Tosefta* 2:1 of *Megillah*, 14 *Hilchos Beis HaBechirah* end of ch. 1).

But it is a wonder: from where do we know this *mitzvah* of lighting, if we say that there is no obligation from the Torah? On the contrary, it would be "strange fire" which He did not command them, and one who enters the Sanctuary not for *avodah* is liable (*Rambam*, *Hilchos Biyas Mikdash* 2:4).

Since the matter has come to hand, let us say a word about it:

Regarding what is written in *Megillas Taanis*, one should note what is written there in Chapter 8: "On the 23rd of Marcheshvan, the *sorig* (partition) was torn down from the courtyard," etc., "and when the Hasmoneans grew strong," etc., "and on that day they tore it down, they made it a holiday." And there at the beginning of Chapter 9: "On the 3rd of Kislev, the stones were removed from the courtyard," etc., "and when the Hasmoneans grew strong," etc., "and on that day they removed them, they made it a holiday." This implies that already at the end of Marcheshvan and the beginning of Kislev, they began the purification of the courtyard. If so, it is difficult why they waited until the 25th of Kislev. I have found in later writings, the Book of Maccabees I, 4: "They built a new altar, etc., and they renewed all the holy vessels and placed the Menorah in the Sanctuary, etc., and upon the Menorah they lit its lamps, etc., and it was on the twenty-fifth day of the ninth month, which is Kislev, etc., and they rose early in the morning and offered burnt offerings upon the Altar, etc., and they celebrated the dedication of the Altar for eight days." However, I am hesitant to bring proof from these books, even though in many places the words of Ben Sira, Wisdom of Solomon, and others are brought.

Regarding the law of the *Yerushalmi* mentioned above, that the Table, etc., are indispensable, etc., and according to the conclusion there, they are indispensable for *avodah* inside at least.

(And what is written in *Korban HaEdah* there, s.v. *v'afilu*, "such as the Ark," is certainly a printing error, for in the Second Temple there was no Ark. But it is difficult to derive from it that the placement is not indispensable, and also the Curtain should not be indispensable. Also, what is written there in *Pnei Moshe*, s.v. *v'rabi*, "and such as the Table," is not understood, for the Table is indispensable even according to Rabbi Yochanan, since it is written regarding it "a side," and he should have said "the Curtain.")

In *Tosefta* (6:1 of *Menachos*), it says the Table, the Menorah, and the Altars are indispensable for one another, and the Curtains are not mentioned, and it also does not distinguish between *avodah* outside and inside. Perhaps the reason they are not mentioned in the verse as indispensable is because the Ark and the Curtains have no *avodah* in them, for the sprinkling of blood on the Curtains and between the poles is considered sprinkling even if it did not touch—*Tosafos* (s.v. *ela* in *Zevachim* 15a). See *Mishneh L'Melech*, *Hilchos Avodas Yom HaKippurim* 3:5.

I have not yet found this law in the Rambam.

It seems to me that for the Rambam, our *Shas* disagrees with the *Yerushalmi* and *Tosefta*, and his proof is from *Zevachim* (59a): "An altar that was uprooted, incense is offered in its place." If the *avodah* of the altar itself is not indispensable, how much more so is the *avodah* of other things not indispensable? From this, we derive for the other vessels.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 82

B"H, Monday, 2 Tammuz, 5703

To our dear friend, the outstanding avreich, G-d-fearing and esteemed,
Rabbi Y. Weinberg, may he live,
Montreal

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letters requesting clarification as to why you have not received a reply to your letters to the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, which detail your avodah regarding the observance of Shabbos and similar matters.

I presented this matter to him before the Yom Tov, and again this week. However, immediately before and after the Yom Tov, the time did not permit for a response to anything other than the most urgent matters. Certainly, in the coming week, you will receive a response to your questions from the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita.

On this occasion, I would like to prompt you once again regarding the continuation of the list of memoirs from the years 5699–5700, which you discontinued at the beginning.

It requires study regarding what is written, "If you forsake Me for one day, I will forsake you for two days"—whether this applies only to Torah (as is somewhat implied in Zohar, Vol. III, 36a), or if it also applies to other matters of holiness (seemingly, this is implied in Rashi—Devarim 11:13—who cites this in the context of "If you shall surely forget," which speaks of fear of Heaven), or if it is a natural phenomenon and applies to all matters where forgetfulness is possible. This requires further study of the parables brought regarding this in the Yerushalmi, end of Berachos.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 83

B"H, Monday, 9 Tammuz, 5703

To our dear friend, the honored and exalted Rabbi, G-d-fearing and so forth,
Rabbi A. Tarshish, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

The Rebbe shlita has conveyed to us your request that "Machne Israel" send a shaliach to your camp to strengthen the influence on your students, may they live, to travel to the yeshivah.

In accordance with this, we ask that you inform us: 
a) Whether you find it more appropriate for the shaliach to come now, or if it would be better at the end of the summer, closer to the beginning of the winter term in the yeshivos.

b) Whether it would suffice for the shaliach to come only for Shabbos.

We are interested in hearing about your activities in the field of "Machne Israel." Even though you are extremely busy during the summer months, surely you can utilize the moments when you meet with many people whom you do not see during the winter to arouse them regarding matters of strengthening Yiddishkeit. Even a few words that come from the heart and enter—therefore—into the heart, have a great influence, b'ezras Hashem, and sooner or later, one can see the good fruits...

#### ***83***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 23, p. 422, and completed based on a photocopy of the letter.

## 84

B”H, Monday, 16 Tammuz, 5703

To the honorable Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, etc.,
Rabbi Z. Halevi, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Your letter was received, and enclosed is the receipt for your donation of two (2) dollars for Machne Israel.

The donation for the Yeshiva and Kollel Chabad has been forwarded to them, and they will surely send you a receipt directly.

Membership cards for the Mishnayos B’al Peh society were sent some time ago to your sons, may they live, and they surely arrived on time.

I would suggest that you also participate in the other activities of Machne Israel and the Merkaz L’Inyonei Chinuch.

I imagine that it is easily within your ability to be active in the above, specifically in two areas: 
a) Distributing the kuntresim and sichos that have been printed—among all those over whom you have influence—by explaining their great value in awakening [a desire for] teshuvah and yiras shamayim. This is especially true in these times, the footsteps of Moshiach, and the concept of "immediately to teshuvah, immediately to Geulah" is explained in the letters of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, which are printed in his second collection of letters.

b) Ensuring that your sons, may they live, also distribute the aforementioned sichos and the "shmuessen"—in Yiddish and English—which are printed for Jewish boys and girls, the content of which brings children closer to Torah and Yiddishkeit.

The price of these kuntresim, sichos, and "shmuessen" is minimal, and anyone interested in them will certainly want to purchase them. Everything depends on finding a person who is willing and knows how to explain the content of the sicha or kuntres to those who do not yet know that the light is good.

It is surely known to you the teaching of the Alter Rebbe, based on the verse "The steps of man are established by Hashem," which states: When a Yid arrives in a certain place, it is for the purpose of fulfilling a mitzvah—whether a mitzvah between man and Hashem or a mitzvah between man and his fellow. A Yid is a shaliach of Above; wherever he is, he is the power of the Sender.

And my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, writes in one of his letters: We find that the primary love of the Holy One, Blessed be He, for Avraham Avinu was because "he will command"—which is interpreted as "he will connect"—his children and his household. This means that all the greatness of his avodah in the trials does not compare to the level of "he will command" and connect others, [the merit of] enabling others to perform mitzvos.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 16 Tammuz, 5703

To the distinguished, honored, and elevated, one who fears the word of Hashem, etc.,
Rabbi D. HaLevi, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Regarding your bewilderment at what I said during the *siyum* of the *Shas* *Mishnah* by heart—that every single Jew, whoever he may be, even a completely wicked person, *r"l*, has hope all his days, and in the end, whether by his own will or through compulsion from Above, whether in his lifetime or after his death, he is raised from the gates of impurity in which he was sunken, and is passed through various stages of purification and refinement, until he, too, is united and attached to his root, the *Ohr Ein Sof, B"H*.

And you raised a difficulty, noting that this is a puzzling matter and that there are several contradictions to it.

Therefore, I am copying here some of the sayings of our Sages that served as the foundation for what I said, and I will explain and resolve the points that are difficult.

**Question**

I heard it said that, according to what is explained in *Chassidus*, every single Jew, whoever he may be, and even if he was a completely wicked person all his days, *r"l*, has hope. And in the end, whether by his own will or through compulsion from Above, in his lifetime or after his death, he is raised from the gates of impurity in which he was sunken, and is passed through various stages of purification and refinement, until he, too, is attached and united to his root and source, the *Ohr Ein Sof, B"H*.

Seemingly, this statement is extremely puzzling, and there are several contradictions to it from Scripture and the sayings of our Sages.

*R' Dovid Stockhammer*
*Shochet u'Bodek, Newark, N.J.*

**Answer**

The source of this teaching is explained in many places, among them:

In the *maamar* "Ki Yish'alcha Bincha" (5700), it states: "All Israel have a share in the World to Come," which refers to the era of the Resurrection... The difference between *Gan Eden* and the era of the Resurrection is that regarding *Gan Eden* it is written, "Who shall ascend the mountain of Hashem... he who has clean hands and a pure heart," etc., meaning there are several conditions required to be able to ascend to *Gan Eden*... There are those who merit to ascend only to the Lower *Gan Eden*, and they do not merit the Upper *Gan Eden*... The general revelation in *Gan Eden* is only for souls, not for bodies. But in the era of the Resurrection—that is, the Resurrection of the Dead—they said "All Israel have a share in the World to Come," meaning that all will come to the revelation of the Resurrection. And even though there will be judgment and reckoning there, and it will be even more difficult than the judgment and reckoning regarding the revelations of *Gan Eden*... the general revelation will be for souls in bodies specifically. End quote.

The foundation for these words is in the *drush* of our *Alter Rebbe*, "L'havin Biur Inyan HaAvos Hem HaMerkavah" (*Torah Or*, *Parshas Yisro*), which states: "The matter of the World to Come, which is *Gan Eden* and the Resurrection of the Dead, is explained by the commentators and by the *Ramban* in *Shaar HaGemul* that the primary reward of the World to Come is in the Resurrection of the Dead, for the level of the Resurrection of the Dead is higher than the Upper *Gan Eden*. Now, in *Gan Eden*, the souls of the righteous sit without bodies... whereas the Resurrection of the Dead is that they will stand in their bodies... even the sinners of Israel are full of *mitzvos* like a pomegranate, and therefore all Israel have a share in the World to Come in the Resurrection of the Dead, except for those whom the Sages enumerated." End quote.

See also *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Shelach*, the first and second *maamarim* beginning with the words "Ani."

And since several sayings, **at first glance**, contradict the above, I am copying here some of the sayings of our Sages which, in my humble opinion, served as the foundation for what is stated in these *Chassidic* discourses, and I will explain and resolve the points that are difficult.

***

**A.** First, it must be clarified from the *Gemara* and the *Poskim* that it is **possible** for even the most severely wicked people to eventually merit the Resurrection of the Dead (unlike *Gan Eden*, as mentioned above). This is as follows:

1) We learned in the *Mishnah* (*Sanhedrin* 90a): "All Israel have a share in the World to Come... and these are the ones who do not have a share... Yeravam, Achav, and Menashe," etc. The *Rambam* rules (*Hilchos Teshuvah*, ch. 3) that all Israel have a share in the World to Come even if they sinned, etc., and these are the ones who do not have a share... In what case is it said that each of these has no share in the World to Come? When he dies without *teshuvah*. But if he repented from his wickedness, etc., even if he **denied the fundamental principles all his days and repented at the end** (*Yerushalmi, Peah*, ch. 1), he has a share in the World to Come.

He adds further: All the wicked and the apostates and the like who repented, etc., even in secret, etc., even though he is still a rebel, for he **repented in secret and not in public**, they accept his *teshuvah*. End quote.

2) Beyond this: One who did not repent even in secret, but died in his wickedness—is there a remedy for him?

Our Sages said (*Sanhedrin* 104a) that "a son grants merit to his father," meaning that if the son is righteous, he brings his father—**who has already died** and should have been counted among those who have no share in the World to Come—to the life of the World to Come. This is true even without prayer on the part of the son, for through prayer, the father also grants merit to the son, as is written in the second answer in *Tosafos* (*Sotah* 10b).

Furthermore, even the efforts and prayers of others, who are not his relatives, are effective, as is stated in *Chagigah* (15b) that *R' Yochanan* helped *Elisha Acher* (and even brought him to *Gan Eden*), even though he was not his relative nor his student.

—Though the prayer of others is not as effective as the prayer of a son or father, for there are many levels in prayer depending on the person praying, the place of prayer, and more. This is not the place to elaborate.

Another proof that the prayer of others is effective even after death is from the *Sifri* at the end of *Parshas Shoftim*, that **all** those who left Egypt who had already died have atonement through the elders of the *Beis Din* of **one** city who would bring the *eglah arufah*. See the end of *Sefer Chassidim* and the commentator there on this.

One could potentially distinguish this from our case, arguing that there the *Beis Din* are the agents of the entire city, and the sin occurred in that city; thus, they are merely removing the sin from those who left Egypt and atoning for them for the sin committed by those they represent.

However, this does not seem to be the case, since they learn from this *Sifri* to give *tzedakah* on behalf of the dead, as is stated in *Orach Chaim* (end of 621), and it is the custom of Israel to give even for the dead who are not their relatives.

In any event, it is not exactly similar to our case, for there it refers to **righteous** dead, where we assume that if they were alive, they would have given to *tzedakah*. But for the wicked, it is not effective, as the *Magen Avraham* writes there.

3) Beyond this: One who is among those who have no share in the World to Come, and he did not repent, and they did not pray for him, and they did not give *tzedakah* for him—he has no share in the World to Come only if he was not punished after his death. But if he was punished, the punishment saves him and is effective for him. As our Sages said (*Sanhedrin* 47a), "It is a good sign for the dead that he is punished after his death" (for he receives atonement thereby, *Rashi*). And even for the most severely wicked, it is effective, as is stated there (103b) that *Yehoyakim* was worthy of being counted with *Yeravam, Achav, and Menashe*—and in fact, he angered [Hashem] even more than *Menashe*—but he received atonement because he was disgraced after his death.

Greater than this, we find in the *Yerushalmi* (*Kilayim*, ch. 9) that even *Yeravam* and his colleagues, whom they counted among those who have no share in the World to Come—through the fact that, many years after their death, their bodies were burned, the attribute of justice was satisfied, and combined with the merit of the Land, they will merit the Resurrection.

—One should not ask: If so, why are *Yeravam* and his colleagues counted in the *Mishnah* as having no share in the World to Come, even though they were atoned for later, while *Yehoyakim* was not counted?

Because they are not similar: In the case of *Yehoyakim*, the "burial of a donkey" was a decree **upon him** for the commission of the sin, and it was already decreed upon him in his lifetime. This is not the case with *Yeravam* and his colleagues, for the punishment of burning was not upon them, but rather **upon the Land of Israel**, and it happened after many years; they were merely buried there, and **consequently** their bodies were also burned. Therefore, **until that time, and from their own perspective**, the status of having no share in the World to Come applied to them.

***

**B.** After we have established the **possibility** of the matter, we can bring proof that it **will** indeed be so—that every single Jew, whoever he may be, will eventually unite with his root and source. This is as follows:

We established that *teshuvah* is effective for everything. Our Sages said (*Rambam, Hilchos Teshuvah*, 7:5, and according to the opinion of *R' Yehoshua* in *Sanhedrin* 97b): "The Torah has already **promised** that Israel will eventually repent at the end of their exile."

Now, one might say that in this case, as in many others, the Torah speaks of the majority—the majority of the Jewish people—and this is no proof that **every single** Jew, even the completely wicked, will repent. But the matter is explained in *Eruvin* (21b), where it says: "The good figs are the completely righteous; the bad figs are the completely wicked. And lest you say their hope is lost and their prospects are nullified, the verse says, 'The mandrakes give forth fragrance'—both these and those will eventually give forth fragrance."

From the fact that it says they will give forth fragrance, it is proof that one cannot say that their judgment is simply finalized and they will be neither alive nor judged, dwelling in neither good nor evil—as the *Tosafos* (*Bava Metzia* 58b) writes. See also *Shabbos* (88b) on the verse, "While the king is in his chamber, my nard gives forth its fragrance," and *Rashi* (Song of Songs 7:14) explains: "The mandrakes give forth fragrance—the good ones and the bad ones... these are the sinners of Israel... **all** seek Your face, and at our doors are all manner of precious things—**we have much reward for mitzvos**." End quote. This is as mentioned above, that even the sinners of Israel have a share in the World to Come because they are **full of mitzvos like a pomegranate.**

Further there in *Eruvin* (19a), the verse (Isaiah at the end) "They shall go out and see... and their fire shall not be quenched" refers to the sinners of the nations of the world. But the sinners of Israel are only liable for that time in *Gehinnom*, and *Avraham Avinu* comes and takes them out (meaning he finalizes their judgment. And furthermore) **he receives them**, except for a Jew who had relations with a non-Jewish woman, etc. And even regarding this, *Tosafos* (*Bava Metzia* 58b) explains that the intention is that a Jew who had relations with a non-Jewish woman does not ascend immediately, but stays there for twelve months.

However, this proof can be refuted based on what is written in *Tosafos* (end of *Chagigah*) that it does not refer to the sinners of Israel in their bodies. Yet, this does not contradict the *Tosafos* in *Chagigah* as to why he explains the verse in Isaiah in *Eruvin* as referring to the sinners of the nations and not the sinners of Israel in their bodies, for that is a more expansive interpretation, and it is forced. The words of the aforementioned *Tosafos* remain difficult, compared to *Tosafos* (*Rosh Hashanah* 17a).

Now, the fundamental principle **from Scripture** that every single Jew will attach to his root is what is said (II Samuel 14:14): "And he devises thoughts so that no one is banished from him." This is cited in the *Shulchan Aruch* of the *Alter Rebbe*, *Hilchos Talmud Torah* (ch. 4, sec. 3): "A wicked person will repent in this incarnation or in another incarnation, as it is written, 'For no one is banished from him.'" And in *Tanya* (end of ch. 39): "**For surely** he will eventually repent in this incarnation or in another incarnation, for no one is banished from him." See also below on this.

(The *Ramban* in *Shaar HaGemul*, "V'achshav Nachzor," writes: "No one is banished from him—except for those who do not stand in judgment, for they are cut off and lost there.")

***

**C.** When we delve into the reason for this, it will be understood that it is **necessarily** so.

I will copy here—since it is not a common book—the language of *Emek HaMelech* (at the beginning, *Shaar Tikunei HaTeshuvah*, end of ch. 3): "And now, children, listen to me, I will teach you the fear of Hashem and His holy love, with us, children of the Living G-d. Why does He trouble Himself so much with these wicked people who anger Him at every moment and every second? There are two answers... The first answer... even though they are completely wicked, etc., there are sparks of holiness in them, etc., for they are 'a shoot of My planting,' etc., and it is a part of G-d **that is eternal**, etc. And the souls are an impression of the light of His Essence, and all that He breathes, He breathes from His Essence... And another second reason: 'My handiwork to be glorified,' etc. The Holy One is, and His handiwork is **alive and exists forever and ever, and it is impossible that it be nullified**, etc."

"The second answer is the benefit of the prayer of *Avraham Avinu*, etc. And the Holy One showed him *Gehinnom* and the subjugation of kingdoms so that through them all these lost ones would be refined and whitened, etc., for His mercies have not ceased over all His creatures."

Similar things are written there in *Shaar Olam HaTohu*, ch. 31.

He also writes (*Shaar Abba v'Imma*, end of ch. 46): "So that no one is banished from him, etc. And why so much? Because the Holy One Himself built worlds and destroyed them, so that there would be good and evil in the world; the evil grew so strong in them that they inherit *Gehinnom*, etc. And because He caused the damage, He brings down to *Sheol* and brings up, and raises them, etc. And they will go from strength to strength until they arrive, after a long time, **to be counted with the righteous**, etc."

In *Midrash Shmuel* at the beginning of *Pirkei Avos*, in the commentary on the *Mishnah* "All Israel," he writes: "The World to Come mentioned here is the era of the Resurrection. And Hashem will not take the soul of the wicked until, after many days, He finds it purified, and then it is hidden in the partition of the righteous, etc. And so it is in this way for all souls until they are all rectified, etc. And this is what the verse says, 'And Your people are all righteous'—meaning **necessarily** they will all be righteous, because He, blessed be He, devised thoughts so that no one is banished from him." End quote.

Similar things are in the *Alshich*, *Parshas Shemini*.

The foundation for the above is in the *Likutei HaShas* of the *AriZal* on *Pirkei Avos*: "All Israel have a share in the World to Come, etc., only that one will rectify himself in a short time and another in a long time, but their end is to be counted with the righteous. And for this reason, the Holy One, as it were, troubles Himself with such wicked people to rectify them, etc. And why so? Because they are 'a shoot of My planting,' which is eternal, and they are an impression of the light of His Essence, and all that He breathes, He breathes from His Essence." End quote.

See also the *Ramban* in *Shaar HaGemul* (his words are brought below), who wrote: "The soul, which is superior, **it is impossible** for it to be nullified and lost, etc."

***

**D.** After it has been explained in the previous sections: a) that it is **possible** for every single Jew, whoever he may be, to merit the Resurrection; b) that it is explained in many places that it **will** be so; c) that it is **necessarily** so,

We will now resolve the sayings of our Sages that appear to contradict the above.

Some of these sayings will be explained here, and from them, the rest will be understood:

1) We learned (*Sanhedrin* 90a): "All Israel have a share in the World to Come... and these are the ones who do not have a share."

Even according to what was established in section A, that *teshuvah*, punishment after death, or prayer and the like are effective for them to merit the World to Come,

Still, those of this category who did not repent, were not punished, and for whom no one prayed, will not rise in the Resurrection—

—And this is indeed what is written in the *drush* "L'havin Biur Inyan HaAvos" (cited in section A), that all Israel have a share in the World to Come in the Resurrection, except **for those whom the Sages enumerated**—

And this contradicts what was established in section C, that every soul **necessarily** is eternal and cannot be nullified because it is "a shoot of My planting," etc., and will eventually be counted with the righteous. Just as there is not even one soul that is not, *ch"v*, a "shoot of My planting" and "handiwork," etc., so too it is impossible that there be even one soul that will be lost and not rise in the Resurrection.

It is a great stretch to say that such a person—who is of the type that has no share in the World to Come, and will not be punished, and no one will pray for him, etc.—never existed and will never exist—even though regarding several matters, including those explained at length in Scripture and the *Shas*, our Sages said they never existed and will never exist (*Sanhedrin* 71a).

—But in truth, there is no contradiction here. For the Resurrection mentioned everywhere refers to the soul with the body, both together, as mentioned at the beginning of this *maamar*.

And those whom the Sages enumerated as having no share in the World to Come—it means that their body is consumed and lost, but the soul, which is a "shoot of My planting," etc., will rise in the Resurrection **in another body**. This is explained in *Shaar HaGilgulim*, Introduction 11, and in *Sefer HaGilgulim*, ch. 5: "If the spark (the individual soul)... committed one of those sins **for which their bodies** are consumed and lost and have no Resurrection, then since that body is consumed, the spark... is reincarnated in that second body, and it will rise in the Resurrection with **all the parts of the spark**, and the first body is lost and cut off."

2) (*Taanis* 7a): *R' Avahu* said, "The day of rain is greater than the Resurrection of the Dead, for the Resurrection is for the righteous, while rain is for both the righteous and the wicked." And even though he concludes there that it is a dispute with *R' Yosef*, the fact that the *Rambam* brings this opinion of *R' Avahu* (in his commentary on the *Mishnah*, "All Israel") implies that the *halachah* is according to him. If so, this contradicts the conclusion above that everyone will rise in the Resurrection. The contradiction is even greater according to the version in *Taanis* (ibid.): "For the Resurrection is for the **completely** righteous" (so it is brought in *Sefer HaIkkarim*, 4:31, and *Sefer Avodas HaKodesh*, pt. 2, ch. 42), and especially according to what is written in *Tanya* (ch. 10 and 14) explaining the nature of a "completely righteous person," regarding whom *R' Shimon bar Yochai* said, "I saw the people of the upper chamber, and they are few," etc., and it is a "taste of the World to Come," etc.

However, the statement of *R' Avahu* requires explanation so that it does not contradict the *Mishnah* that "all Israel have a share in the World to Come," and he does not exclude from the *Mishnah* anything other than one who says there is no Resurrection from the Torah, etc.

Therefore, we must say that the "righteous" referred to by *R' Avahu* are the righteous of the verse "And Your people are all righteous," which refers to all Israel, except for those whom the Sages enumerated, as the commentators have written several reasons why all Israel are righteous. **And according to** what was written in section C, we can add an explanation: that before they merit the Resurrection, they will be refined, whitened, and purified from their sin until they reach the level of the righteous, and only then will they inherit the land.

It follows that all who have a share in the World to Come will reach the level of the completely righteous (and as mentioned in *Tanya* that a completely righteous person is a "taste of the World to Come") beforehand, and afterwards they will rise in the Resurrection. Thus, the statement of *R' Avahu* is explained in accordance with the above.

3) Regarding *kareis* for idolatry and the like, our Sages said (*Sanhedrin* 64b): "That soul shall be cut off—cut off in this world, cut off in the World to Come." And the *Rambam* (*Teshuvah*, 8:1) wrote: "The wicked, etc., will be cut off and die, etc. He is cut off in his wickedness and lost like a beast, and this is *kareis*," etc.

And even though the *Ramban* in *Shaar HaGemul* (his words are brought with a slight change in language in the commentary on the *Rambam* there) does not hold this view, as he wrote: "The *kareis*, etc.—this soul, which is superior, it is impossible for it to be nullified and lost, nor to return to being beastly and join the four elements, etc. (rather, the soul after death) is drawn in its consciousness to ascend and attach to the higher realms like all other things whose nature is to return (to their source), and the thickness of the coarseness and the coarseness of the sins that separated between it and its Creator prevent it, etc. And this is the matter of *kareis*, which is to say that it is cut off from its source."

However, even he writes there: "And the completely, severely wicked who are judged **for generations upon generations**, etc., as it is written, 'For their worm shall not die,' etc."

His intention here is regarding the heretics, informers, and *apikorsim*, etc., regarding whom our Sages said (*Rosh Hashanah* 17a) that they descend to *Gehinnom* and are judged there for generations upon generations, etc. *Gehinnom* is consumed, but they are not consumed.

—See *Likutei Torah* of the *AriZal*, *Parshas Bo*, *Sefer HaLikutim, Parshas Lech Lecha*, *Sefer HaGilgulim*, ch. 6: "The matter of *kareis* is only in the part of the *nefesh*, etc. However, the *ruach* and *neshamah*, etc., are not in *kareis*." (Note also *Emek HaMelech*, *Shaar Olam HaTohu*, ch. 63).

But it has already been explained in *Sefer Asarah Maamaros* (*Maamar Chikkur Din*, pt. 5, ch. 1), where he lists six groups for the Day of Judgment, and the aforementioned are in the sixth group. He concludes: "*Gehinnom* is locked before them, and they are judged in it for generations upon generations, etc. After generations upon generations, etc., it is possible that they too will be examined in the hidden wisdom of the One who devises thoughts so that no one is banished from him. And this is the reason for 'Gehinnom is consumed, but they are not consumed,' which we interpret as the Sages interpreted the verse 'His arrows He made drunk with them'—just as there the arrows are consumed and it is the ultimate of suffering, so too here *Gehinnom* is consumed and it is the ultimate of punishment, for the arrows and *Gehinnom* will not cease all the days that He is angry with them and rebuking them. However, in the end, they are not consumed (they will all be rectified in the general rectification, he explains), etc. And in truth, there is nothing eternal except in the attribute of goodness (unlike suffering and *Gehinnom*, which are consumed, he explains)." End quote.

And similar to all the above is also in *Sefer Emek HaMelech* (*Shaar Tikunei HaTeshuvah*, ch. 3), where he writes regarding the most severely wicked: "They are completely banished, etc., until the time comes for His word, blessed be He, in His great and abundant mercies, for He acts so that no one is banished from Him. And when the time of His visitation comes, blessed be He, He raises them little by little to rectify them and refine them. First, He reincarnates, etc. And so is the secret of *kareis*—did you think that the soul would receive complete consumption? It is not so, but its meaning is that it is cut off from the source of life and reincarnated, etc."

And there in *Shaar Kiryat Arba*, ch. 152, he adds: "After the days of *Mashiach*, the Holy One will renew His world, and even the place of *Gehinnom* will be purified and sanctified, and it will be added to the borders of *Gan Eden* with the wicked sinners of Israel who are within it, etc. The arrows of *Gehinnom* are consumed, and it will be purified with the holiness of the Garden, and there will be the dance of the Holy One with the righteous."

4) (*Pesachim* 54a): "The light that the Holy One created on the second day of creation has no eternal extinguishing (which is the light of *Gehinnom*, *Rashi*)." Seemingly, this contradicts the above.

But it has already been explained in *Asarah Maamaros* (*Maamar Chikkur Din*, pt. 5, ch. 5) and in *Emek HaMelech* (*Shaar Sha'ashuei HaMelech*, ch. 1): "And what *R' Yehudah* said, 'Gehinnom has no eternal extinguishing,' he does not mean to say that it will not cease eternally. As long as this world exists, it will not be extinguished, but when the Holy One destroys this world and nullifies the evil, and it will all be *Shabbos* and rest for the life of the World to Come, then *Gehinnom* will also be nullified."

5) (*Rosh Hashanah* 17a): "The sinners of Israel in their bodies, etc., after twelve months their bodies are consumed, and their **souls** are burned, and a wind scatters them under the soles of the feet of the righteous."

Seemingly, this implies that there will be no Resurrection for their souls either.

But the *Ramban* in *Shaar HaGemul* explains: "Their souls are burned and become ash, meaning that their form is nullified from what it was, like a thing that is burned and turns to ash. And the wind of the Holy One, blessed be He—a wind of rest and favor—scatters them under the soles of the feet of the righteous, meaning in a level that is lower than the delight of the righteous and their rest."

Similar to this is in *Asarah Maamaros* (*Chikkur Din*, pt. 5, ch. 7) and in *Emek HaMelech* (*Shaar Abba v'Imma*, ch. 46), which writes regarding this saying of our Sages that they will be ash: "And this is a wondrous promise which contains kindness and truth for the group of the wicked, etc. They will be entirely holy, and in comparison to the righteous who are above them, they are called by way of parable 'ash under the soles of the feet of the righteous.'"

***

**E.** It remains to explain what is not understood regarding the **possibility** of the rectification.

We established that the completely, severely wicked have their rectification through reincarnation. See also *Reishis Chochmah*, *Shaar HaYirah*, end of ch. 13, in the name of his teacher the *Ramak* (and so it is written in *Sefer Shiur Komah*, sec. 84), that reincarnation purifies and completes what *Gehinnom* cannot purify and complete.

If so, it is difficult according to the saying of our Sages that only three times (besides the first time the soul comes down, as written in *Shaar HaGilgulim*, Introduction 4, and in *Sefer HaGilgulim*, ch. 6) does one come in reincarnation. This is in *Zohar Chadash* (*Ki Teitzei*, p. 107), where *R' Shimon* says: "These wicked ones, if *ch"v* they do not become righteous in these three times (that they come in reincarnation), they have no more rectification, and this is 'that soul shall be cut off from before Me,' etc."

And even though this number is specifically for the wicked, while the righteous can be reincarnated many times, as written, "And showing kindness to thousands for those who love Him" (as written in *Tikkunei Zohar*, end of *Tikkun* 32; see in *Shaar* and *Sefer HaGilgulim*—there—the reason for this), in any event, for the severely wicked, after they have come three times in reincarnation and did not rectify their ways, seemingly their hope is lost.

But the matter is explained in many places, among them in the *Shelah* (*Parshas Ki Teitzei*, in the part *Torah Ohr*) in the name of *Maharash Alkabetz*: "And these who are reincarnated, when they did not repent to Hashem in three times, etc., they will no longer be reincarnated as humans, but in animals and beasts, pure and impure, the easiest first. And this is what is said, 'Twice, three times with a man'—from there on, in a beast. And one who did not descend to the depth of the mind of the divine *R' Shimon bar Yochai*, *a"h*, thought that he, *z"l*, distanced him. But one who contemplates his words will understand that he, *z"l*, brought his existence closer." End quote.

—(See also what is written on this in *Tikkunei Zohar*, end of *Tikkun* 32, and in *Gilgulim* there)—

And in *Emek HaMelech* (*Shaar Tikunei HaTeshuvah*, ch. 1) he writes: "'With a man'—specifically, that he will no longer come in the reincarnation of a human until he wanders as a fugitive and a wanderer on the earth, and then he will be reincarnated in the inanimate, vegetative, animate, or speaking, or in a reincarnation of demons and spirits, etc. And it is under the source of life, and this is what is said, 'That soul shall be cut off from before Me,' etc., for other punishments were decreed upon them that are harder than *Gehinnom* (and afterwards they are twelve months in *Gehinnom*). And there is hope for his end after he receives his punishment, for His mercies have not ceased over all His creatures." End quote.

***

I will conclude with what is written in *Emek HaMelech* (*Shaar Reisha d'Ze'er Anpin*, end of ch. 43): "Blessed be Hashem, the G-d of *Avraham*, the man of kindness, who did not cease His kindness and truth from His people Israel, so that no one is banished from Him. For His mercies have not ceased over all His creatures, as it is said, 'And His mercies are over all His works.' Thus, all Israel have a share in the World to Come, as it is said, 'And Your people are all righteous; they shall inherit the land forever, the shoot of My planting, the work of My hands, to be glorified.'"

With the blessing of "Immediately to *Teshuvah*, immediately to *Geulah*,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 86

B”H, Thursday, 19 Tammuz, 5705

To our dear friend, the distinguished *avreich*, G-d-fearing, etc.,
The *Tamim*,
Rabbi Menachem Zev, may he live, Gringlas

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 5th of Tammuz and the previous correspondence:

1) I have written to R’ Y. Weinberg, and it has surely been received by now. I prompted him regarding the continuation of the list of memories, which was interrupted at its beginning; after all, forgetfulness is common, etc.

2) We received $22.75 some time ago from the *Tamim* Yaakov Leman, in his letter of Thursday—26 shekel. I would like to propose the following: Since their debt is growing, and the lack of income from printing matters prevents us from publishing many necessary items, it is appropriate to endeavor to: a) find a donor who will settle the old debt, or at least most of it; b) find donors who will take upon themselves the cost of printing a *kuntres*, *sicha*, a new *shmuessen* 1 or 2, and the like (and, of course, the name of the donor will be printed, as we did with the second *kuntres* of *michtavim*, *Chanoch L’Naar*, etc.). Surely, together with his fellow *Temimim*, may they live, you will find a way to bring the above from potential into action.

3) The package with the letters to Klatskin was returned to us for some reason, but we have already sent it again. We are puzzled as to why he has not yet received it. When distributing them, **please do not forget to erase** from the cover the words "To Dr. Klatskin."

4) Regarding the copying of the *maamar* from the *Kodesh HaKodoshim* "Why Mashiach Does Not Come" and its distribution: when I know the opinion of *K’vod K’dushat Moreinu V’Rabbeinu* (may his merit shield us) on this question, I will write to you.

5) Thank you for the negotiations with the newspaper agent regarding the distribution of our publications, and we hope to hear of good results in practice.

6) Enclosed is a membership card for *Mishnayos B’al Peh* for R’ Ch. Sh. Greengart (it would be good if he would inform us each time whether it is necessary to write the title "Rabbi," etc.), and why he has not yet received his own.

7) I received the *R.D. D’Chaf-Pey*, and I am enclosing the *R.D.* of 19 Kislev 5705—which is unedited—on the condition that it be returned, of course.

8) Regarding the list of *kuntresim* that you sent via the *Tamim* Glushtein, may he live, he has already been informed that they are not available. If they are received, he will be notified.

9) Of the books by R’ Y.A. Margolies, I only have the *sefer Amudei Arazim*. See there 3a regarding the *kufita d’chamra* mentioned in the *sicha* of 19 Kislev mentioned above, and on page 43a regarding the *Tzemach Tzedek*. I have not seen his other books. Does he have any copies?

10) *K’vod K’dushat Moreinu V’Rabbeinu* (may his merit shield us) will likely travel to rest in the same place as last year.

11) The *shmuessen* for the new month of Tammuz were sent to you before your letter reached us, and for that reason, they were sent as you wrote in your first letter... of each one. Please inform us immediately how many to send for the new month of Av.

12) Just today, a limited quantity of the *sefer Chachmei Yisrael B’Shem Tov* reached our possession. The price is 85 cents; without the cover and the letter—75 cents.

13) We sent you one *tallis katan* and one *mitznefes* as a sample. The *Tamim* R’ Z., may he live, Schechter has begun to handle this based on a letter he received from you, and I am satisfied with this, because for several reasons it is appropriate that the negotiations regarding this, and the entire *tallis katan* business in general, should be conducted without our involvement.

14) Has anything new developed regarding the request of Barenholtz?

15) Regarding the matters of the *Kodesh HaKodoshim*, it has been passed on to the editorial board.

16) On this occasion, I reiterate that there are still some of his friends, and especially some of the *baalei batim* and *Anash* in your camp, who have not yet participated in the writing of the *Sefer Torah*.

17) How is the situation regarding the Shabbos parties, *Beis Rivkah*, and the work at the camp during the summer days?

18) We will send the *bentsherlach* to you, G-d willing, this week.

19) "Seferenu" parts one and five have been published. You will receive samples along with the *bentsherlach*. Enclosed is a review regarding them; it is appropriate to publish it in the press in your country. When you find it appropriate, you are authorized to allocate from the *Melach* fund a modest sum for an advertisement at the appropriate time according to the conditions of your country (whether now or before the start of the study term).

20) We sent you a sample of "Shema Yisrael," the price of which is 15 cents, and it is strange that you did not confirm its receipt. We are also sending you a sample of "Chanoch L’Naar," the price of which is 30 cents.

We await a response regarding the above.

To conclude with a matter from the *parsha* of this Shabbos: Our Sages, of blessed memory (*Berachos* 12b), sought to establish the recitation of the *Parshas Balak* in the *Krias Shema*, etc., because it contains the verse, "He crouches, he lies down like a lion," etc. In another version, the text reads, "Behold, the people shall rise like a lioness and lift itself up like a lion." According to what is written in *Tanchuma* on this verse: "They rise from their sleep, they stand like lions, they snatch the *Krias Shema*, and they crown the Holy One, blessed be He, etc."

To understand the precision of the comparison to a lion specifically, and its relevance to *Krias Shema*—see *Tosefta* of *Sheviis* (end of chapter 6) that "snatching" is a trait of a wolf, and so it is also in *Bereishis Rabbah* (ch. 97).

However, the essence of *Krias Shema* is the *yichud* of the Name, and that one crowns the Holy One, blessed be He, which is the opposite of the logic of "two powers," G-d forbid.

When one contemplates the true meaning of the *yichud* (as explained in *Shaar HaYichud V’HaEmunah* and elsewhere)—that there is nothing else besides Him and nothing is separate—one arrives at the point that **in every thing and matter**, one should utilize it for the service of his Creator. Therefore, one comes immediately to "And you shall love the L-rd your G-d with all your heart"—with both your inclinations (*Berachos* 54a), even with the *yetzer hara* (*Likutei Torah*, *d’h Shema Yisrael*). This is similar to what the Rambam writes in *Hilchos Deos* (ch. 3, halacha 3): "One who walks in this path all his days serves G-d constantly, etc., even at the time that he is intimate, etc.," even though our Sages said (*Yoma* 69b) that were it not for the *yetzer hara*, the heat would cease (see the difficulty in *Torah Or*, *d’h U’Mordechai Yatza*). This is understood more subtly from the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov on the verse, "When you see the donkey of... you shall surely help him." This is the comparison to the lion, for our Sages said (*Bava Kamma* 16b) that it is the lion's way to eat only from the living and not after death. This means that even with the *yetzer hara*, one fulfills "And you shall love the L-rd your G-d." See also *Bava Metzia* (84a): "Your strength"—this very power through which he went down to the Jordan—is for the sake of Torah.

Therefore, the reward for "They rise like a lioness," etc., is *midah k’neged midah*: "He crouches, etc., who shall rouse him?" Since he fulfilled "And you shall love" even within the *yetzer hara*, there is peace in his "small city," and consequently, there is peace in the world as well.

Note the *Taz* (*Orach Chaim*, end of 585) regarding the interpretation of the *Rosh* on the *shofar*. See *Ohr HaTorah* on the verse "And I will put enmity," etc. (section 3); apparently, this is a higher level, and the aforementioned is related to what is explained in the *drushim* of *Parah Adumah* regarding "with both your inclinations," and therefore he did not refer in *Ohr HaTorah* to these *drushim*.

See also *Likutei Torah*, *d’h V’Ahavta* (end of section 2 and section 3).

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

**M. Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 87

B"H, Monday, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5703

To our dear friend, a man of action, wise and understanding, etc.,
The Tamim, R' Hillel Halevi, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

We acknowledge with thanks the receipt of your letters and all that was enclosed with them. You have surely received the letter from our secretary in the meantime.

We have noted to send the "Shmuessen" to everyone for whom you requested them. Likewise, subscription cards for "Mishnayos Be'al Peh" have been sent, as you requested—and whoever adds [to their efforts], more is added to them.

The price of "Chinuch LaNa'ar" is 30 cents.

Thank you for your promise to speak with the directors of the Talmud Torah regarding our books; if they purchase a large quantity, they will receive a discount of 20-30 percent.

We are enclosing a circular from the Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch to educational institutions regarding our books. Perhaps you would be so kind as to provide us with the addresses of all the Talmud Torahs and other educational institutions in your city, so that we may send the circular to them as well.

In accordance with our conversation regarding the necessity of acquiring permanent subscribers for all "Kehot" publications, we are sending you subscription sheets, and we trust they will help you fulfill your promise in this matter, B'ezras Hashem.

If you would like to donate the duplicate copy of the sefer "LeMenachem" you have to the Kehot library, we thank you in advance.

Thank you for your suggestion regarding the conclusion of the letter from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, concerning the closing of the door, where it should say, "and afterwards he can close it." If I learn anything further about this, I will inform you.

And to conclude with a matter related to this Shabbos:

Regarding whether the tribe of Levi also participated in the war against Midian, there are two versions in the Sifri—cited in Yalkut Shimoni—on the verse "for all the tribes of Israel": 1) "For all"—to exclude the tribe of Levi, meaning they did not go out to war. 2) "For all"—to include the tribe of Levi. This is also the version of Rashi, who copied it as such in his commentary on this verse.

One can suggest a hint regarding avodah: It is stated in the Rambam (end of Hilchos Shemitah V'Yovel) that the tribe of Levi does not engage in war like the rest of Israel. If so, why was this war different?

This is understood based on what is explained in the discourses of *Hechalutzu* (in Likkutei Torah and in the discourses of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *Reshimot* 5709, and see *Hayom Yom*, page 74), that the war against the seven nations in avodah refers to the seven evil traits—the coarseness of evil—and the conquest was to settle in their land and to be a person who plows, a person who sows, etc. Consequently, the Levites were separated from the affairs of the world (Rambam, ibid.), and their role is "They shall teach Your judgments to Yaakov and Your Torah to Yisrael" (Devarim 33:10), which is incompatible with being a person who plows and sows (see Berachos 35b). They have no connection, from their own perspective, to worldly matters or to the coarseness of evil.

This is unlike Midian, where the war was not to conquer a place for settlement, but to "wreak the vengeance of Hashem," as the Ramban writes (Bamidbar 31:23, etc.). In terms of avodah, this refers to the subtlety of evil; therefore, even the Levite must gird himself for this war.

With this, we can also understand another difference between the war against Midian and other wars: in this war, there were one thousand from each tribe, equally, regardless of whether the tribe was large in population or small.

The reason is simple, based on the above: in a war of conquest, in order to inherit the land—"to the many you shall increase his inheritance"—the tribe that was numerous needed to increase its soldiers as well. Based on what was explained above, the matter is understood in avodah: overt evil depends on a large degree of involvement in worldly matters—the 39 labors of the weekdays—unlike the subtlety of evil, which is found even among those who serve Hashem (see *Hechalutzu* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe).

However, it is a difficult task to eradicate the subtlety of evil (as is evident from the length and difficulty of this final exile, which is incomparable to the Babylonian exile). Therefore, the war must be conducted specifically according to the instruction of Moshe Rabbeinu (and the extension of Moshe in every generation, and especially in the final exile, the generation of the footsteps of Mashiach, as stated in Tikkunei Zohar, Tikkun 69, and in Likkutei Torah of the Arizal, Parshas Va'eschanan), and the going to war must be in a manner of "and they were armed" (Vayimseru)—with mesiras nefesh (Sifri, cited in Yalkut Shimoni). Through this, not one man was missing in the war, and all will enter Eretz Yisrael through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days.

With the blessing of "Immediately to Teshuvah, Immediately to Geulah,"

**M. Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 88

88

*[Another version of the above, beginning of Menachem Av 5703?]*

To conclude with a point regarding this Shabbos:

Regarding whether the tribe of Levi also participated in the war against Midian, there are two versions in the Sifri—cited in Yalkut Shimoni—on the verse "for all the tribes of Israel": 1) "For all"—to exclude the tribe of Levi, meaning they did not go out to war; 2) "For all"—to include the tribe of Levi. This is also the version of Rashi, who copied it as such in his commentary on this verse.

It can be explained that, as the Rambam rules (at the end of Hilchos Shemitah V'Yovel), the tribe of Levi does not engage in war like the rest of Israel. If so, we must ask: why was this war different?

The reason is simple: the war against the seven nations was a conquest for the purpose of settling in their land, to be a person who plows, a person who sows, etc. Consequently, the Leviim, who were set apart from worldly matters (Rambam, ibid.) and whose role is "they shall teach Your judgments to Yaakov and Your Torah to Yisrael" (Devarim 33:10)—which is contradicted by being a person who plows and sows (see Berachos 35b)—have no connection, in their own essence, to these material matters.

This is not the case with Midian, where the war was not to conquer a place of settlement (for it was only afterward that the tribes of Reuven, etc., came). Rather, it was to "take the vengeance of Hashem." As the Ramban writes (Bamidbar 31:23), even the Levi must arm himself for this war.

With this we can also understand another difference between the war of Midian and other wars: in this war, there were one thousand from each tribe, equally from all the tribes, regardless of whether they were numerous in population or few in population. This is understood based on the above: in a war of conquest to inherit the land—where "to the many you shall increase his inheritance"—the tribe that is numerous also needed to increase its soldiers. This is not the case in a war of the vengeance of Hashem.

One can suggest a hint here regarding a person’s avodah to his Creator, based on what is explained in the discourses on "arm yourselves" (*hachalatzu*) (in Likutei Torah and the year 5659): the war against the seven nations represents the conquest of the seven evil character traits, the "coarseness of evil." Therefore, the tribe of Levi—"and not the tribe of Levi alone, but every single person... whose spirit moved him" (avodah of the heart) and who "understood with his mind" (avodah of the intellect) to set himself apart to stand before Hashem to serve Him and minister to Him (Rambam, ibid.)—has no connection to such a war. This is not the case with Midian, whose subject is the "subtlety of evil," as discussed in the aforementioned maamarim; even the Levi, and his counterpart in all Bnei Yisrael, must arm himself and go out to war.

However, it is a difficult avodah to eradicate the subtlety of evil (as is evident from the length and difficulty of this final galus, which is incomparable to the galus of Bavel). Therefore, this war must be conducted specifically according to the instruction of Moshe Rabbeinu (and the extension of Moshe in every generation, especially in this final galus, the generation of the footsteps of Moshiach, as stated in Tikkunei Zohar, Tikkun 21, and in the Likutei Torah of the Arizal on Parshas Va'eschanan). Furthermore, going to this war must be in a manner of "and they were delivered" with mesiras nefesh (Sifri, cited in Yalkut Shimoni).

Therefore, the reward is also measure for measure: just as the departure is without regard for intellect, but rather with mesiras nefesh, so too the victory is above the way of nature, for not even one man was missing in the war. And all of them will enter Eretz Yisrael through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days.

With the blessing of "and may you be remembered for good," may you and your family live, and may you be remembered for good, the honorable Rabbi and Chossid, etc., Moreinu Harav Y. (may he live), and may we merit immediate teshuvah and immediate geulah.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 89

B"H, Sunday, 7th of Menachem Av, 5705

To the distinguished, G-d-fearing, and esteemed activist, a man of many accomplishments, etc.,
R' Shmuel Palmer, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Thank you for your inquiry regarding the health of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita. His health is as usual. It is understood that the heat wave prevailing these weeks also causes weakness, and it is a pity that until now he has not been able to travel to a pleasant place to rest and recover somewhat from the work that weighs upon him.

The Healer of all flesh will surely grant him health, and he will go from strength to strength, as will all our friends and anash, may they live.

We acknowledge with thanks the receipt of your check for the sum of 112.50 dollars for the publication of the sichos of the holiday season of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita.

We have also received a similar sum from the distinguished, G-d-fearing, and esteemed R' Yehuda Katz, may he live. We are therefore handing the manuscripts over for printing, and as soon as they are published, they will be sent to you.

In addition to our thanks, we offer a blessing of *mazal tov* that you have merited such an important matter: to be among those who bring merit to the many, to illuminate, with Hashem's help, their souls with the light of the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, and thereby to be aroused to Torah, avodah, and acts of loving-kindness.

Regarding the events of these days in the month of Menachem Av, our Sages of blessed memory stated regarding the cause of the destruction: that the First Beis Hamikdash was destroyed because of the "despising of Torah"—that it was not esteemed in the eyes of the Jews of that generation, even though they were engaged in it (Bava Metzia 85b); and the Second Beis Hamikdash was destroyed because of the sin of baseless hatred (Yoma 9b).

Therefore, we find that the building of the First Beis Hamikdash—whose holiness was complete, unlike the Second, which lacked the Ark, etc. (Yoma 21b)—was built specifically by **Shlomo**. Shlomo was his name because there was peace and tranquility in his days (Divrei Hayamim I 22:9), even with those nations against whom his father Dovid had fought—the complete opposite of baseless hatred.

Furthermore, he taught Torah to the people and strove, through matters of fear of Heaven, that the Jewish people should hold fast to the Torah, as our Sages of blessed memory relate (Eruvin 21b)—the complete opposite of the "despising of Torah."

In every time and place, any person who performs an action to bring merit to the many, out of the *ahavas Yisrael* within him—freely and without ulterior motives—and especially an action that ultimately leads to the strengthening of Torah and Yiddishkeit, brings our redemption closer and the building of the Beis Hamikdash by Moshiach Tzidkeinu, who, when he comes, will also begin with nothing but peace (Vayikra Rabbah, end of ch. 9).

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 91

[9 Menachem Av]

...And to conclude with the lesson of the day: Our Sages, of blessed memory (Bava Metzia 85b; Yerushalmi, Chagigah 1:7), state that although the destruction of the First Beis Hamikdash was caused by sins, had the Torah been precious in their eyes, the light within the Torah would have brought them back to the right path, and the Beis Hamikdash would not have been destroyed. The Second Beis Hamikdash, however, was destroyed because of baseless hatred, as is stated in Yoma (9b).

Now, in these *ikvesa d’Meshicha*—the footsteps of Moshiach—when, as our Sages have said (Sanhedrin 97b), all the appointed times have passed and the matter depends only on *teshuvah* and good deeds, it is incumbent upon each and every one of us, in our respective places of residence, to strive with greater intensity and vigor in *ahavas Yisrael* and in the cherishing of Torah and *mitzvos*.

These two matters are fulfilled simultaneously when one engages in strengthening Torah and Yiddishkeit among the broadest segments of the Jewish people.

For there is no love greater than this: when one exerts oneself, with *yegias nefesh* and *yegias basar*, to save one’s fellow—for all of Israel are friends—from descending into the pit through sins and transgressions.

And there is no greater importance one can accord the Torah than by clarifying and explaining to each and every person that it is the wisdom and will of the *Ribono shel Olam*, that it is eternal in every time and every place, and that it is through Torah and *mitzvos* that He has planted within us eternal life—here and now.

May the *Ribono shel Olam* hasten our redemption speedily and in reality, through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With the blessing of *l’alter l’teshuvah, l’alter l’geulah*—immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to *geulah*.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

B"H, Wednesday, 10 Menachem Av, 5705

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, honorable, and distinguished, who conducts his business with integrity, R' Y. Katz, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

We gratefully acknowledge receipt of your letter from Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, along with the check for $112.50 for the printing expenses of the sichos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, from the days of Pesach 5705.

We also received a check for the same amount from the esteemed, G-d-fearing, honorable, and distinguished R' S. Palmer, may he live. We are therefore sending the manuscripts to the printer, and as soon as they are published, we will send you the number of copies you request.

In addition to our thanks, we offer our congratulations on having merited such an important matter—to be among those who bring merit to the public, to illuminate, with Hashem’s help, their souls with the light of the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, and to be awakened thereby to Torah, avodah, and acts of kindness.

Regarding the two types of people—those who dwell in the tents of Torah and those who are involved in business—in many respects, the merit of those involved in business is great. This is especially true in this regard: beyond the fact that they themselves study Torah—which is an obligation upon every single person, as stated in the Shulchan Aruch—they also provide the ability for others to engage in Torah study. It is for this reason that Zevulun preceded Yissachar (Rashi on Devarim 33:18; see Bereishis Rabbah, ch. 72).

And the merit is even greater when the act is done freely, without ulterior motives.

This is the essence of ahavas Yisrael: to do good for a fellow Jew, even if one has never seen him (as per the statement of our Alter Rebbe, see Hayom Yom, p. 28), for in such a case, there is no room for ulterior motives.

This is especially relevant to Kohanim, as we say, "and commanded us to bless His people Israel with love"—specifically with love. This blessing extends even to those who are outside the synagogue, even though the Kohen does not know who is there, as is stated in the Shulchan Aruch.

It is known that "through an awakening from below comes an awakening from above," and through tzedakah given **freely**—

—and our Sages of blessed memory stated (Kesuvos 50a) that the effort to provide others with books to study from is considered tzedakah—

—it hastens the Geulah. Regarding the galus and the Geulah, it is said (Yeshayahu 52:3; see Sanhedrin 97b that this refers to our current galus): "You were sold for **nothing**, and you shall be redeemed **without money**."

We must beseech this through the free, unmerited kindness of the Ribono shel Olam, as explained by the Alter Rebbe (Iggeres HaKodesh, ch. 2), that this is the attribute of **Yaakov**, who was not satisfied with the promise he had been given.

And then, our G-d—of whom our Sages said in their metaphorical language (Sanhedrin 39a), "He is a Kohen"—will bless His people Israel with peace. This is the "peace of the kingdom of the House of David" (Bamidbar Rabbah, ch. 11), speedily in our days, through Mashiach ben David.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee
