This memory must evoke a strong desire to do everything in our power to foster **ahavas yisroel chinam**, without any ulterior motive (see *Hayom Yom*, 15 Kislev, regarding what the Alter Rebbe — author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch — said on this). This applies especially to strengthening **chibas haTorah**, which is achieved through explanation — that it is His wisdom, blessed be He — and in general, through *hisorerus* to *yiras shamayim*.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

Chairman of the Vaad Hapoel

#### ***93***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 18, p. 488, and completed based on a copy.

## Side

*[Before 18 Menachem Av, 5703]*

**Divine Providence**

This is an explanation of the various approaches to Divine Providence (Hashgacha Pratis), from the Sages of Israel to the Baal Shem Tov, and the approach of the Baal Shem Tov.

**1. The Approach of the Baal Shem Tov:**

Hashgacha Pratis applies to every single detail of a person’s experiences, **and also to the inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms (domem, tzomeiach, chai).** This approach is cited in Chassidic literature **that I have at hand**: *Shaar HaTeshuvah*, ch. 9; *Maamar* "Es Hashem He'emarta," 5728; *Maamar* "Hateh Elokai," 5734; *Likutei Dibburim*, 19 Kislev 5734, sections 3-4.

In the *Maamar* "Al Kein Yomru" (5736), it adds: "The concept of Hashgacha Pratis as explained by our master, the Baal Shem Tov, is not merely that all the detailed movements of the creatures of every species are under the Hashgacha Pratis of the Creator, may He be blessed—and this Hashgacha Pratis is the life-force and existence of the creature—but furthermore, that a specific movement of a specific creature has a general connection to the overall intent of Creation... A single movement of a specific blade of grass completes the supernal intent regarding Creation."

**Note A.** The discussion regarding Hashgacha Pratis in *Tanya*, *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*, ch. 2, and *Iggeres HaKodesh*, section 25, refers to the concept of Hashgacha Pratis **in general**, as there are those who deny it, and even deny its **possibility**—even though they admit that the entire Creation is brought into being by the word of Hashem from nothingness to being, as is proven by the response there. Their approach is explained elsewhere: they hold that Creation occurred through a process of *hishtalshelus* (evolutionary descent) of cause and effect, where every effect causes a change in its cause. Therefore, they claim it is impossible for Him to be "clothed" in and supervise the lower worlds (*Likutei Torah*, *Maamar* "Shishim Heimah HaSheni," p. 2), as this would be a degradation, and would also cause multiplicity (*Torah Or*, *Maamar* "Ardah Na"). Therefore, in their opinion, one must say "Hashem has forsaken the land," and He is only the "G-d of gods."

For this very reason, they also deny the possibility of miracles (*Torah Or*, *Maamar* "Ve'Eileh Shemos").

Their refutation is that, on the contrary, it is necessary to say that the power of the Creator stands **constantly** within the created thing; if so, He is always present even in the lower worlds. (See *Pelach HaRimon* by R. Hillel of Paritch, *Maamar* "Ardah Na," section 2, regarding this.)

**Note B.** The supervisions of "one eye" upon those who fear Him, "two eyes," and "one eye" which is above the supervision of "two eyes" (*Likutei Torah*, *Maamar* "Ki Tishma BeKol," and elsewhere) differ in the **manner** of the supervision, but not in its **particularity** (according to the Baal Shem Tov’s approach; this is not the case for the approaches that preceded him). Furthermore, all of them are lofty levels of supervision, at the very least a miracle clothed in nature—and therefore even the "one eye" is specifically for those who fear Him. The conduct of nature is below the supervision of the "one eye," and it is, as it were, an attempt to "blind" it (see *Devarim Rabbah*, ch. 42). This is all explained in *Ohr HaTorah*, *Maamar* "Asher Yomar HaYom." One must necessarily interpret it this way also in the *Maamar* "Hateh Elokai" in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Adar 5702, and in other places.

**2. The Approach of the Sages of Israel before the Baal Shem Tov:**

Hashgacha Pratis exists for every individual human being, while for the animal and vegetative kingdoms, there is only **general supervision, over the species.**

The *Moreh Nevuchim* (Part 3, ch. 17) states, after listing several opinions on the matter of supervision:

"The fifth opinion, which is our opinion, meaning our Torah... is that Divine Providence is over the individuals of the human species alone... but other living creatures, and certainly plants... have species-based supervision, not individual... (ch. 18) And thus, Divine Providence will not be equal for all human beings... the foolish who rebel... their state is base and they are arranged in the order of the other individuals of the animal species, 'likened to the beasts that perish'."

In *Shomer Emunim* (by a student of the Ramaz, mentioned in *Shoresh Mitzvas HaTefillah*, section 34), he writes at the end: Nothing happens by chance without Divine intent and supervision, as it is written, "And I will walk with you in *keri* (chance)," implying that even the level of "chance" is attributed to Him, may He be blessed, for everything is from Him through Hashgacha Pratis. However, the details of the supervisions... as I found them in the books of the Kabbalists, and specifically in the book *Elimah*, the species of creatures in this world that are not subject to reward and punishment, which are three categories: animals, plants, and inanimate objects... their supervision is through the "ministers" appointed over each of the species... to influence the species as a whole. However, Hashgacha Pratis, such as whether this specific ox will live or die... the supernal minister has no power to supervise this, and all animals, and certainly the vegetative and inanimate, are not supervised regarding such specific matters, because the intent for them is achieved through their species alone, and there is no need for supervision over their individuals. Therefore, the entire matter of their individuals is by pure chance and not by the decree of the Almighty, unless some matter reaches the supervision of man from this... and the Almighty did not decree upon these fish whether they should die or live...

But He did decree upon this person his food and sustenance... and similarly, there is supervision for a person regarding his animals, such as if his ox will grow fat... if his pitcher will break, etc. (An example of this, regarding what he wrote about fish, is found in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, section 25: "And even though a human being, who has free choice, curses him... and is liable for the evil of his choice, nevertheless, for the victim, it was already decreed from Heaven, and the Omnipresent has many messengers." And in Rambam, end of ch. 6 of *Hilchos Teshuvah*, it is exactly like this case.)

What he brought from the book *Elimah* is in *Elimah Rabbasi* by the Ramak, who wrote there—(see *Ein Kol Tamar*, *Heh*, ch. 1)—as follows: It should not enter the mind of any believer that any action, small or great, could be by way of chance, G-d forbid. Rather, everything is by supernal supervision, and not supervision by created powers, whether angels, thrones, or *Sefiros*, G-d forbid, but everything is in the mystery of the supervision of the *Ein Sof*, etc.

He continues to explain the details of Hashgacha Pratis as mentioned above in *Shomer Emunim*.

Now, to resolve the contradiction between the beginning of the words of the Ramak and *Shomer Emunim*, which state that nothing is by chance, and the end, which states that the matter of individual animals is by pure chance, one could say that to resolve this, *Shomer Emunim* says that even the level of "chance" is attributed to Him, may He be blessed, for everything is from Him through Hashgacha Pratis.

See also Rambam, *Hilchos Teshuvah*, ch. 5, law 4, where he writes: "Know that everything is done according to His will, and even though our actions are entrusted to us, how? Just as the Creator wills that fire and wind should rise upward... so He **wills** that man should have his authority in his hand and all his actions are entrusted to him." And at greater length in ch. 8 of *Shemonah Perakim*.

And to note from *Tosafos* (Niddah 16b): "And this is not in the hands of Heaven, for the Holy One, blessed be He, **does not wish** to change the course of the constellations."

* * *

And let it be known that even according to the aforementioned opinions, while there is no Hashgacha Pratis in the inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms, He **knows** all the details and the details of the details, as stated in *Ikkarim*, Maamar 4, ch. 7: "It is necessary for His knowledge to encompass everything that exists and occurs in the world, and no small or great thing is hidden from Him, but He does not supervise them (the animals) to give reward and punishment for all their actions, but He supervises their details insofar as they are parts of the whole, to preserve the species, and nothing more."

* * *

And one should not ask: how is it possible—even according to this approach—that there could be a matter in the inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms that does not concern man, since they all exist only for the sake of man, as the Rambam elaborated in his introduction to the *Mishnah*?

For it is obvious (that according to this approach, and it is clear, in my humble opinion, that this is also the case according to the Baal Shem Tov’s approach to Hashgacha Pratis) that what the Sages said (*Berachos* 6b), "The entire world was created only to serve this one," refers to the **general** species of the inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms and to the **general** events. But one cannot say that the manner in which a specific leaf falls in the far reaches of the sea concerns this specific person. Just as the Rambam’s intention is not to interpret the statement of Ben Zoma (which he brought there in his introduction), "Blessed is He who created all these to serve me," to mean that every detail of the people ascending to the festival concerned Ben Zoma. See *Likutei Torah*, *Maamar* "VeSamti Kadkod HaSheni," which generally mentions the secondary and the primary in the creation of animals.

* * *

Now, regarding the approach of the Sages of Israel before the Baal Shem Tov, we must clarify:

1) Regarding Hashgacha Pratis in human beings: is it also for the wicked, the nations of the world, and the foolish, or only for the Jewish people, the righteous?

The opinion of the *Moreh Nevuchim* was brought above (see also *Moreh Nevuchim*, Part 3, ch. 51), that it is not for the foolish and the wicked, because supervision is according to one's attachment to the intellect.

According to this, we also learn that according to his view, the removal of Hashgacha Pratis from the wicked is not a punishment or a special decree, but a natural matter.

Seemingly, this is the opinion of the Ramban (*Bereishis* 18:19), who wrote: "His supervision in the lower world is to preserve the general laws, and human beings are also placed within it to chance until the time of their visitation arrives, but for His pious ones, He sets His heart to know him in particular, etc."

See *Derech Chaim*, *Shaar HaTeshuvah*, section 9, which writes: They raise a complaint against the Rambam, for it is written, "Your eyes are open upon all the ways of the sons of man," etc., and likewise, "He who fashions their hearts together," etc., meaning even for the deeds of the wicked, as it is written, "Can a man hide in secret," etc., even though a spirit of folly has entered him like a beast, but the matter is... for the righteous He supervises with kindness and goodness, and for the wicked with the attribute of judgment, etc.

It requires study, according to his view, how to reconcile this with the language of the *Moreh Nevuchim*.

In *Kav HaYashar*, chapter on "Hashgacha," he brings the opinion of the Ramban (above) and the *Bachya*, that Hashgacha Pratis is divided into two: a) To supervise his deeds—this is for everyone, even the nations; b) To protect from chance—this is only for the righteous.

Whether the removal of Hashgacha Pratis from the wicked is a special punishment or a natural matter, according to the *Elimah* and *Shomer Emunim*, requires study. For at the beginning of his words he wrote: "Each one of them (human beings) is supervised by the Almighty with ultimate particularity," and he concludes: "The tenth supervision is the concealment of the face from the Almighty, for because of his sin, Hashem left him to nature and chance... and this is a parable of a spring flowing with water... he who does not wish to ascend to the source of the spring will drink from the murky water (which is at the end)."

2) In the inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms: is there no Hashgacha Pratis at all, or does the minister and constellation appointed over the species supervise even the details?

In *Moreh Nevuchim*, *Elimah*, *Shomer Emunim*, etc., they wrote **explicitly** that the details in the inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms are by pure chance and no created power, etc., as mentioned above.

But in *Kav HaYashar* (above), he challenges the opinion of the Ramban with the *Yerushalmi* (*Sheviis* ch. 9, law 1; also in *Bereishis Rabbah* ch. 75 and elsewhere), where Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai said: "A bird is not caught without Heaven, how much more so the soul of a human being."

**Note.** Seemingly, it is not understood at all what was innovated for Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai by the bird’s being caught; after all, many verses testify to Hashgacha Pratis in human beings. One could say that he teaches us that even in a place of danger it is so, and it is not certain that he will be caught, and the *a fortiori* argument is from the bird, which was also in a place of danger from the hunter. And the fact that "a person should not stand in a place of danger" (*Shabbos* 32a), perhaps one could say that this is different because he has no choice, for it is impossible to remain in the cave all the days of the decree, as he does not know when it will be nullified, and his flesh has become rusty. Therefore, it is not similar to "thorns and snares" (*Kesuvos* 32a).

- (And one cannot say—as written in the *Chiddushei HaRadal*—that even if you say there is no Hashgacha Pratis in animals, it is different here because the profit of the hunter depends on this: a) because if so, it is not applicable to say that a decree from Heaven goes out for **this specific bird** that it should be caught, as written in *Elimah* and *Shomer Emunim* above; b) because if so, Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai should not have made the *a fortiori* argument from a bird to a human, but from the profit of sustenance to the soul of a human.)

He answers that this refers to the minister, and the minister supervises even the details.

I have not found a colleague for his opinion, for the time being.

3) According to the aforementioned Kabbalists, since in the matter of *gilgul* (reincarnation) some are reincarnated into the inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms, seemingly it is clear that in such inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms **there is** Hashgacha Pratis.

**4. If there are any of the Jewish researchers and sages—who preceded the Baal Shem Tov—who held the approach of Hashgacha Pratis even in the inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms.**

In *Chinuch Mitzvah* 169, he wrote: "There are sects of people who think that the supervision of the Almighty over all matters of the world... when one leaf falls from a tree, He decreed that it should fall... and this is an opinion very far from reason. And there are evil sects who think that He does not set His supervision... and this is the opinion of the deniers. And the masters of the true religion believe that His supervision, blessed be He, is over all species of animals in general... and so we have received from our great ones, etc."

It implies that among the masters of the true religion, i.e., the Jewish people, there were none in his days who held the opinion of the first sect.

And from the language of *Shomer Emunim* (brought above), which explains the matter of Hashgacha Pratis "according to what he also found in the books of the Kabbalists," it implies that it was not found in the books of Kabbalah either.

* * *

It is understood that the opinion of those who did not occupy themselves with this question, and did not know there was room to investigate it and arguments for and against, and in following the simple meaning of the verses, it was common on their lips to speak of Hashgacha Pratis in the inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms—these opinions do not enter into the count of the approaches, even though according to the clarification after some time, when the light of the Baal Shem Tov was revealed, it became known that they had aimed at the truth.

An example of this: what is written in Rambam (*Shegagos* ch. 13, law 5): "When does this apply? When this person knew that the sage or the student who arrived at the ruling **erred**, but if he was an ignoramus (and it is understood that the intention is an ignoramus in this law, and it makes no difference if he is a sage in other laws), he is exempt, for his **knowledge of prohibitions** is not certain knowledge, and he is joined to the category of **those who err based on their words**."

It is easy to distinguish between the above and what is written in *Tanya*, ch. 42: "And now, in order to understand, etc., but all Israel believe, etc." And similarly in *Iggeres HaKodesh*, section 25: "And it is also a simple faith, etc."

* * *

Now, in *Moreh Nevuchim* (Part 3, ch. 17), he explained the fourth opinion—according to the order there—regarding supervision, that it is over all that exists—even in the inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms—and this forces this approach to conclude that reward will be given in the World to Come even to animals, for what they suffered in terms of pain and death in this world, since all His ways are justice. He concludes: "However, this matter of reward for animals that do not speak is not heard at all in our faith (perhaps it should be 'in our nation') among the ancients, and even the Sages of the Talmud did not mention it at all. But some of the later ones among the Geonim, when they heard it from the sect of the Mu'tazila (the sect of the philosophers), it seemed right in their eyes (this approach of reward for animals) and they believed it." (And the Rambam rejects this opinion.)

It requires study whether this is intended for the Baal Shem Tov’s approach, since according to this approach, the matter of reward for animals in the World to Come is necessary, and according to what is explained in Chassidic literature, the matter of reward is not applicable except to human beings who have free choice.

And even if we distinguish between the reward and compensation in the *Moreh Nevuchim* there, that it is only payment for the pain they suffered, and we say that this is similar to what is written in *Likutei Torah*, *Maamar* "VeSamti Kadkod HaSheni" regarding the benefit and rectification of the horse—if so, the Geonim should have said this matter also regarding plants and inanimate objects and not only animals. For if we cut the plant or destroy the inanimate object before its time (and it is known that it is before its time if it is in a manner of *bal tashchis*), this is pain and death to the vegetative and inanimate soul. Furthermore, in *Likutei Torah*, it is about the ascent of the spark of holiness, and it is not a matter of reward for the pain.

And even though through what is explained in *Likutei Torah* the difficulty is resolved, for the aforementioned approach, why there is pain and death to this specific animal, nevertheless, it is a different matter and not a matter of reward. And it requires study.

**5. If the matter of creation being at every moment—as the Baal Shem Tov interprets "Forever, Hashem, Your word stands"—forces the matter of Hashgacha Pratis in every creature.**

Then it must be that those who hold that there is no Hashgacha Pratis in the inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms also disagree regarding the matter of creation at every moment.

Now—even though those who took the matter of *Tzimtzum* literally, seemingly it is clear that they would disagree with the fact that creation is at every moment and the power of the actor must be constantly in the acted-upon—but one can bring several proofs that those who say there is no Hashgacha Pratis in the inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms (and the author of *Shomer Emunim*, who is among them, holds that the matter of *Tzimtzum* is not literal, as he wrote at length in the debate in *Vikuach* 2, section 35) could possibly hold the approach that creation is at every moment. And for all the aforementioned great men of Israel, there is no necessity at all to say that they disagree with the Baal Shem Tov’s approach regarding "Your word stands," even though they did not explain the matter well in their books. The proofs:

a) Even those who hold that there is no Hashgacha Pratis in the inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms hold that His knowledge, may He be blessed, is in every specific event in the inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms, as mentioned above in the name of *Ikkarim*. If so, they could also say this regarding the creating power; what is the difference?

b) The innovation in "Your word stands" is that at every **moment** the creation is renewed. But **according to all**, at the first moment—like at the time of the birth of a child—the placing of the soul is by the word of Hashem. And according to the approach of the Rambam, etc., the birth of an animal, etc., is not by Hashgacha Pratis but by chance.

c) Just as there is no contradiction from the **free** choice of man to the matter of "Your word stands," and they say (as mentioned above from Rambam, *Hilchos Teshuvah*) that the Creator wills to give this to the authority of man, likewise we can say that the life-force belonging to the inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms is given to the minister and constellation appointed over this species of the inanimate, vegetative, and animal kingdoms.

- (And it is obvious that the intention here is not to say that they have free choice. See *Tanya*, beginning of ch. 32; *Likutei Torah*, *Biur VeHeineif*, section 3; *Kevod Malchuso*, 5660) - or that this is clothed in the laws of nature or also that it is handed over to mere chance—(as mentioned above in the language of *Shomer Emunim*)—for from the perspective of the matter of "Your word stands," all these are equal.

d) According to what is explained in Chassidic literature, seemingly it is clear that the matter of creation and the matter of Hashgacha Pratis are on different levels. Hashgacha Pratis concerns changes and is dependent on reward and punishment, knowledge after the fact, etc. Whereas the creation and existence of the thing concerns creation from nothing to being, which only He alone has the power and ability for, etc., the existence of the *yesh*, *sovev kol almin*, except that it comes through *memale kol almin*, etc. See *Pelach HaRimon*, *Maamar* "Ardah Na," section 7, what he wrote regarding the difference between the matter of creation and the matter of supervision.

Now, at the end of *Hemshech Rosh Hashanah* 5663, it is written that the supervision over the creature is its life-force, and he points to *Tanya*, ch. 44 (even though there only the law of knowledge is mentioned. And to note from *Torah Or*, *Maamar* "Ardah Na," that even there it is implied that supervision and knowledge belong to each other), and just as there is general and specific life-force, *sovev kol almin* and *memale kol almin*, so there is general supervision, in which all creatures are equal, and Hashgacha Pratis, in which the Jewish people are on a higher level compared to the nations of the world, etc.

(See also *Maamar* "Al Kein Yomru" 5696, brought at the beginning of this list). And it requires study to compare the two *maamarim*.

#### ***Side***

Printed in *Likutei Sichos*, Vol. 8, p. 277, and edited according to the secretariat’s copy. It is to R. Moshe Dober Rivkin. It was written without a date, and the date given here is according to a confirmation letter from the aforementioned R. M. D. R., which begins: "Light of Thursday, Ekev 5705, to my dear friend, the great Gaon, the great Chassid, son of the holy lineage, R. M. S. Shlita, peace and blessing! I have read, reviewed, and studied four times what your honor wrote regarding Hashgacha Pratis, and I have seen how you have marveled and magnified in expertise, and deepened and expanded, as the good hand of Hashem was upon you."

## 95

B"H, Monday, 29th of Menachem Av, 5705

To the distinguished *avreichim*, who study *Nigleh* and *Chassidus* with diligence, and who yearn for the *terua* and *darta* [the call and the dwelling] of the *Temimim* shlita,
Ferndale, N.Y.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter regarding the comment on the *kavanah* in *Sefer Shel Beinonim*, Chapter 1, concerning what is written there: that the *nefashot* of the *umos ha'olam* are from *kelipat nogah*, and that there is no good in them **at all**. You are in doubt as to whether there is, after all, some small measure of good in the *umos ha'olam*, since, on the face of it, this would seem to be a necessity, given that they were commanded in the seven *mitzvos* of the *Bnei Noach*. Furthermore, there are "pious ones of the nations of the world" (*chasidei umos ha'olam*) who have a share in the World to Come (according to Rabbi Yehoshua, and as ruled by the Rambam in *Hilchos Eidus*, Chapter 11, and *Hilchos Melachim*, Chapter 8), or perhaps there is no good in them at all, as the language of the *Sefer Shel Beinonim* implies.

Now, regarding the logic: one could propose various arguments for both sides. For example: a) If we say that there is some small measure of good in them that is active, then what is the distinction between *kelipat nogah* and the *kelipot* of *tumah*? And why is it said that **all** the charity, etc., that they perform is only for the sake of self-aggrandizement? Especially since in *Sanhedrin* 57b it is stated that "their charity is for their own sake," which implies that the *umos ha'olam* were commanded in charity. Why, then, is it said of them (*Sefer Shel Beinonim*, Chapter 1 and Chapter 6) that they are "completely impure and evil, and there is no good in them at all"? b) If you say that there is no good in them at all, how can they have existence? Even when they perform charity for the sake of self-aggrandizement, there is a good deed present alongside an evil intention. How is a good deed possible if there is no good in them at all?

However, this matter has already been explained in the writings of *Chassidus*. In the *Kitzur Tanya* by the Tzemach Tzedek (printed at the end of *Derech Mitzvosecha*, Part 1), Chapter 6, he writes: "*Kelipat nogah*, and there is no good in them at all (meaning in their essence; however, in the aspect of their exile, there is a vitality of *Elokus*, a spark from the *yud sefiros* of *Asiyah* which is within the *yud sefiros* of *Yetzirah*, which is within them, etc.)."

And with greater elaboration, he writes in the *maamar* entitled *Podeh B'shalom* 5668: "What is written in *Sefer Shel Beinonim* that *kelipat nogah* has no good in it at all does not mean that there is no spark in them whatsoever, for it is impossible for anything to exist without some good spark (even though their existence is from the *makif*, it is nevertheless necessary that there be some spark in them, etc.). Rather, it means that the spark is so distanced and darkened that it is like evil, etc. And this is that there is no *hargashah* of *Elokus* in them at all, etc." And so it is also in the *maamar* *Ner Chanukah* 5668, and in the *maamar* *Vayigdlu HaNe'arim* 5655, where it says: "The good becomes evil, similar to the concept of *chatichah na'asah nevilah*."*

See also *Sefer Shel Beinonim*, Chapter 24, and *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Section 25. See also the *Kuntres U'Maayan*, Discourse 4, which explains the words of *Sefer Shel Beinonim*, Chapter 24, and when quoting the words from *Sefer Shel Beinonim*, "And even though he does not see," he added the words: "meaning, without their feeling it." See also *Torah Or*, *maamar* *Re'eh Reiach Banai*, that there is vitality by way of *makif*—which they do not feel—and by way of *pnimiyus* that is swallowed within them. The concept of this "swallowing" is explained in the *maamar* *Pasach Eliyahu* 5702.

There is much to elaborate on this, but since I am in a hurry to reply, I did not want to delay the letter.

With wishes for great success in study and practice,
And with the blessing of "immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to *Geulah*,"

Chairman of the Executive Committee

In the *maamar* *V'chol Banayich*, Section 6, it is stated that in the future, even the *akum* will be refined, for it will be that "I will remove the spirit of impurity," etc.

## Tzav

B"H, Thursday, 9 Elul, 5705

To our esteemed friend, the outstanding Avreich, Yirei Shamayim and G-d-fearing,
The Tamim,
Rabbi M.Z. Gringlas, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters—briefly, as I am occupied with the printing of the *Kuntres* and *Maayan*, the *Sicha* for the holiday of Pesach, and several other matters (which was also the reason for the delay in my correspondence until now):

1) You have surely received our previous letter regarding your coming here to consult about the *avodah* in your country concerning *chinuch* on the foundation of holiness, and advocacy for strengthening the observance of *mitzvos* and the study of Torah.

2) Due to a certain reason, the publication of *HaKriah VeHaKedushah* was delayed in the past months, and we hope that they will be published (for the months of Tammuz, Menachem Av, and Elul) in about a week’s time.

3) All the printing materials you requested are being sent to you, and surely the copies of the letter to Kliatzkin have arrived in the meantime; it is strange that it has been delayed until now.

4) We received from you 48 booklets on 20 Tammuz, 25 booklets on 1 Elul, and 30 booklets via the esteemed Rabbi Fredmesky.

5) The *Vaad* sent several receipts and letters about two weeks ago regarding the *Sefer Torah*, and they have surely reached all those who participated through you. If not, please be kind enough to inform me of the names of those missing, and I will investigate the matter.

6) As I have heard—and you can verify this with R’ Sh.L., may he live—the *tefillin* of the late R’ D. Shifrin are not *mehudar* at all. If, nevertheless, you still desire them, please let me know, and I will clarify where they are and see to fulfilling your request.

7) Our book, Vol. 1 and Vol. 5, has been sent to Rabbi Carlebach as he requested.

8) Through whom is it possible to act so that our study books penetrate the circles of your Jewish Congress as well?

9) Perhaps it is worthwhile and possible that your newspaper print a review of our "book" in particular, and our other publications in general? Since the efforts from here do not bring results, one should try to have several readers of the newspaper write letters to the editorial board regarding this and similar methods.

10) We are currently preparing a calendar for print—in the English language—like last year, as well as a book about the *Beis HaMikdash* with a diagram of the *Beis*, the *avodah*, and so forth—also in the language of the country. If donors are found, they may print their names. If time permits, we will also publish a calendar, along the lines mentioned above, through *Machne Israel* in Yiddish.

Regarding what you wrote about why the names *Av*, *Sag*, *Mah* have a larger number [in *mispar katan*] than the name *Ban*.

Many years ago, I saw in a certain book—I believe in the name of the Maharash of Ostropol—that explains this: because *Av*, *Sag*, *Mah* in *mispar katan* equal nine, and "Ban" is also so, for the *Nun Peshuta* is 700 (see Rashi, *Sukkah* 52b, and as is known regarding the *Aleph-Beis* of *Ik B'Char*—mentioned in *Likutei Torah*, beginning of *Parshas Bracha*, and see also end of *Parshas Balak*, and explained in *Etz Chaim*, *Shaar Pirkei HaTzelem*, ch. 6, and *Shaar Tikun HaYareach*, ch. 5) and in *mispar katan* it is 7. This is unlike "Nav" [the *Nun* of *Ban*], which is only 7 in *mispar katan*. I do not recall if he explains there the advantage in this, that it must specifically be nine in *mispar katan*.

Perhaps it is because nine is "the ultimate of the calculation, above which there is nothing" (in the words of *Etz Chaim*), for ten is **one** tenth and returns to one, and so on. See the introduction to the book *Shefa Tal* (I believe that in your country they used to study it a lot), which elaborates on the virtue of the number nine, regarding the fact that the name *Mah* in *mispar katan* is nine.

Simply put, one could say that, as is the way with acronyms, they chose in such a way that it would be easy to remember—meaning that the word should have some meaning, unlike "Nav," which has no meaning (and if so, it requires study regarding the name "Mab," for it should have been "Bam").

And more deeply: the aspect of the name "Ban" has a connection to the word "Even" (stone)—(see *Yichudei HaAri*, end of ch. 7).

And incidentally: what he left vague there, writing "for the reason known to its creator," is explained in *Likutei Torah*, *d.h. V'Samti Kadkod*, second *maamar* of *Sag*, and is also hinted at in *Torah Or*, *d.h. V'Tachat Raglav*. Regarding the four sons in the *Haggadah* (*Pri Etz Chaim*, *Shaar Chag HaMatzos*, ch. 6—and mentioned in the *Siddur* of the Maharid of Liadi), the ten sons of the *maamar* of Elkana (*Likutei Torah* of the AriZal, *Shaar Aleph* 1), and more. See the *Sicha* of this year's *Chag HaPesach* regarding the matter of "Here the son asks 'Mah'."

See also in *Biurei HaZohar*, *Parshas Beha'aloscha*, regarding the distinction between a *Nun Peshuta* or *Kefufa*, and in *Likutei Torah*, *s.d.h. Acharei D'A Tielchu*. It requires study whether it is relevant to our case.

Continuation regarding the other questions next time.

With blessings for an immediate answer and an immediate redemption,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 98

[22 Elul 5703]

...I will conclude with a matter relevant to the day: Our Sages, of blessed memory, said that the initial letters of the phrase *Ish L're'ehu Matanos La'evyonim* ("a man to his friend, gifts to the poor") spell *Elul*, for at this time people are diligent in giving *tzedakah*. The Rambam writes (*Hilchos Teshuvah* 3:4) that it is the custom of all the House of Israel to increase *tzedakah*, etc., from Rosh Hashanah until Yom Kippur more than at any other time of the year. And if this is true for *tzedakah* that brings one to the life of this world, how much more so for *tzedakah* that brings one to the life of the World to Come, as is proven in the *Mishnah* (*Bava Metzia* 33a).

Furthermore, one can say there is an additional advantage to *tzedakah* for spiritual purposes over *tzedakah* for the life of this world. Regarding the latter, there can sometimes be a stumbling block involving poor people who are not worthy, in line with what our Sages said (*Bava Basra* 9b): "He caused them to stumble through people who are not worthy, so that they would not receive a reward for it." This is certainly true if the *tzedakah* funds are used to lead young children away from the faith. This is not the case with *tzedakah* that pertains to the life of the World to Come, where such a concern does not apply. This is all the more true regarding the education of children and the strengthening of adults in the observance of *Torah* and *mitzvos*, where there is no room even for the concern regarding "teaching Torah to a student who is not worthy" (*Chullin* 133a).

In particular, this prohibition may be said to apply only when it is possible to do otherwise, as is written in the *Shulchan Aruch* of the Alter Rebbe (*Hilchos Talmud Torah*, Chapter 4, *Kuntres Acharon*, Section 1).

May it be the will [of Hashem] that through "To You, Hashem, is the *tzedakah*," we be written and sealed among all of Israel for a good and sweet year.

## 99

[Elul 5703]

In continuation of the holy correspondence from the Rebbe... in the "Answers to Readers" section:

**Chaim Aharon Dober P.**

Regarding our response in the holy correspondence from the Rebbe that our Sages of blessed memory said, "It was only with difficulty that they permitted speaking words of Torah on Shabbos," which is cited in the *Hosafos* to *Torah Ohr* and *Likutei Torah*—you wish to know if this is also found in earlier books.

Regarding questions of this nature, one must bring to mind the words of our Sages: "Be careful with the coals of the Sages, lest you be burned."

For it is sufficient to rely on the Alter Rebbe and his son, the Mitteler Rebbe, when they cite our Sages—for **certainly** our Sages said it, even if we do not know the source of the statement at this time.

However, since we judge the questioners favorably, assuming there is no doubt whatsoever regarding the aforementioned, and that the intent is merely to clarify the source of the statement—in the manner of the common inquiry, "From where are these words that the Sages said...? The verse says..."—we hereby point out that this statement of our Sages is brought in *Sefer HaYirah* by Rabbeinu Yonah of Gerona, near the end. It is not found in the Midrashim currently in our possession, but it is known that many Midrashim that were available to the *Rishonim* have been lost and are no longer with us.

**Rabbi Y. Y. H.**

1) [Regarding the statement of our Sages, "And I will dwell within them—it does not say 'within it' (singular), but 'within them' (plural), within each and every Jew," which he found in the discourses of the Rebbe shlita]

See the previous response.

This statement is cited many times in *Chassidus*. It is also found in *Reishis Chochmah*, *Shaar HaAhavah*, Chapter 6; *Shelah*, *Shaar HaOsios*, letter *Lamed*; and many other places.

It is simple that when books use the expression "our Sages said," it can refer to our Rabbis who lived after the era of the *Shas* and the Midrashim; it is not necessarily required that it be found specifically in the Talmud or Midrash.

***

**From the holy handwriting:**

**In continuation of the holy correspondence from the Rebbe:** There, in the "Answers to Readers" section (Answers to letter-writers, p. 7), it was written in response to the questioner before us that the source is in the *Hosafos* to *Torah Ohr* and *Likutei Torah*. See above, Letter 96, whose publication was delayed until the middle of Elul.

**Regarding the statement of our Sages, "And I will dwell... within each and every Jew":** There, in response to the questioner before us: "In one of the Midrashim, and at present it is impossible to locate it."

## 100

[5742-43]

Our Sages relate (Shemos Rabbah, ch. 28) that when Hashem wished to give the Torah to Yisrael, He said to Moshe: "Speak to the women first—for they are diligent in the performance of mitzvos—so that they may lead their children toward Torah."

And therefore—through the proper chinuch that existed then—we find in that generation of Matan Torah that when the people gathered gold to fashion the Eigel, the women refused to participate in any way. Yet, a short time later, when Bnei Yisrael gave their contributions for the construction of the Mishkan, the women were the **first** to bring their gifts for the building of the Mishkan.

Parents! Fathers and mothers!

King Shlomo, the wisest of all men, said (Mishlei 14:1): "The wisdom of women builds her house, but folly tears it down with her own hands."

Every daughter and young girl is the one who will, when she grows up, build a home in Yisrael. **Upon her** depends the existence of that home or, chas v'shalom, its destruction.

But to **prepare** her for the fulfillment of this most important role—this task rests upon you, parents. Upon your shoulders lies all the responsibility for the future of your daughter and the future of the home that she must build.

To help you provide your daughter with the proper chinuch necessary for her to find her way—the straight path to a life of happiness, both spiritually and materially:

To provide your daughter, and your daughter’s daughter, with all the knowledge required for the fulfillment of her role:

To establish her upon the firm foundations of the "Ani Maamin" of the entire Jewish people:

To impress upon her the stamp of a Bas Yisrael who is connected to her religion, her Torah, and the tradition of her ancestors:

For this purpose, the schools "Beis Rivkah - Beis Sarah" were founded by the "Melach."

**Parents!** Ensure that your daughter attends the Beis Rivkah or Beis Sarah school in your neighborhood.

**Men and women!** Assist the "Melach" in its work—the work of establishing and expanding its network of schools. Then we are confident that, with the help of Hashem, the students of these schools will be among those who build the young generation—a generation healthy in body and soul, a generation in which the Jewish people will take pride.

With blessing and respect,

Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 101

Erev Rosh Hashanah, 5704

Greetings and blessings!

We are sending you herewith a small booklet—the content of a sicha from the Rebbe, shlita—containing words of encouragement, inspiration, and bitachon. It includes the first paragraph of Krias Shema and several chapters of Tehillim, which the Rebbe, shlita, chose to suggest reciting at designated times, as explained within the booklet. We are certain that you will read it frequently, and from it, you will draw strength in emunah, fortitude of heart, love for your fellow, and closeness to your faith, the Torah, and the mitzvos.

We also wish to transcribe here a few words that the Rebbe, shlita, said at a large gathering in the presence of many:

"It is a great mitzvah and a holy obligation for each and every person to publicize and inform every one of the Bnei Yisrael who is in the military—at sea, on land, or in the air—of the following:

Our Sages, of blessed memory, have said: 'Whoever puts on tefillin will live a long life.'

Our brothers in the military! Take care to put on tefillin every single weekday.

A soldier who finds it impossible to put them on in the morning should put them on in the afternoon, provided it is before sunset.

This is a segulah that Hashem will return you safely to your homes."

Be diligent in the fulfillment of mitzvos, especially this mitzvah, and caution all your comrades to do the same.

As we approach the coming year, we wish you a good and sweet year, in which wickedness will soon be consumed like smoke, and a year of blessings will begin. May you return to your home healthy and whole, with distinction both as a Jew and as an American. May we all, together with all our brethren of Bnei Yisrael, merit the complete Geulah through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days.

May you be inscribed and sealed for a good year!

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 102

B"H, Between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, 5704

To the esteemed Avreichim HaTemimim, G-d-fearing, men of action, students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, may they live, Montreal.

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your greeting for the coming year: I have received the blessing and I return to you a blessing of *chasimah* and *gmar chasimah tovah* — both materially and spiritually, in a manner that is good, revealed, and manifest.

These days are the days between Rosh Hashanah and "Rosh Hashanah," meaning Yom Kippur, which is also called Rosh Hashanah (Tosafos, Nedarim 23b). There are several concepts to be learned from this. Among them is the distinction between the two: the Rosh Hashanah of the beginning of the year is in the realm of *chitzoniyus* (externality), while the Rosh Hashanah of Yom Kippur is in the realm of *neshamah* and *penimiyus* (internality) (Likutei Torah, *Maamar* "Vehayah Bayom Hahu Yitaka").

Now, just as on the simple level the theme of these days is the *avodah* of *teshuvah*—as our Sages of blessed memory (Rosh Hashanah 18a) expounded on the verse "Seek Hashem..." as referring to these ten days between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur—it is understood that all of them are a preface and preparation for Yom Kippur. For then is the true and ultimate *teshuvah*, as it is written, "Before Hashem you shall be purified," and the essence of the day atones.

See also the *maamar* "Tzohar Ta'aseh" 5702: "Rosh Hashanah is the root and source for *yirah*... and Yom Kippur is the source for *teshuvah*."

Similarly, in the inner dimension of these matters, it must be that all the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah*—aside from the specific aspect within each of them—are a preparation for Yom Kippur. This is how one moves from the external to the internal, which is the general concept of *teshuvah*, which occurs specifically in the *penimiyus* of the *nefesh*. This is true even for *teshuvah tata'ah* (lower-level repentance) (see *Maamar* "Ar'a" 5691), and all the more so for *teshuvah ila'ah* (higher-level repentance). See Likutei Torah, *Maamar* "Shuvah" (the second one), which states: "During the *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah* until Yom Kippur, when 'before Hashem you shall be purified,' one reaches the level of 'the face of Hashem'... 'Your face, Hashem, I will seek.'" And in the *maamar* "Ki Seitzei" (the second one), section 7, it explains that through "Your face, Hashem, I will seek," one comes to "seek His face"—meaning the essential *penimiyus*, the point of the heart (and not merely its illumination).

It can be said that in this sequence—Rosh Hashanah, *Aseres Yemei Teshuvah*, Yom Kippur—the entire concept of the creation of man is included: Rosh Hashanah is established on the day of his creation, for man was created from the place of his **atonement** (Bereishis Rabbah, ch. 14). However, this is still in potential, not in actuality. In the *avodah* of each individual, this corresponds to the fact that when the *neshamah* descends, it is sworn to be "satisfied" (*sova*), receiving powers from Above. The ultimate intent of this is that the spirit shall return to the G-d who **gave** it, which is the level of Yom Kippur, the day of *teshuvah* and the *Yovel* (Jubilee). (All of this is well understood from the first *maamar* "Ha'azinu" in Likutei Torah; see there, 282).

—It should be noted that the primary reason Yom Kippur is called Rosh Hashanah is in reference to the Yom Kippur of the *Yovel* (Arakhin 12a; and the commentators on Ezekiel 40:1).

One reaches this through one's *avodah* from the depths, the *omka d'liba* (depth of the heart), the *penimiyus* of the heart, the ten depths within one's *nefesh*.

May the Ribono shel Olam return us, very soon, in complete *teshuvah* before Him—(see Likutei Torah, the *be'ur* on "Velo Avah" at the end: it is in *Ne'ilah*..., and in the *be'ur* on "Ki Seitzei" that *Ne'ilah* is the level of marriage (internality) and not betrothal (externality))—and may we merit **immediately** (in the language of the Rambam, *Hilchos Teshuvah* 7:5, and the Alter Rebbe in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, ch. 11) the complete redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With a blessing for a *chasimah tovah* and *gmar chasimah tovah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 103

[5 Tishrei, 5704]

We acknowledge with thanks the receipt of the "Aleph-Beis" chart you sent us. Regarding the differences between the "Aleph-Beis" published by the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch and the one you sent us, the primary distinction is that in our version, the vowels are labeled by their names—Kamatz, Pasach, etc.—whereas in the other version, this is not the case. Aside from the fact that a child would never learn the true names of the vowels from that chart, they are labeled there not as they are in themselves, but as if they were attached to letters. As far as this concerns the education of *taharas hakodesh*, you will surely understand this yourself.

See the *Tikkunei Zohar*, in the Introduction and in *Tikkun* 70, regarding several expositions on the names of the vowels. See also *Zohar Chadash* (*Tikkunim*, page 99c, Warsaw edition), which states that they are acronyms for the names of angels. See also *Torah Or*, *d'h Osri LaGefen*, which explains "and to his vine, the choice vine" (*v'lisruka bnei asono*)—*shruka* refers to the vowel *shuruk*. See also *Likutei Torah*, *biur* to *v'lo tashbit*, end of section 7, regarding the concept of the vowel *cholam*, as well as in many other places.

We are interested to know the status regarding the distribution of the *Kuntres U'Maayan*, and would appreciate it if you could inform us about this, as well as regarding the *Hayom Yom*.

With the blessing of *Chasimah v'Gmar Chasimah Tovah*, immediately for *teshuvah*, immediately for *Geulah*.

## 104

104

Friday, the month of Tishrei, 5704

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, elevated and respected... may he live,

Shochet u’Bodek,

Peace and blessing!

From time to time, we correspond with Jewish soldiers and send them various pamphlets to strengthen their hearts in general and to arouse them in matters of Yiddishkeit in particular.

A maamar for soldiers has now been published, based on the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita, regarding emunah and bitachon. It is being sent (naturally, free of charge) along with a letter of blessing to all Jewish soldiers whose addresses are known to us. If you would provide us with the addresses of your son and son-in-law, may they live, who are serving in the army, we will send them the aforementioned pamphlets as well and add their names to our list, so that we may maintain correspondence with them in the future, as mentioned above.

We are sending you in a separate package some of the kuntresim and pamphlets that have been published by Kehot, as we were greatly surprised to learn that you do not yet possess the books that have been published by us at various times (and if the cedars have been scorched...).

These days between Rosh Hashanah and "Rosh Hashanah"—meaning Yom Kippur, which is also called Rosh Hashanah, as stated in Tosafos, Nedarim 23b (and see Sefer Chassidim, section 258, and Likkutei Torah, beginning of the maamar "Vehayah bayom hahu yitka" and the beginning of the maamar "Yechayenu miyomayim")—contain many deep allusions. One of them is:

Every "living one"—for the Jewish people are called "living"—should take to heart that the Ribono shel Olam commanded us to observe and celebrate Rosh Hashanah not on the first day of the act of Creation, when the heavens and the earth and all their hosts were created (Bereishis Rabbah, ch. 1; and see Tosafos, Chagigah 12b), nor on the seventh day of creation, the day Hashem chose to sanctify above all other days. Rather, Hashem commanded us to observe Rosh Hashanah specifically on the day that Elokim created man—a creature who, immediately upon his creation, declared and proclaimed to all created beings: "Hashem is King, He has robed Himself in majesty... Come, let us bow down and prostrate ourselves, let us kneel before Hashem our Maker," as related by our Sages (Pirkei D'Rabbi Eliezer, ch. 11; Zohar Vol. I, 221b).

Each one of us, and you in particular, whom Hashem has graced with influence among his circle of acquaintances and associates, must proclaim through speech and through his actions:

Before the bright day arrives when Hashem will be King over all the earth, come and prepare yourselves for the great and awesome day of Hashem through teshuvah, Torah, and good deeds.

You should stand in the front line of those working—with soul, body, and wealth—in the campaign to strengthen Yiddishkeit and the observance of Torah and mitzvos among the widest circles of the Jewish people (various methods for this avodah are explained in the program of Machne Israel and Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, which were printed in the Hayom Yom).

And may Hashem grant us that through the "shechitah" that we perform—that is, the one who slaughters his yetzer (Sanhedrin 43b)—the day will come very soon when the Ribono shel Olam will slaughter the yetzer hara, as promised by our Sages (Sukkah 52b).

With the blessing of a good sealing and signing, immediately for teshuvah, immediately for Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

105

105

B"H, 13 Tishrei, 5704

To the distinguished, G-d-fearing, energetic activist, a man of many accomplishments, etc.,
R' Sholom Palmer, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

The printing of the Sicha for Pesach 5703 was completed today, and I am enclosing one booklet herewith. I have also instructed that several copies be sent to you immediately in a separate package. Please let me know how many more copies should be sent to you.

The printing was delayed until now for several reasons. Among them is that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, added much more to the Sicha, and it grew in both quality and quantity beyond what we had initially anticipated. Furthermore, it was because we wanted the Sicha to be printed with the utmost care and beauty, including indices, source references, and the like.

We bless the completion of this task, and I would like to express my gratitude once again, on behalf of all those who will read and study this Sicha, for the fact that thanks to you, together with the distinguished and esteemed Mr. Katz, may he live, it was possible to publish this booklet.

On the festival of Sukkos—which is the first day for the reckoning between Hashem and Yisroel after the atonement of Yom Kippur, as related by our Sages in the Midrash (Vayikra Rabbah 30)—we were commanded, "And you shall take for yourselves on the first day the fruit of a beautiful tree, palm branches, boughs of thick trees, and willows of the brook." Our Sages explain in the Midrash there: These represent Yisroel. The Esrog represents people who possess both Torah and good deeds; the Lulav represents people who possess Torah but lack good deeds; the Hadass represents people who possess good deeds but lack Torah; the Aravah represents those who possess neither Torah nor good deeds. And Hashem says: "Let them all be bound together in one bundle, and at that moment, I am exalted."

This is what a **Sicha** possesses that a **Maamar** does not: it is not only the Esrog and the Lulav that are made "beautiful" through it, but even the Hadass and even the Aravah (and according to the explanation of our Sages regarding their meaning in people, as mentioned above)—if a person is found who will exert effort in this, he can beautify them and make them pleasant through various parts of the Sicha, until they all become one bundle—see Kerisus (6b), "Every fast..." and from here, "and His bundle..."—to do the will of Hashem with a whole heart.

Happy is the man whose name is Sholom, for he will make peace among all four types of people within Yisroel, as mentioned above. And when they are all as one, then there will be granted to them—as we request in the blessing of *Sim Shalom*—blessing, mercy, and life.

With wishes for a happy holiday, and for immediate Teshuvah—immediate Geulah.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

Your letter from the 7th of Menachem Av surely arrived on time.

B"H, 13 Tishrei, 5704

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, honorable, and exalted, who conducts his business with faith,
Rabbi Y. Katz, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter for the coming year (which reached me only on Erev Yom Kippur in the afternoon, hence the delay in my response).

May you be blessed with blessings a thousand-fold, from above, in both soul and body, with revealed and manifest goodness.

You surely received my letter dated 10 Menachem Av in due time.

For several reasons, the completion of the printing of the Sicha for Pesach 5703 was delayed until now. One of the reasons is that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, shlita, added much to the Sicha, and it grew in both quality and quantity beyond what we had initially estimated. Another reason is that we wanted the booklet to be of the utmost quality.

Today, finally, they brought it from the bookbinder, and I have instructed that a few copies be sent to you in a special package (in addition to what is enclosed here). Please let me know how many more copies to send you.

On this occasion, I once again express my gratitude to you, on behalf of all those who will read and study this Sicha, for the fact that thanks to you, together with the esteemed, G-d-fearing, honorable, and exalted Rabbi S. Palmer, may he live, it was possible to print this booklet.

Our Sages said (Avos, Chapter 1, Mishnah 12): "Be of the disciples of Aharon... love the creatures and bring them closer to Torah." Our Alter Rebbe explains in Tanya (Chapter 32) that even those who are distant from the Torah of Hashem and His avodah—and are therefore called merely "creatures"—must be drawn with cords of love, and perhaps, just perhaps, one will be able to bring them closer to the Torah and avodah of Hashem.

This is what a "Sicha" possesses that a "Maamar" does not: in addition to the fact that a scholar and learned person will be inspired by it, even a simple person, and even those who are merely "creatures," can be brought closer to the Torah of Hashem and His avodah through many of the matters discussed in the Sicha.

And to effect this closeness in particular is part of the avodah of the aspect of Aharon that is found in every single Jew, and especially in his descendants, the Kohanim.

Concluding with wishes for a joyous holiday, and for immediate teshuvah—immediate Geulah.

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

108

B"H, Tuesday, Parshas Lech Lecha, 5704

To the distinguished avreich, the G-d-fearing, etc., the Tamim,
Rabbi Tzvi Schuster, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your invitation to your wedding, may it be in a good and auspicious hour, which was received with some delay,

I send you my blessing of Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov, and may you build a home in Israel upon the foundations and the inwardness of Torah and mitzvos.

One may explain, by way of possibility, the term *chassunah* (wedding) and *chassan* (groom) as related to *nachus darga* (descending a level) (Yevamos 63a): For it is explained in several places (including in a letter from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, which is transcribed in the *Hayom Yom*, p. 78) that the descent from above and the journey in this world until old age and advanced years—regarding this it is said, "And you shall walk on the way."

Now, in "walking," there must be two elements: 1) The walking itself. 2) Knowing where to walk. The walking in *po'al mamash* (actual deed) is accomplished by the body, and the guide for the straight path is the neshamah—and this is the parable of our Sages regarding the neshamah and the body (Sanhedrin 91a and there), that the neshamah repairs the blind man and the body repairs the lame man. And specifically through their union—which are called by the names "man" and "woman," and their coupling, which is the matter of this world, which is called *hillula* (festivity) (Eruvin 54a)—is the matter of a wedding, as is evident in the Zohar (beginning of Parshas Chayei Sarah and p. 181b and there), that a "walk" (a process) is created.

And the purpose: *Ahavah* and *yirah* (love and fear—the "wings") and Torah and mitzvos.

Now, one might ask, seemingly, on the contrary—as our Sages say (Bereishis Rabbah on the parsha)—the "way" diminishes three things: 1) Diminishment of the name—the matter of which is a diminishment in the involvement in mitzvos, as Rashi and the *Matnos Kehunah* explain in the Midrash. 2) Diminishment of wealth—the matter of which is in the *avodah* of the diminishment of *ahavah* and *yirah*, which are called gold and silver, for even if one were a complete *tzaddik*, etc., he would not reach the level of his *dveikus*, etc., prior to his descent—as is written in *Sefer Shel Beinonim*, Chapter 32. 3) Diminishment of involvement in *peru u'revu* (procreation)—the matter of which is in the *avodah* of a diminishment of involvement in *Talmud Torah*, as hinted at in the words of our Sages (Bechoros 44b), "May you not be barren of students," for on the "way"—that is, in this world—there are many obstacles to the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos.

And to this, the Midrash (ibid.) answers that the Holy One, Blessed be He, blesses Avraham (this is the neshamah, as written in the Zohar, Parshas Chayei Sarah, ibid.) that, on the contrary, specifically through "Lech Lecha" (Go for yourself), etc., through this, "I will bless you," etc., in wealth, name, and *peru u'revu*.

And the general concept is that which a person's *yetzer* overcomes him every day, and were it not for the Holy One, Blessed be He, helping him, he could not overcome it (Sukkah 52b), and the blessing is that which is granted to him as help.

—See *Kuntres Uma'ayon*, Maamar 13, Chapter 2, and Maamar 14, Chapter 1, for the roots of these matters—

And then, **specifically** through the descent of the neshamah into the body, one reaches the love of "with all your *me'odecha*" (wealth), and likewise the mitzvos (ibid.) were given specifically **in physicality**, and regarding Torah, our Sages said, "Happy is he who comes here and his study (procreation/students) which he learned **specifically in this world** is in his hand."

Now, of the three aforementioned things, which are the purpose of walking on the path of life, the essence of the *yichudim* (unifications) is through Torah and mitzvos, for *ahavah* and *yirah* are [merely] "wings," as explained in *Sefer Shel Beinonim*, end of Chapter 50.

And within Torah and mitzvos themselves—the mitzvos are still in the category of *erusin* (betrothal), and Torah is specifically in the category of *nisuin* (marriage) (*Likutei Torah*, Bamidbar, *d.h. Vayidaber Elokim*, Chapter 4, and elsewhere), which is the purpose of the creation of this lower world from which we are departing, for "He did not create it for chaos; He formed it to be inhabited."

And when, in addition to the simple walking on the way, there is also the matter of *galus* (exile)—that they were exiled to Bavel, etc., to Edom—then one must prioritize, before everything else, the ascent from *galus*—which is the matter of *teshuvah*—and this is: just as the descent is not by way of gradation at all, so too must the ascent be by way of a leap, not through gradation at all (and the matter in *avodah* is understood). And regarding this it is said, "Flee, my beloved, and be like a **tzvi** (gazelle)."

—As explained well in the additions to *Torah Or*, *d.h. Lehavin Lamma Le'atid Lavo, etc.—

With blessings for a Mazal Tov, immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to *Geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 109

[Erev Shabbos Parshas Lech Lecha, 5704]

...I asked... my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita... and his holy words were:

"The *chavitas aravah* (beating of the willow) represents *gevuros memutakos* (sweetened *gevuros*), and *gevuros memutakos* is *v'rav chesed* (abundant kindness), as it descends into a good that is visible and revealed."

...Possible notes on the above...

1) That *gevuros* are sweetened specifically through *v'rav chesed* can be understood from what is written in *Likutei Torah*, Parshas Naso, in the *maamar* beginning "Hashem will shatter those who contend with Him" (Section 1).

2) From what is written in *Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe (Section 10) and in *Likutei Torah*, Parshas Beha'aloscha, in the first *maamar* (Section 3, Section 6, and in the *Biur* Section 1), one can understand the distinction between *chesed* in general and *rav chesed* in the *avodah* of man. In *Likutei Torah* there, it is explained that *rav chesed* pertains to Aharon the Kohen.

3) Based on what is written in *Likutei Torah*, Parshas Korach, in the *maamar* beginning "And behold, the staff of Aharon had sprouted," it is understood: a) that through *v'rav chesed*, [the light] is drawn down literally below into a visible and revealed good; b) that this *hemshech* (drawing down) is brought about by "Aharon and his descendants after him, the Kohanim who lift their hands and bless the people with *Birchas Kohanim*."

#### ***109***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 4, p. 1367.

## 110

Wednesday, 12 Cheshvan, 5704

To our esteemed friend, the maskil and navon, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc.,
Rabbi... may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Our conversation at the time of your farewell blessing strengthens my hope that upon your return to your city of residence—with renewed strength derived from the spiritual life of Tishrei in general, and Zman Simchaseinu in particular, during which you benefited from the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita—you have already approached your holy work, beginning the new study term with success.

And although it is clear to me how occupied you are with the educational institution under your leadership, I am nevertheless confident, based on what we discussed while you were here, that you will dedicate time and attention to our general work. This applies particularly to the matter of making our "books" known in circles that have connection to and influence upon education, as well as the dissemination of "shmuessen," a maamar, or a review in newspapers and the like. Surely, you do not require instruction in the methods of promotion and distribution, and we hope to hear good news from you in this regard.

As we cannot delay the printing of the "Luach" any longer, we are sending it to the press before having secured a donor. If you are able to do anything further regarding this, it will be a great merit for you, given the beloved influence of the Luach on the spirit of the youth, as last year's experience has shown us.

The selections from Chazal and the subjects I have included in this year's Luach are different from those in the previous Luach (aside from the dinim and minhagei haYom Tov and the like, which, of course, are included in the Luach currently being printed). Its external format is the same as that of last year.

Chazal state in this week’s parsha (Bereishis Rabbah, end of chapter 59): "Throw a stick into the air, and it will land on its root." This means (as explained by the Maharzu in Midrash Rabbah, ch. 20, sec. 23, and other commentaries) that it falls and lands on the thick side, which is near the root. From this we learn two things: a) Even though it is a dry stick and has long been severed from its root, it is still possible to awaken its source and root; b) The stick requires assistance in this, and the assistance consists of disturbing its rest, lifting it from the ground, and throwing it into the air. This is the duty of everyone according to their ability, and especially those whom Hashem has graced with a pedagogical sense, to engage and strive in this assistance.

With best regards to all those who seek your welfare, and with the blessing of "Immediately to Teshuvah, Immediately to Geulah,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 111

111

B”H, Tuesday, 18th of the month of Mar-Cheshvan, 5704

To the honorable Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, the man of many accomplishments, wise and understanding, whose lips guard knowledge, etc., Moreinu HaRav R’ A.A. HaKohen, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Vayeira.

Regarding your request that I mention you inside and deliver your Pidyon Nefesh to my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita: I have fulfilled this. And in accordance with the words of our Sages (Mechilta, Shemos 19:8), who taught that even if the sender already knows, one still informs him of the mission, I am writing to you regarding this.

It is worth noting that the Targum Yonasan (ibid.) adds the word “in His shadow” to both verses—verse 8 and verse 9—and it is possible that his intent in doing so is to resolve the difficulty raised in the Mechilta: Was it truly necessary for Moshe to report back? (And this is not in accordance with the opinion that it is to teach you, etc.).

In our current case, it is possible to say that there is no argument, since here, the sender’s knowledge will only come after some time.

With the blessing of “immediately to Teshuvah, immediately to Geulah,”

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 112

112

B"H, Tuesday, 18th of the month of Mar-Cheshvan, 5704

To the honorable Rabbi, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, distinguished and exalted, etc.,
Rabbi Ch. B. [Ginzburg], may he live,

Peace and blessing!

Your letter reached me with a delay, and subsequently, I was occupied with the printing of the *sicha* for *Chag HaPesach* from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *shlita*, and the *kuntres* *Ma'ayan MiBeis Hashem*. Even now, time does not permit me to write at length, as I am preparing for print the *sicha* of *Chai Elul* of this year and another *kuntres* of *maamarim*—and all this is in addition to the regular *avodah* of *Machne Israel* and *Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch*.

Nevertheless, I am writing these few lines out of respect for the Torah. Enclosed, as per your request, is a copy of my letter to you from last summer. Since I have retrieved it from the archives, I am sending it **on the condition that it be returned**, and I thank you in advance.

Now, all of this concerns the matter of "great is Torah study," but what shall we do on the day when we speak of "great is action"? The Alter Rebbe already wrote (in *Tanya*, *Iggeres HaKodesh*, ch. 9): The entire essence of the *avodah* of Hashem in these times, in the footsteps of Moshiach, is the *avodah* of *tzedakah*, as our Sages of blessed memory said: "Israel will only be redeemed through *tzedakah*." And our Sages did not say that "Torah study is equivalent to acts of loving-kindness" except in their days, when Torah study was the primary *avodah* for them, and therefore they were great sages, etc. This is not the case in the footsteps of Moshiach, etc.

It is known from our Sages (*Tanna D'bei Eliyahu*, ch. 27) regarding the verse, "Is it not to share your bread with the hungry... when you see the naked, that you cover him, etc.," that this refers to one who clothes his fellow in *tallis* and *tefillin*, etc.—thereby granting him the life of the World to Come.

This is the *avodah* of *ta'amulah* (outreach) to bring Jews closer to Torah and *mitzvos*.

Our Sages have already assured us in *Midrash Rabbah* on this *parsha* (*Bamidbar Rabbah* 19:6): "Throw a stick into the air, and it will land on its root." The meaning—as explained by the *Maharzu* in *Bamidbar Rabbah* (ch. 2, sec. 23), and other commentaries—is that it falls and lands on the thicker side, which is near the root. From this we learn two things: a) Even though it is a dry stick and it has been a long time since it was severed from its root, it is still possible to awaken its source and root; b) The stick requires assistance in this, and the assistance is that one disturbs its rest, lifts it from the ground, and throws it into the air; then, **it lands on its root**.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee
