## 114

10 Kislev, 5704

To my friend, the distinguished and exalted Torah scholar, G-d-fearing and learned, spreader of Torah, etc., the *Tamim* Rabbi Sh. (may he live):

Peace and blessing!

In response to what you wrote regarding the difficulty cited in *Kuntres U’Maayan* — by the Rebbe *n.e.* — beginning at the end of *Maamar* 17, concerning the contradiction in the words of our Sages (who stated in *Beitzah* 16a that a person’s sustenance is determined for him from Rosh Hashanah to Yom Kippur, while in *Rosh Hashanah* 16a they stated that a person is judged on *Kaf-Hey* [the 25th of Elul]), you write that a great scholar raised the following questions:

1) Is it not so that Rabbi Yossi, who is the one who says a person is judged on *Kaf-Hey*, is a lone opinion, and the Sages disagree with him and hold that one is judged on Rosh Hashanah?

2) In the book *Mikraei Kodesh* by Rabbi Yosef Mamiga (Part 2, Section 10 and onwards), he concludes that in truth, according to Rabbi Yossi, there is no difference between Rosh Hashanah and the rest of the year **regarding the judgment**; rather, Rosh Hashanah is designated to remind and arouse people to do *teshuvah* on *Kaf-Hey* and every day, without distinction between one day and another.

3) It is puzzling why the *Kuntres U’Maayan* does not mention that the *Mikraei Kodesh* discusses this contradiction.

Regarding this, my view is as follows:

1) Even if we say that the *halachah* does not follow Rabbi Yossi, and therefore, **for us**, there is no difficulty from the fact that a person is judged on *Kaf-Hey*, nevertheless, for Rabbi Yossi himself, the question remains: What is the nature of the judgment of Rosh Hashanah, given that one is judged on *Kaf-Hey*?

It is surprising that the questioner raised this, as the *Kuntres U’Maayan* itself explains this very point. It states: "One must say, based on the words of our Sages that a person is judged on *Kaf-Hey*, how can this be reconciled with the aforementioned statement that his sustenance is determined from Rosh Hashanah, etc.? For certainly, even **Rabbi Yossi**, who said that a person is judged on *Kaf-Hey*, admits that the judgment and sentencing take place on Rosh Hashanah, etc." This is explained at greater length in *Likutei Torah*, end of *Parshas Korach*, where it writes: "And even though the statement that a person is judged on *Kaf-Hey* is the view of Rabbi Yossi and Rabbi Nassan, unlike the Sages, nevertheless, it is certain that even for Rabbi Yossi and Rabbi Nassan, the essence of the judgment is on Rosh Hashanah; for if not, etc. Similarly, the words of our Sages that a person’s sustenance is determined from Rosh Hashanah to Yom Kippur imply that this is certainly agreed upon by all, and there is no dispute regarding this. And nevertheless, they hold that a person is also judged on *Kaf-Hey*." (End quote).

Furthermore: The assumption of the questioner that the *halachah* does not follow Rabbi Yossi but rather the Sages — as is also stated in *Mikraei Kodesh* (Part 2, beginning of Section 14) that the *halachah* follows the Sages — is highly questionable. On the contrary, the opposite seems to be the case: that the *halachah* follows Rabbi Yossi. This is because: a) According to the known rules of the *Gemara*, if *Amoraim* engage in a *shakla v’taryah* (discussion) regarding the reasoning of a specific *Tanna*, it is a sign that the *halachah* follows him. Rav Chisda (*Rosh Hashanah* 16a) discusses and explains the words of Rabbi Yossi. One cannot refute this from the fact that several *Amoraim* discuss the words of the Sages in the *Mishnah* (*Rosh Hashanah* 18a), because there, it does not pertain to the opinion of the Sages, but rather to the manner of the judgment Above, and their explanation is applicable even according to Rabbi Yossi. b) All those who hold that a final decree of an individual is not torn up (see *Rosh Hashanah* 17b and *Niddah* 70b), unlike Rabbi Yitzchak, must also hold according to the opinion of Rabbi Yossi, since we pray for the sick and the suffering, as is stated in *Rosh Hashanah* (16a). It is very forced to explain that they all did not pray for the sick and suffering, especially since the *Gemara* says simply, "As whom do we pray nowadays?" which implies that everyone did so. See also *Nedarim* (49b), where Rava does not say "If you wish, I can say" that we pray for the sick and suffering even according to the Sages (though one could dismiss this by saying that the matter was only brought up there incidentally).

**Note**: One should not bring proof that the *halachah* follows Rabbi Yossi from the rule that the *halachah* follows Rabbi Yossi against his colleagues. Even if we say that this applies specifically against *his* colleague and not against *his* colleagues (see *Tosafos*, *Eruvin* 46b, and *ibid.* 86b, where the books on the rules of the *Gemara* have already elaborated on this), here, since each of his colleagues has a distinct opinion, they are considered individuals, as is implied in *Eruvin* (47a), where Rabbi Meir, Rabbi Yehudah, and Rabbi Yossi disagree.

It is not a valid argument, because since it is a dispute in a *Baraita* and an anonymous *Mishnah* follows the Sages, the *halachah* follows the anonymous *Mishnah* (*Yevamos* 43b).

2) Regarding the conclusion in *Mikraei Kodesh* (Part 2, Section 12) that Rabbi Yossi (and certainly Rabbi Nassan) holds "that a person is judged on *Kaf-Hey* just like on Rosh Hashanah, without any difference... not that it is a day of judgment different from other days of the year, and what we say... 'All creatures will be remembered on it' means that on this day they will be remembered, and likewise on all other days," and he elaborated on this: even if we accept his position that the *halachah* does not follow Rabbi Yossi and Rabbi Nassan, it is highly questionable how one can say that Rabbi Yossi and Rabbi Nassan hold this, as was questioned in *Likutei Torah* (ibid.). Especially after the length at which the *Zohar* discusses Rosh Hashanah, describing it as a *Yoma D’Dina Rabba* (a day of great judgment), how could Rabbi Yossi, who was one of the *Chavraya* (the circle) of Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai, disagree with all of this?

It is even more difficult given the *Zohar Chadash* (31b and 32a), which elaborates on the matter of the *petkin* (decrees) of *Hoshana Rabbah* and the matter of *reach* (scent), and Rabbi Yossi is among those speaking there. How can the author of *Mikraei Kodesh* reconcile such an explicit contradiction?

3) As to why the *Kuntres U’Maayan* did not mention that the *Mikraei Kodesh* discusses the aforementioned contradiction: this *Kuntres* comes to clarify the matter based on the foundations of the Arizal and the teachings of Chassidus, and it is not its purpose to bring every place that discusses this. The fact that it cites the book *Asarah Maamaros* is to provide support that one can interpret the passage in *Rosh Hashanah* such that Rabbi Yossi and the Sages do not disagree, and that one says one thing and the other says another.

***

He also raised a difficulty regarding what is written in the introduction to *Kuntres U’Maayan* (page 25b), that upon the publication of the *Iggeres HaKodesh* regarding 19 Kislev, which is the Rosh Hashanah for Chabad Chassidus, they said, "Chabad *b'Hashem* lives, and may Hashem grant that *Chagas* should also live." The question is: how can one use such language regarding *Chagas*, which are holy *Sefiros*?

Now, surely it is simple even to the questioner that the speaker’s intent is regarding the Chassidim of Chabad — whose order of *avodah* is to contemplate and meditate, etc. (and through this they arrive at *ahavah* and *yirah*) — that they received added strength and vitality through the publication of this *Iggeres*, and this is "Chabad *b'Hashem* lives." By saying *Chagas*, he intended the Chassidim of Poland, whose order of *avodah* is in the faith of the *Tzaddikim* (and that the *Tzaddik* will bestow upon them) and *ahavah* and *yirah*. It seems his question is only regarding the phrasing.

But in truth, we have already found similar expressions, as our Sages said (*Zohar Chadash* 113a), "'And you shall perform them' — it is written 'you' (*atem*); I consider it as if you have created Me." **And truly, the language is the same as the aforementioned in the introduction, but regarding the *Sefiros***. This is also found in the revealed Torah, in *Berachos* (32a): "As I live, etc.," where the Holy One, blessed be He, said to Moses, "Moses, you have revived Me with your words." The books have already elaborated on this (and many of our Sages’ statements have been cited in this regard) in explaining the concept that *avodah* is a "need of the High One" (*tzorech gavoah* — see *Avodas HaKodesh*, introduction and beginning of *Chelek HaAvodah*; *Shelah*, introduction to *Drush Shaar HaGadol*, and others).

The matter, in short, is explained in *Chassidus* based on the introduction of the Maharash to *Pri Etz Chaim*. It states (regarding our topic) that there are the *Sefiros* themselves — which do not lack and do not exceed, each in its level and *avodah*, from the *Keter Elyon* to the end of all levels. In this regard, they have no share in the lower beings at all, whether they do good or evil, for the **established** law is not interrupted. However, through the *avodah* of the lower beings, they add light from Above and they are refined with great refinement, and this addition is greater than the essence, etc., to the point that one does not consider their fixed measure in comparison to that addition (see *Likutei Torah*, *Shir HaShirim*, discourse beginning *Lehavin Inyan HaTaam*).

It is explained in many places that there are *mitzvos* that depend on the "Head of the King," some on the body, and some on the hands, etc. (*Zohar Chadash* 85b, *Tikkunei Zohar*, *Tikkun* 70, page 130a, and elsewhere). When one uses the intellect of his soul for contemplation and understanding in Torah, this depends on the *Mochin* of Above.

This is also hinted at in the revealed Torah, as our Sages said (*Tana D’Bei Eliyahu*, Part 1, Chapter 18): "Every Torah scholar who sits and engages in Torah and reviews it, the Holy One, blessed be He, sits opposite him, reading and reviewing with him."

Similarly, when one arouses *ahavah* and *yirah* in his soul, or performs an act of *chesed*, etc., it depends on the *Chagas* of Above, regarding the addition of light, as mentioned above.

This is the language of the Chassidim mentioned in the introduction: if they are not prophets, they are the children of prophets, for through the engagement in the contemplation and understanding of Torah, and especially the inner dimension of Torah, *Chabad* lives below in the person who is learning, and through this, he draws from the *Ohr Ein Sof* that encompasses all worlds, light and vitality into the *Chabad* of Above (*Likutei Torah*, *Shir HaShirim*, discourse beginning *LeSusati* — the second one). And through the *avodah* in the *Chagas* of his soul, he also draws an addition of light into the *Chagas* of Above.

***

Incidentally, since I have the *Mikraei Kodesh* at hand, I wanted to point out something puzzling that I saw in the aforementioned chapters.

In Chapter 14, he concludes that on the fourth day, the luminaries were suspended and stood at the threshold of the firmament (like the grasses), and only upon the creation of man on the sixth day did they begin to serve, move, and rotate; therefore, it was fixed for Rosh Chodesh Tishrei, and not on the fourth day.

Now, with all due respect, this is extremely puzzling: a) It is beyond doubt that the blessing of the sun (*Birchas HaChamah*), where one sees the sun in its cycle and the moon in its strength, is on the fourth day and not on the sixth day (*Berachos* 59b). From Rabbi Yehoshua, we know this even according to Rabbi Eliezer, who said the world was created in Tishrei. b) Since the luminaries were created on the first day — as is also written in *Mikraei Kodesh* — and began to rotate and shine upon the earth (according to his opinion) only on the sixth day, then why did the moon complain on the fourth day when they were suspended in the heavens? In any case, it should have complained immediately upon their creation, or when they began to serve and shine. (One cannot answer that initially it said they should not be suspended in one firmament — *Chagigah* 12b — because if in this manner it did not matter to it, then why was there a need for the "diminishing of the moon"?) c) In *Targum Yonasan* (*Bereishis* 1:16), it says that the sun and moon were equal in their glory, each for one hour minus 1,782 parts. (The precision of this duration is explained in the book *Asarah Maamaros*, *Maamar Ach"ch*, Part 1, Section 14, and not as in the glosses of the *Radal*). Here, too, the same question applies: in any case, one must count either from the time they were created or from the time they began to shine, but not from the time they were suspended in the firmament. d) It is stated in the *Baraita* of Shmuel, beginning of Chapter 6: "The sages of Egypt said, the beginning of the creation of the luminaries: the sun was created in Leo at 15 degrees, the moon in Cancer at 15 degrees, etc. Thus, the month of the moon (until the *molad*, at which time the sun and moon are in one place in the zodiac) is... two days and a quarter (during which time the moon travels 30 degrees from Cancer to Leo. See *Hilchos Kiddush HaChodesh* by the Rambam, Chapter 14)." This implies explicitly that immediately upon the creation of the luminaries, they began to rotate in their orbits (*posh u'mosh*). (Unlike *Tosafos*, *Rosh Hashanah* 8a, s.v. *LiTkufos*, which says this is only for calculation, but it is not necessary to say that the rotation was in their orbits. Like the *molad* of *Beha"rd*, which is a *molad* of *tohu* and not that it was in its orbit). And even though I have not yet found a colleague elsewhere in the words of our Sages for the opinion of the *Chachmei Mitzrayim* mentioned above that the luminaries were created on the 15th of Av, why should we multiply disputes and say that they also disagree regarding the rotation of the zodiac immediately upon their creation?

In conclusion, I have not been able to understand the opinion of the author of the book. Since we have been privileged to have the teachings of the Arizal, it is explained in *Etz Chaim*, *Shaar Miut HaYareach*, Chapter 2, as follows: "And then — on the fourth day — all three aspects were magnified... until it was a complete *partzuf*. And when the moon complained, it was diminished. The matter of the diminishing of the moon was on the fourth day. Afterwards, on the sixth day, it returned to be magnified in the aforementioned three aspects, being a complete *partzuf* (until Adam HaRishon sinned)." From the secret, we know regarding the *peshat* that they correspond. Regarding the matter of the diminishing of the moon according to *Chassidus*, see *Ohr HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek, *Parshas Bereishis*, and references there.

With the blessing of "immediately to *teshuvah*, immediately to *geulah*,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 115

115

B"H, 10 Kislev, 5704

To the esteemed and exalted, the diligent activist, etc.,
Rabbi A. Feigelshtock,

Shalom u’Bracha!

We were pleased to hear that you are engaged in your new place of residence in strengthening Torah and Yiddishkeit, and that you have surely heard by now, more or less, about the work of "Machne Israel" and the "Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch" in general, and the books and reading material published by our publishing house, "Kehot," in particular.

Already before last Pesach, we sent you samples of our various booklets, and it is surprising that we have not yet received confirmation of their receipt.

We are enclosing a list of our publications so that you may choose what you need. Upon informing us of the required quantities, we will send them to you, G-d willing.

Institutions engaged in Jewish education that wish to distribute our material may receive a discount of ten percent (10%) and be exempt from shipping costs—which amount to a significant sum—to their country, or a 25% discount with shipping at their own expense.

I will conclude with the mitzvah of this month—the Chanukah lights. We find three mitzvos regarding lights: the lights of the Beis Hamikdash, the Shabbos light, and the Chanukah light. Among the differences between them: the lights of the Beis Hamikdash illuminated the sanctuary of the Beis Hamikdash but ceased to exist after the Beis Hamikdash was destroyed. The mitzvah of the Shabbos light exists even in this time, but its role is to illuminate the home of the Jewish person. The Chanukah light adds to these: beyond the fact that we find it is eternal (see Ramban on the Torah, beginning of Parshas Beha'aloscha), we find that it must also illuminate the outside, in the public domain (and the hint is understood). It must be for **pirsumei nisa** (publicizing the miracle), that ultimately, Hashem delivers the impure into the hands of the pure, and the wicked into the hands of those who occupy themselves with Torah.

And it is ruled as halacha that even one who lives in an attic (and the hint in a person’s avodah to his Creator—"I have seen the people of the attic, and they are few" [Sukkah 45b]—is that their avodah is on a very high level) and has no entrance to the outside (meaning he has no connection to commerce or the general affairs of this world), nevertheless, he too must illuminate the outside by placing the Chanukah lights, at the very least, in the window.

With the hope of maintaining constant contact with you, and with blessings for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 116

Wednesday, 11 Kislev, 5704

To the esteemed Rabbi, the accomplished scholar, distinguished and exalted...

Peace and blessing!

Your letter was received, along with one dollar, and you complain that we are being burdensome by sending books, etc.

In truth, there was no intention to be burdensome at all. It is well known from our Sages (Chullin 7b) that "the Jewish people are holy; there are those who wish [to fulfill their obligations, etc.]," and as is explicitly written in the letter sent regarding the book, anyone who wishes may return the book for any reason whatsoever (see Sotah 44a, "Therefore the Torah hung [the obligation of returning home from war on the person's own desire]").

I am returning the dollar herewith, in accordance with the aforementioned passage in Chullin. You need not return the *Kuntrus* "U'Ma'ayan" to us; please keep it. It has been sent to many people without any financial obligation, and I am confident that if you examine it, you will find it to be of value, etc. It does not require my endorsement.

I am particularly surprised by your letter, as I see you citing—regarding the matter of sending the books—a verse and the Shulchan Aruch, Choshen Mishpat, section 97. It seems you are referring to subsection 2, which states: "It is forbidden to press a borrower for repayment when one knows that he does not have the means, and it is even forbidden to show oneself to him, because he is shamed when he sees the lender and his hand does not reach to pay."

Since you have touched upon a point of law, and in my humble opinion your words are puzzling, I have seen fit to elaborate somewhat in clarifying the matter.

The difficulty with your argument stems from several reasons:

1) The verse—"You shall not be to him as a creditor"—and the Shulchan Aruch apply specifically **when one knows** that the borrower does not have the means, as is the language of the Gemara and the Poskim.

If the lender is in doubt as to whether the borrower has the means, and one might suggest applying the rule of "we act stringently," the *Minchas Chinuch* (Mitzvah 67) has already noted that the language of the Shulchan Aruch (Choshen Mishpat 97:2) implies that there is no prohibition at all. See there for his reasoning, which is logical. This applies all the more so in the present case.

2) What is even more puzzling in your citation of the law that it is forbidden to "press," etc., is that this law is stated only regarding a borrower and a lender.

The distinction is simple: both from the perspective of the "presser"—for "the borrower is a slave to the lender" (see Ramban on the Torah, Shemos 22:24), and regarding this it is said, "He imposes a burden upon a person" (Bava Metzia 75b).

One should also include the concept that "a person does not brazenly face his creditor," according to the version of Rashi (Bava Kamma 107a), which is because the lender did him a favor; this also applies to pressing and shaming him.

And both from the perspective of the matter itself—that he is obligated to pay him—which is not the case in the present matter, where none of this applies. It is simple.

Furthermore, even regarding *tzedakah*, where there is a mitzvah—although the obligation is not like the obligation of repaying a debt, for there, even if his hand does not reach to pay, the obligation remains upon him at that very moment, whereas in *tzedakah*, one is not obligated if he does not have his own livelihood (see Tur Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, beginning of section 246 and section 251, and this is not the place to elaborate)—in *tzedakah*, because the concept of "the borrower is a slave," etc., does not apply, the law of "you shall not be to him as a creditor" does not apply. As is stated in Bava Basra (8b), they needed the verse, "And I will punish all his oppressors," and it is only a matter of *Divrei Kabbalah* (Prophetic writings), not *D'oraisa* (Torah law). Even this prohibition regarding *tzedakah* only applies when one demands it, as the Rambam writes in *Hilchos Matnos Aniyim*, chapter 7, halacha 11, which is copied in Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah 248:7. This is unlike the case of a borrower, where even showing oneself to him is forbidden.

Based on this, the incident in the Yerushalmi, *Horayos* (3:4), regarding Rabbi Elazar, etc., who saw our Rabbis and despaired of them and went up to his house, etc., is **simply** understood. Seemingly, it is difficult: they did not need to show themselves before him, for since it concludes there that "they prayed for him," it implies they knew he had lost his wealth.

One could counter that perhaps they did not know that his hand did not reach [to pay] **at all**, especially according to the version in *Bereishis Rabbah* 4:8, which states, "He said to them, 'Pray for me.'" But from the language of the Poskim, the law is clear that it only applies when one demands payment, and certainly in a case of a sale, and even more so when they are notified in advance that it is in their power not to purchase.

3) In many places in the Shas and the Poskim, it is proven that one of the ways of selling merchandise was by circulating in homes with one's goods (Bava Basra 22a and elsewhere), and no one opened their mouth to object at all. This is certainly the case when it is done via a letter from the seller and not by word of mouth, as it is easier to decline, and **there is no room at all for such misgivings.**

With the blessing of "immediately to Teshuvah, immediately to Geulah,"

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

117

B”H, Monday, 16 Kislev, 5704

To our dear friend, the distinguished avreich, the Chassid, Rabbi M. Z. (may he live and be well),

Shalom u’vracha!

1) All the printing materials you requested have been sent to you, and I am sure you will confirm their receipt.

2) Regarding what is being published (as I estimate) in the near future, they are, in order of appearance: the Kislev sichos, the English calendar, and the 18 Elul sicha, all of which are already at the printer. I hope to be able to send another kuntres of sichos and maamarim from the Rebbe (may his merit shield us) to be printed next week. Following that, the items on the agenda are *Hayom Yom* and the parts of *Sefer HaSichos* that have not yet been printed. The *Kuntres Eitz Chaim*, for several reasons, is not relevant for the near future.

3) We have received more copies of *Chachmei Yisrael B’Shem Tov*. Please let me know if I should send them to you, and how many.

4) Why has the matter of the *Reshimas HaZichronos* stalled?

6) We received from you, in the interim since the last accounting, 150. Of this, a portion is for Machne Israel, and the rest has been distributed according to your instructions.

7) I was alarmed to hear of the coldness and caution—which, according to Rashi’s commentary (on *Avos* 2:2), is understood to be the tactic of the *yetzer hara* (the "known craftsman"), who strives to ensure that if a mitzvah comes a person’s way without any effort on their part, they should at least not "stumble" by participating in or assisting with that mitzvah—of members of your group regarding *shlichus*.

(See the *Likutim* of the Rebbe Rashab of Strashelye, page 13c, where it is explained, according to *Chassidus*, the magnitude of this matter and how much it concerns everyone who wishes to be *mekushar*. In the *nigleh* [the revealed Torah], this is known from the words of our Sages.)

The *shlichus* of our friend, the great Rabbi, etc., during his time in your camp.

It seems that this "craftsman" has already provided several excuses and justifications drawn from the side of holiness—that, on the contrary, etc.—as is explained briefly, with subtlety, and on a higher level in the letters of the Rebbe (may his merit shield us) (transcribed in *Hayom Yom*, page 104). The results in *avodah* are understood from what is explained in *Kuntres U’Maayan*, Maamar 17, Chapter 2.

9) Enclosed is the *Reshimas Divrei* from Simchas Torah. Since this concerns the *po’alim* (workers) more directly, once you return them, Part 1—that is, the *Reshimas Divrei* from Rosh Hashanah, the *Chag* (Sukkos), and Shemini Atzeres—will be sent to you. Surely you will not delay their return. If this *reshimah* has not yet been printed, please note that it is prior to *hagahah* (editing), and therefore, extreme caution is needed in its distribution.

11) Please loan 18 shekalim of the Kehos funds currently in your possession to the Chassid, the Chassid, Rabbi Y. Weinberg, on the day of his wedding, and sign it in my name—this is not related to Machne Israel or the general funds, but is a private matter from me—and I will settle the debt here. The concept of this gift is explained in *Likutei Torah*, end of Parshas Nasso.

May it be the will of Hashem that through the matters of this third month—

(The division of the third month from the summer days: the summer days are *avodah* in the manner of *ohr yashar* (direct light), the *avodah* of the *tzaddikim*, whereas the winter days are in the manner of *ohr chozer* (returning light), *baalei teshuvah*, the *avodah* of the days of *galus*, and especially *ikvesa d’meshicha*—as understood from the *Seder HaMaamarim* of Shemini Atzeres 5729.)

—we will merit, immediately, the revelation on the "third day" (the day of our resurrection), which comes through Mashiach Tzidkeinu. This is achieved through the prerequisite of "your springs shall spread outward" (see the Simchas Torah sicha of 5730, section 32 and onwards), which is the revelation of the light of *Chassidus*. Especially after the imprisonment on the 12th-13th of Tammuz, when he emerged to freedom on the third day—the day that was doubled with "it is good," good for Heaven and good for **creatures** (*Kiddushin* 40a)—which is the precise meaning of "outward."

(To note from *Sefer HaTanya*, Chapter 32, why they are called "creatures," etc.)

This is through the person who is "two lights," a light that is "good," and who acts within himself to double the light, which is the *gematria* of "And you shall love... with all your might" (*b’chol me’odecha*) (see the 20 Kislev sicha of 5733, section 17). The vessel for this is "Love your fellow as yourself."

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

118

B"H, Friday, 20 Kislev, 5704

To the distinguished avreich, the G-d-fearing, etc., the Tamim,
Rabbi Meir, may he live, Greenberg

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your invitation to your wedding, may it be in a good and auspicious hour, I wish to express my blessing: Mazal Tov, Mazal Tov. May you build a home in Israel upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos.

One may suggest the following: The descent of the neshamah into the body is not for its own sake, as it requires no rectification whatsoever; rather, its descent is to rectify the body, the nefesh ha-chiyunis, and one’s portion in the world (as explained in Tanya, Chapter 37). Torah—which comes from the word *hora'ah* (instruction)—is the guide for how to achieve this, specifically through the mitzvos, all of which are intended to elevate the nefesh ha-chiyunis, and so on.

When one has already progressed in his avodah to the point of refining his portion in the world, regarding this our Sages said (Yevamos 63a): "A man brings wheat... he is in need of his 'help-mate'—this is his wife."

This is also the universal order outlined in the Mishnah (Avos, end of Chapter 5): "Five years for Scripture, ten for Mishnah, thirteen for mitzvos, fifteen for Talmud, eighteen for the chuppah." For in this manner, when he reaches the point of "pursuit" (which is the "great preoccupation" mentioned in the Shulchan Aruch of the Alter Rebbe, cited below) regarding the rectification of this world—which occurs when he is twenty—

He has already fulfilled "adorn yourself" (kshot atzmecha), for he is in a state of complete perfection, as is understood from what is written in Likutei Torah in the discourse *Ben Esrim L'Mikor*.

- He will have already completed the study of Talmud, which takes five years, as stated in the Laws of Talmud Torah by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 2, Section 9.

- Regarding what is written there, "two or three years," one may suggest that it refers to different perspectives, depending on the two interpretations of "eighteen": whether it means a full eighteen years (Tosafos, Kesubos 50a) or the beginning of the eighteenth year (Rambam, Laws of Ishus, Chapter 15, Halacha 2; see also Shulchan Aruch Even HaEzer 1:3 and the commentaries there).

As for the fact that even before this, our Sages said "thirteen for mitzvos," one may suggest that this is the beginning of the avodah, which pertains only to his body and his nefesh ha-chiyunis, without connection to his portion in the world, for "little by little I will drive them out."

However, since this is not the primary purpose of the mitzvos, it is not called the "choicest mitzvah" (mitzvah min hamuvchar). With this, we can clarify the precision of the language of the Shulchan Aruch there: "And one who marries early, at thirteen, it is a **mitzvah min hamuvchar**." According to Rashi, this applies even a year before that, for even then he is a *mufla samuch l'ish* (a minor nearing maturity) whose vows are binding by Torah law.

Now, just as in the physical realm, through marriage, the power of procreation is revealed—which is analogous to the power of the Ein Sof (see Likutei Torah, end of the explanation of *Shishim Heimah Melachim*, and elsewhere)—so too in the avodah of man, as mentioned above, its ultimate purpose is the revelation of the Ein Sof. This is achieved through the mitzvos, whose superiority over Torah lies in the fact that Torah is in the category of "strands and hairs" (Likutei Torah, ibid., end of 61 and 62).

The neshamas of Israel and their avodah draw this down even into the Torah, by connecting it to its root. This is especially true for the unique individuals whose attainment was in the Torah as it exists above the tzimtzumim, as explained regarding Rabbi Meir, who would "reveal hidden faces," and as explained in Likutei Torah, beginning of Parshas Tazria.

With blessings for Mazal Tov, for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 119

Tuesday, 24 Kislev, 5704

To the distinguished avreich, G-d-fearing, etc., the Temimim, Rabbi Yosef Weinberg, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Upon your entering into the blessing of marriage with his bride, may she live, I wish to express my blessing that this building be an "everlasting edifice" built upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos.

May it be the will of Hashem that—following the order of level after level—after the descent of the neshamah and its enclothement in the body (where the neshamah and body are like a man and woman in relation to one another, as is stated in Zohar Vol. I, beginning of Parshas Chayei Sarah, and 181b, and elsewhere), their conduct must follow the teaching of our Sages (Yalkut Shimoni, Shoftim, Remez 42): "There is no woman as worthy as the woman who does the will of her husband"—meaning that the body does the will of the neshamah.

And after a period of time, for his avodah in the world, man requires an "ezer k’negdo"—this is the wife, in the literal sense (Yevamos 63a). In this, too, husband and wife merit that the Shechinah dwells between them (Sotah 17a).

Then, through his avodah, he acquires his portion in the world, refining it and illuminating it. This portion is analogous to a woman in relation to the one working within it, who is called "man" and "master"—see Yalkut Shimoni, Parshas Vayishlach, Remez 143, regarding the parable of a man who went to take a wife, etc.

The man who performs the avodah takes the primary portion—in spirituality—and is drawn through the woman also into the literal physical realm, to "bring a blessing to your house," as our Sages taught (Yevamos 62b), and as explained in Likutei Torah, end of Parshas V’zos HaBerachah.

However, even in the man’s own avodah, there must be an analogy and an *is'hapcha* to draw down to the very lowest level. This is the avodah of tzedakah—as the Alter Rebbe elaborates in Iggeres HaKodesh in many places—both tzedakah in its literal sense, and tzedakah in spirituality, where one has compassion on "one who has nothing at all"—in Torah and mitzvos. Consequently, this relates only to Asiyah alone, without understanding or ahavah and yirah (see Iggeres HaKodesh, sections 8-9, and elsewhere). Furthermore, beyond this, through the fact that one has sinned and caused a blemish, etc., one has descended even lower than the world of Asiyah. This [avodah] awakens him to Torah and mitzvos and draws down life to the lowest of the low, to raise him from the "deep pit," as is known from the interpretation of the verse, "When you see the naked, you shall cover him" (Sicha of Purim 5691, based on Tanna D’bei Eliyahu, Chapter 26).

The general point is that through the fact that these two "women" mentioned above are worthy and do the will of their husbands, then this woman too—his portion in the world, which was created only to serve him—does the will of her husband, as it is written: "If you walk in My statutes... I will provide your rains in their time... and you shall dwell securely in your land."

With blessings for a mazal tov, "immediately to teshuvah, immediately to Geulah."

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**

Wednesday, 2 Teves, 5704

To the honorable, the Torah scholar, the G-d-fearing, the distinguished and exalted, etc.,
Rabbi Y. Shapira, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Surely your honor has heard of the activities of "Machne Israel" and the "Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch," which were founded by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita. The main points regarding their objectives can be understood from the enclosed leaflets, and we are sending your honor, in a separate package, samples of the monthly booklets for youth published by the Merkaz.

Based on what we have heard about your honor, you will surely be able, with the help of Hashem, to accomplish much in the work of "Machne Israel" and the "Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch" in your city in general, and among those closest to your influence in particular, and thereby be among those who merit and bring merit to the public.

Particularly worthy of attention is the distribution of educational books that are on the purity of holiness among the widest circles of youth, even those who are, for the time being, far from kosher education.

We would be pleased if you would maintain correspondence with us, and it goes without saying that we are ready to assist you, with the help of Hashem, in your aforementioned work to the extent possible.

These days of Chanukah, when the obligation of the day is *pirsumei nisa* (publicizing the miracle) specifically in the *reshus harabim* (public domain/courtyard) and specifically after sunset by lighting the candles, must certainly awaken in us additional courage for the campaign of our work.

**In the *reshus harabim*** — a place that is open and accessible, a place where everyone has a foothold and expresses their opinion, even if it is the opposite of the opinion of Torah —

**And after sunset** — a time when the nations, and the Hellenists among the Jewish people, ask "Where is your G-d?" of whom it is said, "For Hashem Elokim is a **sun** and shield" —

Until they light the candle of Hashem, the soul of man, which is in every single Jew. And even the sinner, etc., for even though he has sinned, he is a Jew, and we must increase and continue from day to day, for we elevate in matters of holiness and do not lower.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 121

Wednesday, 2 Teves, 5705

To the esteemed and distinguished, G-d-fearing and pious, the Temimim,

Rabbi Shmuel Dov Gancz, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Our friend, the esteemed Chossid, R’ Dober Haskin, may he live and be well, has delivered to us your donation of fifty dollars to "Keren Shalom," the fund dedicated to publishing the seforim of the Rebbe Rashab, may his merit shield us.

On behalf of Kehot Publication Society, and on behalf of all those who merit to study and illuminate their souls with the light of these seforim, we wish to say to you:

May his strength be fortified, and may the merit of the many stand by him forever, that he be blessed with all that is good, and that he continue to participate in the future in matters of publicizing and disseminating the Torah of our holy Rebbes to the widest possible circles of Bnei Yisrael.

The days of Chanukah, whose theme is *pirsumei nissa*—and which surpass Purim in that the light must be placed at the entrance of one’s house, specifically on the outside, and specifically after sunset—clearly require an illumination and drawing down from the highest source, as is explained at length in Chassidus in the *maamarim* of Chanukah.

The parallel to this in a person’s life is the *avodah* during the time of *galus*, which is compared to the night. For then, Elokus is hidden, and the "sun and shield of Hashem Elokim" does not shine openly. Yet, the primary purpose of *galus* is not a matter of punishment, but rather of refining and purifying so that we become worthy of receiving the revelations of Moshiach. As it is written in *Torah Or*, in the *maamar* "Kol Dodi," section 6: "The purpose of the descent and the *galus* is for the sake of a great ascent, that the light of Hashem should shine with great revelation in the days of Moshiach." This is stated in many *maamarim*, and during the time of *galus*, one must prepare the *keilim* (vessels) for these revelations.

This is the meaning of the response to the Baal Shem Tov’s question, "When will the Master come?"—"When your fountains spread outward." The light of the Torah of Chassidus is the *keli* for the revelation of Moshiach, and when the *keli* is completed, the light is revealed.

The condition is that they must spread "outward"—even to those in whom it is not apparent that they are in the *reshus hayachid* (private domain) of the "Unique One of the World" (similar to the *mitzvah* of Chanukah, which is to illuminate specifically on the outside). See the *sicha* of Simchas Torah 5690, and specifically in sections 32-33.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 122

B"H, Wednesday, 2 Teves, 5704

To our dear friend, the distinguished and exalted Chassid, etc.,
Rabbi Chaim Hillel Haivlin, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 11 Mar-Cheshvan:

1) Bearing in mind that we strive to lower the prices of our publications as much as possible, and that we do not charge you for shipping costs, which are currently very high, you will understand that despite our consideration of your reasons and justifications, we are unable to provide a discount greater than twenty percent.

2) We have passed on your request regarding the holy correspondence to the editorial board.

3) We have already sent you a portion of the books you requested, and, G-d willing, we will soon complete the full quantity. Due to technical reasons, we sometimes send packages in installments, but they are all intended for your office—for instance, the shipments we sent in the names of Rabbi Galitzenstein, Orenstein, and Paris; you will surely be able to collect them from them.

4) Because the publication of "Hayom Yom" for this year was delayed, a small booklet was printed containing the daily study lessons, and we have sent you one hundred copies.

5) It is surprising that we have not yet received a response to my letters to the distinguished Rabbi and Chassid, our relative, Rabbi Shneur Zalman A., and our relative, Rabbi Chaim Avraham Naeh, may they live.

I conclude with a matter relevant to these days, the days of Chanukah. The obligation of the day is *pirsumei nisa* (publicizing the miracle). Chanukah even surpasses Purim in that the *pirsumei nisa* must take place specifically at night and specifically in the public domain. As explained in Chassidic discourses on Chanukah, this relates to the time of *galus* (exile), which serves as a preface and preparation for the revelations of Moshiach and the time of *geulah* (redemption).

It is well known that when the Baal Shem Tov asked Moshiach, "When will the Master come?" he replied, "When your wellsprings spread outward (*chutza*)." Specifically *chutza*—as explained at length in the *sicha* of Simchas Torah 5690—which is why there must be a more elevated illumination, and "the fourth [letter], with the addition of a *vav*, will illuminate my darkness" (as discussed in the aforementioned discourses).

Therefore, regarding *avodah* as well, our Sages have said that even one who "dwells in an upper chamber" (I have seen the "people of the upper chamber" and they are few, whose level is explained in Tanya, end of Chapter 9) and has no opening (or connection at all) to the public domain, is nevertheless obligated in this *avodah* and must illuminate the public domain through a window.

- One should note the word **window** (*chalon*), which is higher than illumination through a screen or even through a hole; see *Likutei Torah*, discourse beginning "Lehavin Inyan Yom Tov Sheni Shel Galius."

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*,

**Rabbi Menachem Schneerson**
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 123

[Chanukah, 5704]

We are sending you the book "Yalkut Yomi – Pocket Encyclopedia," which we are certain will interest you greatly, to the point that you will frequently consult it and find much of value within it.

The Yalkut has been printed in a pocket format so that it may be convenient to carry, and it can be readily available to you at any time you may require it.

We have also set aside a special place in it for listing matters and brief, necessary items, as we are confident that the Yalkut will accompany you and be a good friend, not only when you are at home but also when you are traveling on the road.

We would appreciate it if you would inform us of the receipt of the book and the impression it has made upon you—and if you have any comments regarding the Yalkut, we will discuss them with the appropriate attention in relation to the Yalkut for the coming year.

We will take this opportunity to awaken you once again—though it is our hope that even without this, this thought is always before your eyes—that wherever you may be, Hashem, the G-d of Hosts, is with you, watching over you always and observing all your deeds (as explained at length in the message of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita). Therefore, there is no place for fear; be strong in your spirit and in your confidence in victory over the oppressive enemy.

Increase your courage in your connection to your religion and faith, and strive with all your might in the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos to the best of your ability and capacity, for behold, Hashem stands over you.

As it is written (Devarim 23:10-15): "When you go out as a camp against your enemies, then you shall keep yourself from every evil thing... for Hashem your G-d walks in the midst of your camp to deliver you and to give up your enemies before you; therefore shall your camp be holy."

With the wish that you return home soon, whole, after a complete victory, and with the wish for a complete Geulah for all Bnei Yisrael.

## 124

[Winter 5704]

Greetings and blessings!

You surely received in due time all the printed materials we sent you, and we are confident that they are providing great benefit, particularly in strengthening the spirit of Torah and Yiddishkeit among the soldiers, and in bolstering their morale and the strength of their faith in general.

It is self-understood that we stand ready at all times to assist you in all of the above to the best of our ability, and you will surely inform us if an opportunity for this arises.

The holy task has been placed upon you to be a spiritual leader and guide for all the soldiers under your influence: both to encourage their spirit so that they remain strong in their confidence of a complete victory and not be intimidated by the enemy, and to arouse them to be firm in their faith and religion, and to strive with all their strength and possibility to fulfill Torah and mitzvos. For Hashem, the G-d of Hosts, is in their midst, watching over them always and observing all their deeds, and therefore—"your camp shall be holy."

As it is recounted in the Torah of Moshe (Devarim 23:10-15): "When you go out as a camp against your enemies, then you shall keep yourself from every evil thing—for Hashem your G-d walks in the midst of your camp to deliver you and to give your enemies before you; therefore your camp shall be holy."

And further there (20:2-4): "And it shall be, when you draw near to the battle, that the priest shall approach and speak to the people, and shall say to them: 'Hear, O Yisrael, you draw near this day to battle against your enemies; let not your heart faint; fear not, nor be alarmed, neither be you terrified because of them; for Hashem your G-d is He that goes with you, to fight for you against your enemies, to save you.'"

Our hope is strong that you are striving in your avodah to the best of your ability, and then, without a doubt, you will see much fruit from your labor, for the heart of a ben Yisrael is always awake if only there is someone to arouse him regarding his religion and faith, and to remind him of the fulfillment of mitzvos as it is written in the Torah.

With the above, we wish you great success in the fulfillment of this role.

With blessings for a complete victory soon and a complete Geulah for all Bnei Yisrael through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

## 125

125

B"H, Wednesday, 16 Teves, 5714

To the honorable Rabbi and Chossid, man of integrity and lofty character, etc.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter in its time, but I have only now managed to obtain—after searching and inquiring—the book *Birkas Avraham* by R. Avraham Avish, which you mention in your letter. My response has therefore been delayed, and I ask for your forgiveness.

As you requested, I am transcribing here the words of the author’s grandson in the aforementioned book, in answer to the question:

What is different about the mitzvah of *ner Chanukah* that we find in it the levels of *mehadrin* and *mehadrin min hamehadrin*, unlike other mitzvos?

The following is the text regarding this matter (the text in parentheses is my own):

It is appropriate to explain why this mitzvah (of *ner Chanukah*) is distinguished by *mehadrin* and *mehadrin min hamehadrin*, etc. Furthermore, if one has many household members, there is a financial loss in the *mehadrin* practice, as he must light a candle for each individual, whereas the *mehadrin min hamehadrin* practice is that he lights for everyone.

— (According to the view of Tosafos—*Shabbos* 21b—and the Sephardic custom. It is puzzling why he chose the opposite of the simple custom of these lands, given that he was the *Av Beis Din* of Serock. Perhaps he holds that it is merely a custom—similar to what the *Lechem Mishneh* explains (Rambam, *Hilchos Chanukah* 4:3) regarding the Sephardic custom—and not because he holds according to the Rambam’s interpretation of the *sugya* in *Shabbos*. Perhaps he was compelled to say this because in all Ashkenazic places they hold like Tosafos against the Rambam, as testified to in the commentaries on *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim* 671, although the simple reading of the *Rema* there does not imply this.) —

It seems appropriate to explain that the decree was against Shabbos, etc., and certainly there were various levels among the Jewish people. Some were devoted solely to His Name, may He be blessed and exalted... while others were motivated also by honor in this world. Their victory corresponded to the warmth of each person’s heart... Therefore, even in the revelation of the miracle, the power was divided according to the individual’s deeds. The group of the pure, who accumulate mitzvos, light many candles (apparently he refers to the law of *mehadrin min hamehadrin*). In truth, the mitzvah is more *mehudar* when they stand in one row (the meaning here is puzzling). But the group of the *tzaddikim* do not focus on doing many mitzvos because it is difficult... to perform many mitzvos... Yet, one finds in them an inner *yirah*... one who is a *tzaddik*... performs a little in the most appropriate manner (this is apparently the law of one candle for each person). In this way, this mitzvah is divided, and the *mehadrin min hamehadrin* is to beautify the essence of the mitzvah (the meaning is unclear). End quote.

It requires study: 1) According to this, the "group of the pure," who are on a lower level than the "group of the *tzaddikim*," correspond to the *mehadrin min hamehadrin*, while the *tzaddikim* correspond only to the *mehadrin*. How can this be?

2) It is obvious that even at the Exodus from Egypt there were various levels among the Jewish people—as is proven by the fact that at the Red Sea they were divided into four groups, as stated in *Yerushalmi Taanis* 2:5—and likewise at the Giving of the Torah, and elsewhere. If so, what is different about the miracle of Chanukah?

3) One should note more precisely that the answer does not address the question. The question of what is different about the mitzvah of *ner Chanukah* compared to other mitzvos is not about the fact that in *ner Chanukah* there are three ways of performing the mitzvah (a candle for each person and his household, a candle for each individual, and *mosif v'holech*), while in other mitzvos there are only two ways (for example: an *esrog* the size of a *kabeitza*, or an *esrog* larger than that—see *Bava Kamma* 9b).

4) For several reasons, this is not much of a question: a) This is not a difference in the **quality** of the ways of performing the mitzvah, but in **quantity**. b) Even in other mitzvos there are more than two ways. For example, regarding an *esrog*, there is an *esrog* the size of a *kabeitza*, one a third larger, one even larger (see there in *Bava Kamma*). We find something more similar to the mitzvah of *ner Chanukah* in the oil for the *menachos* (*Menachos* 86a), where the "first of the first" has none above it, below it is the "second of the first," etc., and it counts five levels.

And even more similar to *ner Chanukah* is the law of the Four Species, where according to the Ramban, for the *mitzvah min hamuvchar* one needs three complete *hadasim*. If he does not have them, he must at least have three *ketumim* (cut ones), and *bedieved* one fulfills the obligation with one *katum*.

(See the commentaries on Rambam, *Hilchos Lulav* 7:7, that since Shmuel says—*Sukkah* 34b—that we follow Rabbi Tarfon, and he does not mention Rabbi Tarfon and Rabbi Akiva together, it implies that there is also a *hiddur* in having three *ketumim* compared to one *katum*.) And one should also note the **eight** levels of *tzedakah* (Rambam, *Hilchos Matnos Aniyim* 10), and more.

The question regarding the difference of *ner Chanukah* from other mitzvos concerns the difference in quality:

In all other mitzvos, we find only "mitzvah" and "hiddur mitzvah." As in the aforementioned *esrog*, whether it is a third larger or more, it falls into the **single** category of *hiddur mitzvah*. Similarly, regarding the oil for the *menachos*, it must be the most select available, as it is written, "All the fat is for Hashem" (Rambam, end of *Hilchos Issurei Mizbe'ach*), where all levels are included in this.

This is not the case in *ner Chanukah*, where we find a new category of *mehadrin min hamehadrin* in addition to the category of *hiddur*.

— For example: If the language of *Chazal* regarding *ner Chanukah* had been: "The *mehadrin* light a candle for each person; above this, *Beis Shammai* says *pochas v'holech*," then there would be no room for the question—even though everything written in the book *Birkas Avraham* stands on its own merit, explaining why some light only one candle and others add.

***

Regarding what appears to me in answer to the question of why it is specifically in the miracle of Chanukah that we find *mehadrin min hamehadrin*: This is preceded by an explanation—in brief, as this is not the place to elaborate—on the concept of *hiddur mitzvah* and the concept of miracles in general. Then it will **automatically** be understood why it is specifically in the miracle of Chanukah that *Chazal* said there is not only *mehadrin* but also *mehadrin min hamehadrin*.

*Chazal* said (*Berachos* 13a): "Why does the *Shema* precede the passage of *Vehayah im shamoa*? So that one may first accept upon himself the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven, and afterwards accept upon himself the yoke of the *mitzvos*." The reward for this is as it is written, "And it shall be if you diligently obey My commandments... I will give your rains in their season..."—a natural order in its fullness—for the good.

Now, as is apparently evident even to the senses, one who acts solely out of acceptance of the yoke and fear of the Master will do only what he is obligated to do, since, left to his own devices, he prefers to be unrestrained.

In addition to him is one who has refined himself and subdued his *yetzer hara*—in the language of the Rambam (ibid.)—who will not only perform the mitzvah but will also beautify it and be meticulous with himself even in matters that are not a strict obligation.

Corresponding to this in the reward for *mitzvos*—

For all the attributes of the Holy One, Blessed be He, are "measure for measure" (*Sanhedrin* 90a)—

He is given not only "your rains in their season," which comes from the natural order—good, but still natural—that is, **obligated** by the conduct of nature,

But rather, the conduct toward him is also "beyond the letter of the law." Even if, according to the law and the **obligation** of nature, he should fall into distress, he is saved from it through a miracle that is above nature.

This is what *Chazal* said (*Berachos* 20b): "He said to them (the Holy One, Blessed be He), 'Shall I not show favoritism to Israel, for whom I wrote in the Torah, etc., and they are meticulous with themselves, etc.'"

— And that which is stated there (20a) that "the early ones experienced miracles because they sacrificed their lives for the sanctification of the Name"—

Beyond the fact that this does not necessarily mean *mesiras nefesh* to the point of death, but rather that one does not care about his honor or money even if he is **not obligated** to do so, as it concludes with the story of R. Elazar bar Avina—there it refers to the fact that his prayer for a miraculous outcome for the **entire community** would be accepted.

Now, the miracle of the Exodus from Egypt, of Purim, of the Clouds of Glory, etc., came primarily to save the Jewish people from a distress that was about to befall them—or that had already befallen them.

Therefore, even in the *mitzvos* associated with these miracles, there is "mitzvah" and "hiddur mitzvah."

And likewise, in the entirety of all *mitzvos*—their foundation and root is "I am Hashem your G-d who brought you out of the land of Egypt," regarding which *Chazal* said (as brought in Rashi there) that the Exodus is sufficient reason for you to be My servants—therefore they said, "Beautify yourselves before Him in *mitzvos*."

In addition to all the above, in the miracle of Chanukah, besides the fact that there was also a matter similar to the above—that is, the victory and the miracle of the war, where You delivered the strong into the hands of the weak, etc.—

There is also the miracle of the oil, which did not come to save from distress, but rather—as a sign of even greater affection—a **miracle so that the Jewish people could perform a mitzvah**. Therefore, there was added to the performance of its mitzvah a greater affection: *mehadrin min hamehadrin*.

With this, that which is in Chanukah itself is also sweetened: the matter of *mehadrin min hamehadrin* applies to the lighting of the candles, which relates to the miracle of the oil, and not to the obligation of *hoda'ah* (thanksgiving) and *hallel* (praise), for one leads to the other.

And why such a miracle occurred specifically on Chanukah—

It is understood according to what is explained (see *Levush* and *Taz*, *Orach Chaim* 670) that the Greeks did not seek to kill, and the Jews lived on their land and the *Beis Hamikdash* was built, and the decree of the Greek kingdom was only to "make them forget Your Torah and turn them away, etc.," and as *Chazal* said (*Bereishis Rabbah* 2), "Write... that you have no portion in the G-d of Israel."

— And the war was only a result of this. With this, one can also reconcile the language of the Rambam at the beginning of *Hilchos Chanukah*: "And they stretched out their hands against their money, etc."—so that it does not contradict what is written in the *Levush*, etc.—

And therefore, it was specifically then that such a miracle occurred, in which the soul alone finds delight.

***

The above is the resolution of the question according to the *peshat*. For the sake of completeness, I will also transcribe what I found on this matter in *Chassidus*:

1) In the book *Kedushas Levi* (Likutim, end of *Kedusha* 4): "The *taanug* of every thing is called 'the subtle of the subtle.' Therefore, the incense of Yom Kippur was 'the subtle of the subtle,' for Yom Kippur corresponds to the world of *taanug*, etc. The spirituality of every thing is 'subtle,' and the *taanug* of the spirituality is 'the subtle of the subtle.' Therefore, since the dispute between *Beis Shammai* and *Beis Hillel* regarding whether one increases and continues or decreases and continues is a dispute as to which **taanug** is greater—the *taanug* of the body (performance) of the *mitzvos* (for this *taanug* increases from day to day) or the *taanug* that it was revealed to them that they could perform the mitzvah (which decreases from day to day), etc.—therefore it is *mehadrin min hamehadrin*, like 'the subtle of the subtle,' and it corresponds to the world of *taanug*." End quote.

— It requires study: If so, then on Yom Kippur there should also be a matter of *mehadrin min hamehadrin*.

2) In the *Siddur* with the commentary of the *Maharid* of Liadi (grandson of the *Tzemach Tzedek*), Vol. 2, *Shaar HaChanukah* (177b), it states: "The *mehadrin*—see the *maamar* 'Shachorah Ani' regarding the explanation of 'and you shall beautify,' etc., also the eighth king beautifies the *tikkun*, etc. And *mehadrin min hamehadrin* is according to the concept of *Akudim*, which is above *Tohu* and *Tikkun*." End quote.

The connection of this specifically to Chanukah can be explained according to what is explained in *Chassidus* in the *maamarim* of Chanukah (*Torah Or* and *Shaarei Orah*, *maamar* "Ki Atah Neri," and others), that at that time the Greeks entered the Sanctuary and defiled all the oils of the level of *Chochma* of *Kedusha*, and a miracle was performed through an illumination from above, above the *Seder Hishtalshelus*—see the explanation of the matter there.

Seemingly, the two aforementioned interpretations are one and the same—except that the *Maharid* speaks of the root of the illumination of Chanukah and the names of the worlds from the perspective of their inclusion, while the *Kedushas Levi* speaks of their names borrowed from the powers of the soul and the illumination of Chanukah after it was drawn down from its root.

For the *Admur HaEmtza'i* explains in *Shaarei Orah* (ibid., sec. 17) that the cruse of oil they found is in the level of the concealment of the essence of *taanug* before it came to revelation in *Chochma*, etc., where all the arousal of the *midos* in *ratzon* and *taanug*, etc., are included as one (for example, the essential *taanug* and the *hylic*, etc.)—and it is explained in many places regarding the concept of *Akudim* (*Torah Or*, end of *Parshas Noach*, and in more detail in *Torah Ohr* there, and elsewhere) that it is, for example, in the powers of the soul as they are still included in the soul without any division.

This still requires study.

With blessings for immediate *teshuvah* and immediate *geulah*.

#### ***125***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 5, p. 4, and completed based on a transcript.

## 126

B”H, 24 Teves, 5704

In response to your letter of 20 Teves.

1) Regarding your observation from Bava Kamma (9b) that one could say the *hiddur mitzvah* of up to a third is analogous to *mehadrin*, while more than a third is analogous to *mehadrin min hamehadrin*, and therefore a special reward is established for it, which is "from the Ribono shel Olam's treasury"—

In my humble opinion, this is not the case, as I also wrote in my previous letter. Since the Gemara does not once distinguish within the concept of *hiddur* itself between *hiddur* and *hiddur min hamehadrin*—as it does regarding *Ner Chanukah*—we have no basis or necessity to divide it into categories. Especially since both the third and the amount beyond a third share the same obligation (the verse, "This is my G-d and I will beautify Him"). Just as it is not said regarding the oil for the *menachos* that it must be beautiful and choice, with categories of *mehadrin* and *mehadrin min hamehadrin*, etc., up to five levels corresponding to the five qualities of oil (Menachos 86b)—and the same applies to the other *mitzvos* I noted in my previous letter. And just as it is said in Menachos that because of the obligation to bring from the choicest, one is immediately obligated to use the best oil available if it is in his possession, so too in the case of Bava Kamma: if one wishes to fulfill the command of "beautifying Him" in a *mitzvah*, he is immediately obligated—according to the Sages of the West in the name of Rabbi Zeira—to use the most beautiful [item] he finds, even if it costs more than a third. (This is unlike *Ner Chanukah*, where if one wishes to beautify, one cannot be obligated to specifically perform *mehadrin min hamehadrin*, as that is a different category of *mitzvah* performance.)

For the plain meaning of the language in Bava Kamma implies that the Sages of the West in the name of Rabbi Zeira distinguish between a third and more than a third regarding whether he is repaid in this world or not, but not regarding the obligation itself. This is also the implication of the language of the Rashba, cited in *Shitah Mekubetzes*.

It requires further study, as the commentary of Rabbeinu Chananel implies somewhat that he distinguishes regarding the obligation as well.

However, the fact that Rabbeinu Chananel in Bava Kamma cites the *braisa* regarding *Ner Chanukah* does not necessitate the conclusion that his opinion in Bava Kamma also involves the concept of *mehadrin min hamehadrin* (just as it is impossible to say so according to the second explanation in Rabbeinu Chananel, which interprets "from the Ribono shel Olam's treasury" as meaning if the Ribono shel Olam has expanded his wealth).

Rather, his intent is to bring support from another place in the Gemara regarding the matter of *hiddur mitzvah*.

For the time being, I do not know of another place in the Babylonian Talmud where the term *hiddur mitzvah* is brought, other than the aforementioned (even though according to Rashi, it is one and the same with "beautifying Him" from Shabbos 133b).

2) Regarding your doubt whether in *gemillus chasadim* one eats the "fruits" in this world, etc., or only in the case of *hiddur*—see Kiddushin (40a), which proves the former view.

3) Regarding your suggestion that the "eating of fruits in this world" is exactly the same as "from the Ribono shel Olam's treasury" (and apparently you were compelled toward this interpretation by the Tosafos, *dih* "mishal," in Bava Kamma, ibid.)—

Seemingly, one must say this is not so, and each has its own unique aspect:

a) The "eating of fruits in this world" is not necessarily in the very same object. For example: if one suffered a financial loss due to the honor of his parents, we do not find a promise that the Ribono shel Olam will fill this specific loss, for the "eating of fruits" of honoring parents is simply "so that it may be well with you."

—And the incident of Dama ben Nesina (Kiddushin 31a), where in the following year he received the money he had lost, is not proof that this is always the case, since the verse "so that it may be well with you" is written as a general statement—

This is unlike *hiddur mitzvah*, where "from the Ribono shel Olam's treasury" means that they reimburse him for the money he spent (similar to the expenses for *Yom Tov* and the Torah study of one's children, Beitzah 16a), as is the plain meaning of the language in the Gemara.

b) Furthermore, "from the Ribono shel Olam's treasury" implies nothing more than repayment in this world for what was spent—a filling of a deficit.

This is unlike the "eating of fruits" from the *Mishnah* in Peah, regarding which it is written in the context of *gemillus chasadim*—"he shall find life, righteousness, and honor," and similarly for other *mitzvos*—which refers to abundant fruits, disproportionate to the expenditure.

And if we say that in the aforementioned [case] the interpretation of "eating of fruits" and "from the Ribono shel Olam's treasury" is forced, then we must stretch the intent of the Tosafos (Bava Kamma 9b) to mean that it does not mean he is literally eating from the Ribono shel Olam's treasury in the exact sense of the *Mishnah* in Peah.

Rather, it comes to say that the reimbursement of what he spent is merely the "fruits," but the "principal" remains for him in the World to Come; or, it comes to exclude the second interpretation brought in Rabbeinu Chananel, that "from the Ribono shel Olam's treasury" means if he is wealthy, and it does not refer to the reward for the *mitzvah*. And the Tosafos use the language of the *Mishnah* in the same way we find the *Mishnah* using the language of the verse (Peah, Chapter 2, Mishnah 2), as is cited in the book *Klalei HaShas*.

It is worth noting that through this interpretation of the words of the Tosafos, two difficulties are resolved:

a) In Kiddushin (40a) it is stated that there are "fruits" only for *mitzvos* that are good for people, whereas in the *hiddur mitzvah* of an *esrog* and the like, it is only good for Heaven.

b) "These are the things for which a person eats the fruits in this world," and not for other things, as is stated in Shabbos (127a) and Kiddushin (ibid.), and *hiddur mitzvah*—not more than a third—is not included.

## 127

B"H, Tuesday, 29 Teves, 5704

To the dear and distinguished avreichim...

Shalom u’vracha,

In response to your letter of 18 Teves:

1) Regarding the Talmud Torah: It is advisable to urge the teacher to visit the Melach, as he has not yet been here. Please also provide us with the address of the Talmud Torah and the teacher.

2) You can find maamarim and short ideas on the topics you desire in the *Hayom Yom* compilation, in the sicha of Chof-Hei Teves 5703, and so on.

3) Regarding Mincha on Erev Shabbos: It is correct—according to the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, shlita—to daven Mincha in a tzibbur as Mincha Gedolah, rather than Mincha Ketanah in yechidus.

4) Regarding what you noted about saying Pesukei D’zimra: It is a clear halacha (*Berachos* 32a) that "a person should always arrange the praise of the Omnipresent and only then daven." From where do we derive this? From Moshe, etc. Therefore, they instituted saying Pesukei D’zimra before davening, and also in order to stand in davening with the simcha of a mitzvah. This enactment is cited in all the seforim of the Geonim, the commentators on the Shas, and the poskim. Consequently, one who treats the recitation of Pesukei D’zimra lightly is treating lightly an enactment that has been accepted by the Geonim, the pillars of Torah and instruction of every generation—men upon whom the entire House of Israel relies. Among them: Rav Amram Gaon, Rav Saadia Gaon, Rav Natronai Gaon, Rav Moshe Gaon, the Rif, Rabbeinu Yonah, Rashi, Rambam, Rashba, Ramban, Semag, Semak, Tur, Beis Yosef, Rema, Bach, Levush, Taz, Magen Avraham, and many, many others.

The fact that b’dieved they permitted skipping parts of Pesukei D’zimra for the sake of davening with a tzibbur (and specifically according to the methods explained in the Shulchan Aruch) is entirely irrelevant to your question. The reason for this is explicitly stated: Pesukei D’zimra was instituted for the sake of davening, so that it should be desirable and accepted, and through davening with a tzibbur, one’s davening is certainly accepted (and one could add a supporting point: the tzibbur, in their davening, has already preceded and recited Pesukei D’zimra, and he includes himself with them). Since this is a case of b’dieved, where it is impossible for him to fulfill both (and the same applies if he cannot even say *Baruch She’amar* and *Yishtabach*), he skips and davens with the tzibbur.

—And the Acharonim have already ruled that after davening, he should recite everything he skipped, except for the berachos, namely *Baruch She’amar* and *Yishtabach*—

However, l’chatchilah, every person is obligated to urge himself so that he will not need to skip anything; this is simple.

One who acts with defiance against the above, and treats the enactment of the Chachomim and the custom of all Israel lightly—his status is explicitly defined in the Mishnah, Gemara, etc., and there is no need to elaborate.

With blessings for immediate teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

Rabbi Menachem Schneerson
Chairman of the Executive Committee

## 128

128

*[Teves 5704]*

From the time it became widely known that the eighteenth day of the month of Elul is the birthday of the Baal Shem Tov and of the Alter Rebbe, it has become the custom in many places—and especially in Chabad shuls—to hold a farbrengen on that day. This gathering is dedicated to sharing stories of tzadikim, strengthening the ways of Chassidim in general and Ahavas Yisrael in particular, and accepting resolutions to set fixed times for the study of Torah—both the revealed and the hidden.

This birthday is celebrated with special inspiration in the home of the Rav, where the Admur shares words of inspiration regarding Torah and avodah, and at times, a maamar Chassidus as well...

#### ***128***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 21, p. 518; it is from the introduction of the Rebbe Shlita to the Kuntres of Chai Elul 5703.

129

B"H, 9 Shevat, 5704

To the honorable, the great Rabbi and Chossid, distinguished and exalted, G-d-fearing and wise, etc., etc., Rabbi A. Krasik, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 10 Kislev:

1) It is a pity that it was not known in time that printing materials should not be distributed for free. However, our hope now is that you will endeavor to have everything arranged, G-d willing, according to our instructions, and also to rectify the past as much as possible, for only a lack of funds is delaying the printing of several items.

2) The Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch (MLC) is striving to ensure that in all countries and in all schools where the Holy Tongue is taught, it should be taught with holiness. To this end, we are publishing textbooks and reading materials suitable for this purpose. However, this does not constitute an instruction regarding any attitude of the MLC—positive or negative—toward the aforementioned schools.

3) We are happy to hear valid comments that are worth considering for future publications. In any case, we are interested in knowing all the criticism, and we would be grateful if you would inform us of what you have heard in this regard, and from what type of people the criticism comes: from those whose intentions are desirable, or from those who seek pretexts against Chabad and Chassidim, and the like.

4) Since it is very important that the committee for the distribution of printed materials—both in Chassidus and in matters of Chinuch and Machne Israel—be established as soon as possible and begin its work, and since we do not know who is suitable for this in a way that the work will be conducted with vigor while simultaneously not interfering with other matters in which they are currently engaged, we are enclosing a general letter. Surely you will all gather and choose those most suitable for this, and after you inform us who they are, we will be able, G-d willing, to correspond directly with them.

5) If for any reason the establishment of the aforementioned committee is delayed, please be kind enough to inform us how many copies of each type of printed material to send them for the time being.

6) The following have now finished printing: *Kuntres Sichos* and *Maamarim* Chicago 5702, as mentioned above, 18 Elul 5703, our *Sefer* Vol. 2, our *Sefer* Vol. 4. Permission is granted to print: *Tzemach Tzedek* on *Mishnayos* (a photographic reproduction of the first printing), *Hayom Yom* 5704. We are preparing for print a book of letters from the Rebbe, may he live and be well.

7) Please inform us if the *Tanya* that was printed is a photographic reproduction or if it was typeset anew, how many copies were printed, and if you have any matrices or the like on hand.

Awaiting your response to the above, and with blessings for immediate Teshuvah and immediate Geulah,

M. Schneerson
Chairman of the Executive Committee

Many thanks if you would deliver the enclosed letter to Rabbi Ch. Y. Rosenblum, may he live.

B"H, 9 Shevat, 5704

To the honorable, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., Moreinu Harav Ch. Y. (may he live and be well),

Peace and blessing!

From time to time, I hear news of you and your family (may they live and be well) through my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (shlita), but it seems you write infrequently. The main thing, however, is that goodness and kindness should follow you in all matters.

About a year ago, I sent one hundred and fifty shekel in your name (which was included in the five hundred sent by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, as was explained at the time in the telegram), and you were requested via telegram to send packages to my parents (may they live and be well). I wrote to you again after that regarding this, asking if any word had arrived from them as to whether they received the packages, and in general, how they are doing. However, I have not yet been honored with a response from you, even though it appears from your letter to my mother-in-law, the Rabbanit (tichyeh), that you did send packages. I repeat my request, doubly and triply, to inform me—even if only briefly—regarding the packages, and most importantly, if there is any news as to how they are doing.

I look forward, in any case, to a prompt response from you.

Signing with much gratitude in advance, and with the blessing of "Immediately to Teshuvah, immediately to Geulah."

Best regards to your family (may they live and be well).
